# Naudokis.lt — Full-Site Design Audit vs 2026 Marketplace Standards

*2026-07-06 · 30 finder agents in 3 rounds over a fresh 641-PNG corpus (8 breakpoints × LT+EN, all surfaces + 74 interaction/state shots), every finding adversarially verified against the live server. Audited state: working tree at commit a6dc1c2 (2026-07-01 "Remove mock data layer") plus 21 uncommitted modified files (the prior audit's fix pass), production build (`next build && next start`), live dev API (api-dev.naudokis.lt), captured 2026-07-05 evening.*

## Executive summary

The site is in genuinely strong shape for a pre-launch bridge product: the token-driven visual system holds together across nine surfaces and both locales, the honesty architecture (truthful counts, em-dash zero-states, real deposits, "shown in the app" instead of fake €0 fees) is above what Airbnb-tier marketplaces typically ship, and the independent oracles found **zero horizontal overflow at 21 widths × 9 surfaces** — the 205 verified-good notes in the appendix are there precisely so none of this gets re-litigated. Against that base, this audit confirmed **199 new findings: 2 blocking · 16 high · 78 medium · 103 polish**, plus 1 plausible-unproven, 26 re-confirmed known-open items (2 of them high), and 14 findings killed by adversarial verification. The two blockers are both on the mobile listing detail — the gallery paints over the booking card's price row (F-058) and the "Galutinė suma" value clips at the viewport edge (F-059) — i.e. the single most trust-sensitive block on the core conversion path. The real risk concentration is conversion mechanics rather than visual quality: the desktop app-redirect modal's dominant CTA is a decoy that loops back to the homepage (F-123), the similar-items rail silently never renders with live data (R2-022), price and reserve sit below the fold at common desktop sizes (F-068), and the owner side of the marketplace is one muted text line on the homepage (F-139). A second cluster is code-level accessibility (invisible FAQ focus, focus loss in every custom listbox, invisible-but-tabbable drawer controls) and canonical-locale grammar in generated strings ("Vilnius mieste", nominative titles in SEO templates). Both dev and prod hold ~3 active listings with 0 reviews — the sparse marketplace is the real launch-day state, and several findings are about how the design handles exactly that. Discovery converged cleanly across rounds — 179 findings in round 1, 34 in round 2, 12 (mostly polish) in round 3 — so this is close to the full defect surface, not a sample. More findings than the June audit's 74 is a function of a deeper method (three rounds, adversarial verification, code-level a11y/i18n review), not a regression.

## Verdict: 2026 marketplace design-readiness

**8.0 / 10** as audited. The June 2026-06-26 audit scored 7.5; its fix passes earned the estimated 8.5+ on the surfaces they touched, and that improvement is real — chrome consistency, legal typography, empty/error states and trust presentation now sit at or above the Airbnb/Turo/Booking bar in the re-verified evidence. But this deeper pass found two blocking regressions on the mobile listing detail, a dead benchmark feature (the similar-items rail), and a decoy primary CTA at the funnel's last step — defects the 8.5 estimate did not price in. Versus named benchmarks: header/footer/legal/state-handling are at Booking/Stripe class; discovery and detail conversion mechanics are a tier below Airbnb/Turo/Fat Llama (no price filter, no search suggestions, no cross-sell, price below fold); owner-side conversion is well below the Turo "Become a host" norm.

| Dimension | Score | Justification |
|---|---|---|
| Visual craft | 8.5 | Token discipline + full-res micro-craft verified (concentric radii, baseline-aligned prices); seams in overlay chrome (three close-button styles, F-113) and mixed section-header grammars (F-006) |
| Responsive | 8.0 | Zero horizontal overflow at 21 widths (oracle-verified), but both blockers are responsive layout failures (F-058/F-059) and 1280 gets the worst HIW layout (F-075) |
| Trust signals | 8.5 | Honest zero-review/deposit/Stripe stack above the 2026 bar; undefined "Griežta" policy tier (F-066), fee opacity (F-138), dead legal references (F-084) |
| Conversion — renter | 7.0 | Price/CTA below desktop fold (F-068), decoy desktop modal CTA (F-123), similar rail never fires (R2-022), no price filter (R2-025), sparse-grid holes (F-017) |
| Conversion — owner | 6.0 | The HIW owner tab is genuinely Turo-class (verified good), but home, nav and the default modal barely acknowledge the supply side (F-139, F-141, F-142) |
| Accessibility | 7.0 | Strong foundations (skip links, focus rings, 44px system, modal a11y at the bar) undermined by hard fails: F-156, F-157, F-158, F-159 |
| i18n & copy | 7.5 | Full LT/EN parity, compile-time dictionary contract; broken LT grammar in generated strings (F-070, F-174, F-176), EN calques (R2-035), unlabelled LT UGC on /en (R2-033) |
| States & robustness | 8.0 | Designed offline/error/empty set most marketing sites lack; stale-offline window (F-099), error-state count contradiction (F-100), 400-UUID retry dead-end (F-108) |

**Bottom line.** What stands between this and "ship it proudly" is not a redesign — it is the 20-item fix-before-launch list below (18 new blocking/high + 2 known-open highs), of which roughly half are sub-day fixes, plus three decisions that need an owner: how the design presents a 3-listing marketplace (a strategy, not patches), whether the owner funnel gets a real track before launch, and the external unblockers (assetlinks fingerprints, photography, pending copy sign-offs). Land those and the honest answer against the 2026 cohort is 8.5–9: a small marketplace that looks and behaves like a disciplined large one.

## Top priority fixes

Blocking first, then highs ordered by conversion impact. These are the fix-before-launch list.

1. **F-058 · BLOCKING** — Listing detail ≤560px: gallery paints over the booking-facts card, hiding the price row and clipping the CTA — fix the `.nk-bento` grid-template-rows to `auto` so row 1 sizes to the hero tile.
2. **F-059 · BLOCKING** — Listing detail 390px: "Galutinė suma — Apskaičiuojama programėlėje" clips at the viewport edge with no ellipsis — drop `nowrap` on the value span, let it wrap right-aligned.
3. **F-123 · HIGH** — Desktop app-redirect modal: the dominant purple "Atsisiųsti programėlę" button 302s back to the homepage on desktop — hide the /go button >560px and promote the QR to hero.
4. **F-068 · HIGH** — Listing detail 1280/1440: the hero photo consumes the viewport; price is cut in half at the fold — make gallery height viewport-aware (`min(46vw, calc(100dvh - 470px))`).
5. **F-065 · HIGH** — Booking card 1440: fee/total rows wrap raggedly and the total row overflows the card border — un-nowrap long i18n values, baseline-align rows, shorten LT values.
6. **R2-022 · HIGH** — Similar-items rail queries by localized display name and always gets 0 results, so the detail page is a dead end — query by `category_id`, allow a single sibling under an honest heading.
7. **F-139 · HIGH** — Homepage has no owner/host section; the entire supply pitch is one muted hero line — add a server-rendered owner band deep-linking to /kaip-tai-veikia?role=owner.
8. **F-099 · HIGH** — Offline feed asserts stale cached results under the new query's heading ("3 pasiūlymai" for a 0-match query) — add an offline strip and dim/blank the count while placeholder data backs a changed query.
9. **F-025 · HIGH** — pSEO category landing H1s render "…nuoma | Naudokis" with a dangling pipe — strip the brand suffix in `toCategory()` so H1 and JSON-LD are clean.
10. **F-075 · HIGH** — How-It-Works at exactly 1280px serves the blown-up single-column layout with ~60% dead space — lower the collapse breakpoint to ~1120px and constrain the active card.
11. **F-110 · HIGH** — Locale listbox inside the mobile drawer clips off-screen at x=0 and occludes the install CTA — left-align the panel from the drawer or expand in-flow.
12. **F-084 · HIGH** — Terms incorporate ~8 sub-policy documents (payments, deposits, cancellations) that are published nowhere on the site — publish them, or reword every "Read the X Rules" reference to say where they live.
13. **F-070 · HIGH** — "dėl pristatymo Vilnius mieste" — broken LT case agreement on the listing handover line — use the existing `cityLocativeLt()`.
14. **F-178 · HIGH** — Listing meta descriptions hard-cut at 200 chars mid-word — reuse the legal `truncate()` (word boundary + ellipsis) and strip tags.
15. **F-156 · HIGH** — Hero search placeholder falls back to UA default at ~2.2:1 contrast, the field's only visible hint on desktop — one line: `::placeholder{color:var(--nk-text-slate)}`.
16. **F-157 · HIGH** — Keyboard focus is invisible on every FAQ row (outline clipped by `overflow:hidden`) — mirror the card `:focus-within` box-shadow pattern.
17. **F-158 · HIGH** — Closed mobile nav drawer keeps 6 invisible controls in the Tab order — `inert={!menuOpen}` (or visibility-hidden with transition).
18. **F-159 · HIGH** — All three custom listboxes (filters, locale, hero city) drop focus to `<body>` on Escape/select — restore focus to the trigger via a shared close helper.

Also still open from previous audits, same tier: **F-013** (hero phone mockup asset: "0,0★" ratings, LT-only UI on /en, sloppy status bar — the largest visual on the most-viewed surface) and **F-060** (the "Daikto perdavimas" left panel renders as a completely empty bordered rectangle at 1440). Both are on the launch list.

## Quick wins

Dictionary-only, one-line CSS, or single-attribute changes with outsized polish return:

- **F-027** — Search chip renders English curly quotes on LT ("Sony" vs „Sony“); add a `chipQuery` dict function.
- **F-100** — Error state asserts "0 pasiūlymų" next to "couldn't load"; one-line `!isError` gate on the count.
- **F-111** — Desktop filter popovers run past the viewport with options clipped; add `maxHeight + overflowY:auto` to the panel.
- **F-116** — City popover right-anchors while category left-anchors; delete one `align="right"`.
- **F-063** — Lightbox shows "1 / 1" on single-photo listings; gate the counter on the existing `many` flag.
- **F-090** — LT legal titles wrap needlessly at desktop; raise `.nk-lg-title` cap 18ch → 26ch.
- **F-098** — Legal H2s break with single-word widows; `text-wrap:balance` on the heading span.
- **F-018** — Home hero H1 wraps as an uneven 4-line rag; add `text-wrap:balance` to `.nk-h-hero`.
- **R3-008** — HIW hero strands the preposition "iš" at line end; bind with a non-breaking space in lt.ts.
- **R3-002** — EN CTA banner wraps "Book it in / the app."; non-breaking spaces in en.ts.
- **R3-004** — LT step-2 mock shows "Rezervuota" above a "Rezervuoti" button (state contradicts action); one dict word.
- **F-078** — "Mokėjimai per Stripe" trust card uses a Snowflake icon; swap to CreditCard.
- **F-004** — "Aiškios taisyklės ir pagalba" card uses a MapPin; swap to ScrollText/LifeBuoy.
- **R2-008** — Delivery filter uses a Car icon while the delivery badge uses Truck; standardise on Truck (4 edits).
- **R2-019** — Offer-card map pin is flood-filled into a blob; remove one `fill` prop.
- **F-165** — Legal drawer close announces "Contents", categories clear announces "Close"; wire the existing correct keys.
- **F-160** — Feed/categories search inputs have no accessible name; add `type="search"` + `aria-label` from existing dict keys.
- **F-166** — Breadcrumb "Home" on /en pages navigates to the LT homepage; locale-prefix the home crumb.
- **F-153** — EN says "New" on cards but "New item" on the gallery; unify one dict value.
- **R3-001** — EN footer heads the category column "Browse" (already the section eyebrow); change to "Categories".
- **F-177** — EN listing meta reads "Rent DJI Mavic 3 photo & video in Vilnius" (word salad); restore the LT parenthesis treatment.
- **F-186** — EN home `<title>` is 65 chars and truncates in SERPs; shorten to ≤60.
- **F-179 / F-181** — One straight apostrophe and four missing terminal periods in otherwise carefully typeset dictionaries.
- **R2-015** — Categories skeleton renders 8 tiles for an always-12 result; change one constant.
- **F-134** — Middle feature-card title floats off-baseline; `alignItems:'flex-start'` on the title slot.
- **F-045** — Footer "Visos kategorijos" link was designed (dict key exists, unused) but never wired; append one Link.
- **F-154** — Hero store badges are ~36–40px tap targets on mobile; `min-height:var(--nk-tap)` on the anchors.

## Larger design improvements

Thematic programs, not single patches:

1. **Sparse-inventory presentation strategy** (F-017, R2-012, F-026, F-041, F-057, F-054, F-051, F-050, R2-016; plus R2-022's single-sibling gate). Three listings is the real launch state, and today it produces empty fourth columns, dead grid space, intros that promise inventory above empty states, and recovery paths that vary arbitrarily by landing type. This needs one policy — ghost "browse all" tiles, owner-CTA fills, capability-framed (not inventory-asserting) copy, reason-aware empty states — applied consistently across home, feed, landings and detail, because each surface currently improvises.
2. **Owner-side conversion track** (F-139, F-142, F-141, R2-030, known-open F-077). The site has one excellent owner asset (the role-aware HIW tab, verified at the Turo bar) and almost no routes into it: no homepage band, a dead-end earn card, renter-only default modal copy, renter-slanted FAQ on the owner tab. The program: a `?role=owner` deep link, an owner band on home, owner-variant modal copy on owner surfaces, owner FAQ items — plus marketing sign-off on the new copy.
3. **App-handoff funnel hierarchy** (F-123, F-130, F-124, R2-031, F-127, R2-023, F-125/R3-011, F-007, F-023/R3-010). The single conversion gate currently stacks up to four parallel install actions with the wrong one dominant per device class. Decide one hierarchy — desktop: QR hero + "email me the link" fallback + smart app banner meta; mobile: single smart /go CTA + sticky header install button — and carry listing context across the install (deferred deep link). This is one surface but touches modal, chrome, metadata and analytics, and interacts with the tracked app deep-link work.
4. **Review/social-proof readiness** (F-176, F-168, F-067, R2-026, known-open F-071; with-reviews layout is an explicit coverage skip). Zero reviews exist anywhere, so the with-reviews layout has never rendered with real data — and the first review will hit a broken LT pluralization, a reviews section marooned in the narrow column, and an aria pattern many screen readers ignore. Fix these now, stage host-tenure signals and the owner mini-rail, and smoke-test the layout with a seeded review before launch.
5. **EN content strategy for LT UGC** (R2-033, R2-032, F-055, R2-035, R2-034, known-open F-013). Effectively all owner descriptions will be Lithuanian forever; /en currently renders them unlabelled, mixes "25 metai" into English spec rows, and its own chrome copy drifts (three nouns for one concept, calqued headlines). Near term: an "original language" disclosure, a unit-localization stopgap, and one en.ts terminology pass. Long term: labelled backend translation (Airbnb pattern) — a cross-team decision, not a frontend patch.
6. **A11y focus-management pass across custom widgets** (F-159, F-158, F-164, F-161, F-163, R3-006, F-170, F-157). Seven findings share one root cause: hand-rolled listboxes, drawers, sheets and live regions each reimplement (or skip) focus/visibility management the site's own modal already gets right. Extend the shared listbox helpers with close-and-restore-focus, adopt `inert` for hidden layers, add roving tabindex to the radio groups, and keep one always-mounted live region per screen — fix the pattern once, not eight instances.
7. **Discovery benchmark-gap adoption** (R2-025 price filter, R2-024 search suggestions, R2-004 mobile category rail, F-144 persistent header search, F-114/R3-012 sheet reordering, F-112 count-in-apply-CTA). Each is a standard Airbnb/Booking-class mechanic the feed lacks; several need small backend asks or design decisions, so they batch better as one discovery-IA iteration than as piecemeal patches.
8. **Legal center completion** (F-084, F-086, F-085, F-091, F-092/F-093). The document system itself is Stripe-grade (verified), but the IA around it is unfinished: incorporated sub-policies unpublished, a "Rules Center" advertised that no longer exists, zero hyperlinked cross-references, run-on contact blocks, three names for the TOC. Mostly a legal-team content program; the renderer already supports everything needed.

## Remaining risks

- **Data-dependent.** UGC length/quality is uncontrolled (an unclamped 25-line description already dictates mobile page rhythm, F-061); any listing outside the 8 picker cities emits broken LT locatives in titles and H1s (F-175); backend-authored `seo_title_*` carries the brand suffix into H1s until stripped (F-025/F-053); `value_label_en` composes raw LT units (R2-032). The first real review lands on untested layout (see program 4).
- **Coverage skips** — unreachable with real data, explicitly not audited: with-reviews listing layout (no reviewed listing exists in any environment), invite valid-reward state (Branch attribution dormant), error.tsx crash boundary + home SSR band error states (not forceable against prod SSR), categories offline/error (SSR-hydrated), in-grid install banner (needs a longer result tail than 3 listings), lightbox multi-photo nav (pinned listing has 1 photo).
- **Copy sign-offs pending.** Use-case cards (F-191), owner step tags (F-143), LT genitive tiles (F-192), detail state copy (F-193), plus every new string this audit's fixes introduce (owner band, EN hero rewrite R2-035, bridge copy) — marketing/legal review is the bottleneck, not implementation.
- **External blockers.** assetlinks.json still carries placeholder fingerprints (launch blocker at deploy); Branch keys dormant (invite degrades to /go); no Maps key behind the empty handover panel (F-060); real photography for category tiles and the hero phone asset (R2-017, F-013); backend asks — category id on the detail wire, `owner_id` filter, unit localization, seo_title de-suffixing.
- **What the audit could not see.** Animation/motion quality (frozen in captures); real-device behaviour — iOS Safari safe areas, the smart app banner, actual scroll feel; screen-reader behaviour beyond code inspection; and the thing the site exists for: actual store-conversion rates, which only analytics after launch will show.

## Method & coverage

Working tree at a6dc1c2 + 21 uncommitted files, production build, live dev API; both dev and prod verified at ~3 active listings, 0 reviews, all with ≥1 photo. Corpus: 641 fresh PNGs — 8 breakpoints (320/360/390/430/768/1024/1280/1440) × LT+EN across home, feed (5 states), categories, pSEO landings, listing detail, how-it-works (both roles + steps), 3 legal docs, invite and 404s, plus 74 interaction/state shots (drawers, filter sheet, lightbox, app-redirect variants, locale pickers, offline/forced-error, keyboard-focus crops, sticky states). Review: 30 finder agents in 3 rounds (23 surface/dimension vision reviewers + 2 code reviewers + 5 targeted round-2 + 4 round-3), findings deduplicated, then every finding adversarially verified by independent verifier agents with full-resolution element re-captures against the live server. Independent oracles: Playwright e2e suite 11/11 passed; zero horizontal overflow at 21 widths × 9 surfaces, confirmed again by each capture script's own overflow check. Discovery converged: 179 → 34 → 12 findings across rounds. Explicit skips are listed under Remaining risks. 14 findings were killed in verification and are preserved in the rejected appendix — treat that as evidence of calibration, not weakness: what survived, survived an adversary. Screenshot paths in the body are repo-relative and gitignored (evidence is local-only).

---

## Full findings by area

**199 confirmed new findings** — 2 blocking · 16 high · 78 medium · 103 polish. Plus 1 plausible (unproven), 26 re-confirmed known-open, 14 rejected by adversarial verification (appendix).


### Accessibility (cross-cutting) (28)

**F-123 · HIGH** — App-redirect modal (desktop dialog, all trigger variants) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])
- **What:** On desktop, the modal's visually dominant primary CTA — the full-width purple 'Atsisiųsti programėlę' button — links to /go in a new tab, and /go on a non-iOS/Android UA just 302-redirects back to the marketing homepage (app/go/route.ts:16). So the most prominent action in the site's single most important conversion moment is a decoy on desktop: clicking it opens a duplicate homepage tab instead of installing anything. The code comment in AppRedirect.tsx:117-120 admits '/go only resolves to a store on a phone' and that store badges are the real desktop path, yet the dead-end button keeps top visual hierarchy in every desktop variant, above the working QR and badges.
- **Why it matters:** This is the Locked-mode bridge — the whole site funnels here. Best-in-class app-handoff dialogs (Airbnb's app interstitial, Booking.com's 'Get the app' page) make the working path the hero on desktop: a large QR front-and-center or an SMS-link field, never a button that silently loops back to the page you came from. A user who clicks 'Download the app' and lands on a second homepage tab loses trust exactly at the conversion moment.
- **Fix:** Give the /go anchor in AppRedirect.tsx:122 a class (e.g. nk-redirect-smartlink) and make it the mirror image of the existing .nk-redirect-qr breakpoint pair in globals.css:957-965: display:none at min-width:561px (where the QR is shown), visible ≤560px where /go genuinely resolves to a store. On desktop promote the QR block to hero action: bump <QR size={96}/> to ~128-152, wrap .nk-redirect-qr in a subtle card (background:var(--nk-surface); border:1px solid var(--nk-border); border-radius:var(--nk-r-card); padding) so it reads as the primary path, with the existing dict.bridge.qrHint copy and the store badges as the desktop click path beneath. Keep the trackEvent('Smart App Link Click') on the mobile button. No new copy or data needed.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/redirect-reserve-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/redirect-contact-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/redirect-favorite-1440.png`; code: `app/components/AppRedirect.tsx:117-125`, `app/go/route.ts:11-16`, `app/globals.css:952-965`

**F-156 · HIGH** — Hero search (home) (/)
- **What:** The hero search input has no ::placeholder rule anywhere in the CSS, so the light field falls back to UA defaults: Chrome's darkgray #A9A9A9 on --nk-light-field #F9F9F9 computes to 2.23:1, Firefox (input color #282C2D at 54% opacity) to 3.28:1 — both fail WCAG AA 4.5:1. Compounding it, the visible micro-label .nk-search__label is display:none above 560px (globals.css:794), so on desktop this failing placeholder is the field's ONLY visible hint. The token --nk-text-slate #455759 (7.23:1 on #F9F9F9) is documented at globals.css:89 as 'placeholder text in light search field' but is never applied to ::placeholder.
- **Why it matters:** The hero search is the primary conversion entry point; a 2.2:1 hint is illegible for low-vision users where Airbnb/Booking ship ~4.6:1+ placeholder text with a persistent visible label.
- **Fix:** Add to globals.css next to the .nk-search__input rule: `.nk-search__input::placeholder{color:var(--nk-text-slate);opacity:1}` — the token exists for exactly this purpose (7.2:1 on --nk-light-field) and it also aligns the placeholder with the city-picker's 'Visa Lietuva' value which already uses it. Optionally un-hide .nk-search__label at all widths for a persistent visible label (the aria-label already names the field for AT), but the one-line placeholder rule is the core fix.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/globals.css:89`, `app/globals.css:576`, `app/globals.css:794-797`, `app/globals.css:1326`

**F-157 · HIGH** — FAQ accordion (home + How-It-Works) (/)
- **What:** FaqRow's outer div sets overflow:'hidden' (cards.tsx:200) and the disclosure <button> fills the container's full width/height. The global focus indicator is `outline:2px solid` with `outline-offset:3px` (globals.css:484-485), drawn entirely OUTSIDE the button's border box — i.e. outside the overflow-clipped container — so keyboard focus on every FAQ row is invisible. No :focus-visible fallback exists on .nk-faq itself.
- **Why it matters:** Keyboard users get no visible focus on an entire interactive band on two core pages — a hard WCAG 2.4.7 failure; the codebase already solved this exact clipped-ring problem for offer/category cards via :focus-within box-shadow.
- **Fix:** Mirror the card pattern in globals.css next to the .nk-faq hover rules: `.nk-faq:focus-within{box-shadow:0 0 0 3px var(--nk-purple-hover)}` (or the stricter `.nk-faq:has(button:focus-visible)` so pointer clicks don't ring), and suppress the now-redundant clipped outline with `.nk-faq button:focus-visible{outline:none}` scoped to this component only. Applies to both the home and How-It-Works FAQ since they share FaqRow. Do not remove overflow:hidden from the outer div — it protects the rounded hover background.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/cards.tsx:197-211`, `app/globals.css:484-485`, `app/globals.css:650`, `app/globals.css:694`

**F-158 · HIGH** — Mobile nav drawer (all pages ≤1120px) (/skelbimai)
- **What:** When closed at ≤1120px the drawer is collapsed with `max-height:0;opacity:0;overflow:hidden` (globals.css:536-538) — not display:none, visibility:hidden, or inert — so its 6 interactive descendants (Search, 3 nav links, LocaleSwitcher trigger, Get-app button; sections.tsx:221-278) stay in the Tab order and can be focused and activated while fully invisible. Above 1120px the base `display:none` (globals.css:526) is fine; the defect is only in the collapsed mobile state.
- **Why it matters:** A keyboard user at mobile/tablet width tabbing past the burger walks through six invisible stops where the focus indicator vanishes entirely; screen readers can also reach opacity:0 content. The legal TOC drawer does this correctly (display:none when closed, legal.css:203).
- **Fix:** Two equivalent options: (a) CSS-only — add `visibility:hidden;transition:visibility 0s .3s` to the closed .nk-nav-drawer rule (globals.css:536) and `visibility:visible;transition-delay:0s` on `.nk-nav-drawer.open`, preserving the max-height/opacity exit animation; or (b) set the inert attribute from React: `inert={!menuOpen}` on the drawer div in sections.tsx:218 (React 19 supports the boolean prop), which also blocks screen-reader access in one move. Option (b) is the most robust; keep aria-expanded on the burger as-is.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/globals.css:526`, `app/globals.css:536-538`, `app/components/sections.tsx:215-280`, `app/components/legal/legal.css:203`

**F-159 · HIGH** — FilterSelect / LocaleSwitcher / HeroCityPicker listboxes (/skelbimai)
- **What:** All three custom listbox popovers move focus INTO the panel on open (focusListboxSelection), but never restore it to the trigger on close. Escape (`setOpen(false)` in the document keydown, ui.tsx:386 / sections.tsx:378-380 / HeroSearch.tsx:47-49) and option selection (onClick → setOpen(false), ui.tsx:420 / sections.tsx:468 / HeroSearch.tsx:111-114) unmount the panel while an option inside it holds focus, dropping focus to <body>. The next Tab restarts from the top of the document. Tab out of an open panel also leaves it open.
- **Why it matters:** Focus loss after every keyboard filter interaction on the feed's core sort/category/city controls, the nav language picker, and the hero city picker; the site's own modal/sheet layers restore focus correctly via useDismissableLayer, so this is an inconsistency in the shared listbox pattern.
- **Fix:** In each of the three components, hold a ref to the trigger button and restore focus whenever the panel closes while focus is inside it: e.g. add `const triggerRef = useRef<HTMLButtonElement>(null)` and a close helper `const close = () => { setOpen(false); triggerRef.current?.focus(); }` used by the Escape document handler and the option onClick/onSelect paths (for LocaleSwitcher's Link options, refocus before navigation or skip restore only when the locale actually changes). Since the shared listbox helpers already live in ui.tsx (focusListboxSelection, listboxKeyNav), the cleanest shape is extending that helper set with a `closeListbox(setOpen, triggerRef)` so all three stay consistent; additionally close the panel on focusout to an element outside the component (matches WAI-ARIA listbox pattern).
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/ui.tsx:384-396`, `app/components/ui.tsx:420`, `app/components/sections.tsx:369-393`, `app/components/sections.tsx:468`

**F-124 · MEDIUM** — App-redirect modal (reserve/favorite variants) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])
- **What:** The handoff loses all listing context. The reserve and favorite modals are triggered from a specific item (background shows 'Dodge RAM 2016'), but the panel shows only generic brand + copy, and the QR always encodes the generic smart-install URL https://www.naudokis.lt/go (visual.tsx QR default; AppRedirect passes no value). Nothing carries the item, price, or intent across the install: scan → store → install → app opens at its home screen, and the user must re-find the Dodge RAM.
- **Why it matters:** Turo and Airbnb app-continuation surfaces show a compact card of the exact item ('Continue with BMW X5 in the app') and use deferred deep links so post-install the app opens on that listing. For a marketplace whose only transaction path is the app, intent preservation is the difference between a completed reservation and a lost session.
- **Fix:** Phase 1 (pure frontend, real wire data only): extend RedirectPayload (ui.tsx:256) with an optional listing context ({ listingTitle, listingThumb, priceLabel } — all already present in the ListingScreen/ListingDetail view models), pass it from the reserve/favorite/dates/contact triggers (ListingScreen.tsx:94-114, ListingDetail.tsx:527/736), and render a compact item row in the panel above the CTA using existing nk- card tokens (var(--nk-surface), var(--nk-r-tile), nk-imgph fallback when no photo). Phase 2 (blocked on the app deep-link work already tracked in the www-migration memory): accept a ?listing= param on /go and encode it in a per-listing DynamicQR value (QR already supports a runtime value prop, visual.tsx:147) so intent survives install. Phase 1 alone fixes the visible context loss; do not fabricate any field.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/redirect-reserve-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/redirect-favorite-1440.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-redirect-0390.png`; code: `app/components/ui.tsx:256-262`, `app/components/AppRedirect.tsx:113-115`, `app/components/visual.tsx:139-158`, `app/components/ListingScreen.tsx:94-114`; seen independently by 3 reviewers

**F-154 · MEDIUM** — Home hero (mobile) — store badge install CTAs (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** At 320px the Google Play / App Store badges in the hero measure ~34px tall (capped at max-height:40px), and the wrapping anchor `.nk-badgebtn` has `padding:0`, so the tap target is the image height only — under the project's own `--nk-tap: 44px` minimum and Apple's 44pt HIG.
- **Why it matters:** These are the primary conversion elements of the entire bridge site on the device class where installs actually happen. Airbnb/Turo app-download rows keep store badges at >=44px effective tap height. The repo itself defines `--nk-tap: 44px` as 'minimum interactive target (WCAG 2.5.8)' and the bridge modal passes height={44} to the same badges — the mobile hero is the one place that undershoots it.
- **Fix:** In the @media(max-width:560px) block (globals.css ~1317), add min-height to the badge anchors so the hit area meets the project's own standard while the artwork stays 40px: `.nk-appbadges .nk-badgebtn{flex:1 1 0;min-width:0;min-height:var(--nk-tap);align-items:center}`. No markup change needed; verify the row still doesn't wrap at 320px. Downgraded from high: measured 36.4-40px passes WCAG 2.5.8 AA (24px) — the miss is against Apple's 44pt HIG and the repo's --nk-tap standard on the primary install CTAs, a consistency/conversion polish rather than a hard accessibility failure.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-vp-lt-0320.png`; code: `app/globals.css:488`, `app/globals.css:1316-1318`, `app/globals.css:144`, `app/components/ui.tsx:110`

**F-155 · MEDIUM** — Home hero — owner CTA 'Skelbti daiktą ir uždirbti' (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** The owner-side link is 15.5px/700 in `--nk-purple-hover` (#8A89FF) rendered over the translucent hero glass on top of the purple-glow photo background; sampled local contrast in the 320 shot is roughly 3.9:1, below the 4.5:1 AA threshold for text this size (15.5px bold is not 'large text'). The token's documented 4.8:1 holds only against solid `--nk-bg`, not the lighter purple-washed hero panel.
- **Why it matters:** This is the sole owner-acquisition entry point in the hero; supply-side conversion depends on it being unmistakably legible. Turo's 'Become a host' hero link sits on a solid surface precisely to avoid image-dependent contrast. The adjacent prompt line uses rgba(255,255,255,.70) muted text over the same variable image and is also near the floor.
- **Fix:** Lift the CTA text above 4.5:1 against the lightest glass the hero can render (measured max bg luminance ~0.047): add a lighter accent-text token to :root, e.g. `--nk-purple-bright:#A8A7FF` (computes ~5.0:1 vs the lightest measured glass pixel), and use it for the HeroOwnerCta button color — or render the CTA text in var(--nk-text) with the ArrowRight icon carrying the purple accent. Keep the prompt line as-is (it passes). Do not add a scrim panel just for this; the token swap is the minimal fix consistent with the --nk-* system.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-vp-lt-0320.png`; code: `app/components/HeroSearch.tsx:26-30`, `app/globals.css:88`, `app/components/sections-home.tsx:30-33`

**F-160 · MEDIUM** — Feed + categories search inputs (/skelbimai)
- **What:** Both page search inputs have only a placeholder for a name — no <label>, no aria-label, no type="search" (the accessible name falls back to placeholder, which disappears visually while typing). The hero search input does carry aria-label={dict.search.inputLabel} (HeroSearch.tsx:169), so the dictionary key pattern already exists but wasn't applied here.
- **Why it matters:** Placeholder-as-label is the classic WCAG 3.3.2/1.3.1 antipattern; typed text leaves the field with no visible purpose indicator, and voice-control users must guess the control's name.
- **Fix:** Add `type="search"` and an explicit aria-label to both inputs, reusing existing dictionary copy: on the feed input `aria-label={t.searchPlaceholder}` (or add a dedicated feed.searchInputLabel key to types.ts + both dictionaries for a cleaner name), and the same on the categories input. Optionally wrap each field's container in role="search" (the feed filter bar is a natural landmark). No visual change; keeps copy in the Dict per project rules.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:320-321`, `app/components/CategoriesScreen.tsx:50-51`, `app/components/HeroSearch.tsx:169`

**F-161 · MEDIUM** — FeedFilterSheet radio groups (mobile filters) (/skelbimai)
- **What:** FilterSheetGroup renders role="radiogroup" containing <button role="radio" aria-checked> elements with no roving tabindex and no arrow-key handling: every radio is a separate Tab stop (up to ~19 for the city group) and Left/Right/Up/Down do nothing, violating the WAI-ARIA radio-group keyboard contract that screen readers announce ('radio, 1 of 19' invites arrow navigation that fails).
- **Why it matters:** SR users are told these are radios and will try arrow keys per convention; keyboard users must tab through ~30 stops (sort+category+city) to cross the sheet. The codebase already has listboxKeyNav — the same roving-focus helper this needs.
- **Fix:** Implement the APG radio-group pattern in FilterSheetGroup: give each radio tabIndex={sel ? 0 : -1} (fall back to first when nothing selected — never happens here since every group has a default value), and add an onKeyDown on the .nk-filtersheet__opts group that on Arrow/Home/End moves focus AND selection (arrows select in radio groups, so call onChange(options[next].value) after focusing). Generalize listboxKeyNav to take a role selector (e.g. keyNav(e, '[role="radio"]') returning the next element) so the roving logic stays shared. Simpler-but-honest alternative: drop role=radiogroup/radio and keep plain buttons with aria-pressed — but the roving pattern is better since the options are mutually exclusive.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:555-567`, `app/components/ui.tsx:328-344`

**F-162 · MEDIUM** — How-It-Works step tag pills (/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** The .htw-tag step pills are 14px/500 body text, so they need 4.5:1. Computed against their tinted fills composited over --nk-bg #282C2D: purple tone = #8A89FF on rgba(102,101,224,.16) → 4.07:1 (fail); green tone = #10B981 on rgba(16,185,129,.14) → 4.44:1 (fail, marginal); yellow = 8.09:1 (pass). The :root comments only certify these fg colors against the flat bg (4.77/5.56), not over their tint washes.
- **Why it matters:** Sub-AA text on the flagship explainer page; the token system already contains the fix precedent — --nk-green-text #34D399 exists precisely because #10B981 fails on green tints (globals.css:25).
- **Fix:** In TONE_FG (HowItWorksScreen.tsx:251-253): point green at var(--nk-green-text) (existing token, ~5.84:1 over --nk-green-tint). For purple, add a dedicated :root token — e.g. --nk-purple-tag-text: #A3A2FF (~5.3:1 over the --nk-purple-tag wash; keep the token comment certifying the pair) — and use it in TONE_FG.purple; --nk-purple-hover stays for flat-bg links where its 4.77:1 passes. Yellow unchanged. Audit other --nk-purple-hover-on-purple-tint pairings (e.g. Pill purple variant uses solid --nk-accent-bg, unaffected).
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/HowItWorksScreen.tsx:251-258`, `app/globals.css:1378-1379`, `app/globals.css:14`, `app/globals.css:24`

**F-163 · MEDIUM** — How-It-Works step list semantics (/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** Each step is a <button> that CONTAINS an <h3> (HowItWorksScreen.tsx:224) — buttons only permit phrasing content, so the heading is invalid HTML and its heading semantics are stripped/unreliable in the accessibility tree. The buttons also set aria-expanded + aria-controls="htw-preview", but that live-region target is display:none at ≤1280px (globals.css:1515 hides .htw-right) and the replacement inline device is aria-hidden, so on tablet/mobile aria-controls points at a hidden node and step changes announce nothing.
- **Why it matters:** Screen-reader users lose the h3 outline of the 4 steps and get a dangling aria-controls reference on all sub-1280 viewports; the FAQ rows in the same codebase show the correct pattern (heading wraps button).
- **Fix:** Restructure each step to the FaqRow pattern: <h3><button aria-expanded={active} aria-controls={stepRevealId}>{title}</button></h3> with the tag pill, body reveal, and inline device rendered outside the button; give each step's own .htw-step__reveal an id and point aria-controls at that (it exists at all widths), dropping the reference to the desktop-only #htw-preview — the preview's existing aria-live="polite" already announces content changes on desktop without aria-controls. Keep aria-current="step" as-is. If the whole-row click target must stay, make the button absolutely-filled within the row (::after overlay) rather than wrapping flow content.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/HowItWorksScreen.tsx:212-245`, `app/components/HowItWorksScreen.tsx:224`, `app/components/HowItWorksScreen.tsx:215`, `app/components/HowItWorksScreen.tsx:73`

**F-164 · MEDIUM** — Hidden-but-focusable fixed controls (listing mobile bar + legal back-to-top) (/skelbimai/{id})
- **What:** Two always-rendered fixed controls are hidden with opacity+pointer-events only, which does not remove keyboard focusability: (1) .nk-mbar.is-hidden (globals.css:1169) — when the footer scrolls into view the mobile Reserve button stays tabbable while invisible; (2) legal .nk-lg-totop (legal.css:187-192) — opacity:0 + pointer-events:none until .is-on, but the <button> (LegalChrome.tsx:134) is focusable from page load, so Tab lands on an invisible control at the top of every legal document read.
- **Why it matters:** Keyboard focus disappears onto invisible controls — same failure class as the nav drawer but on the listing purchase path and legal pages.
- **Fix:** Add visibility to both hidden states so the controls leave the tab order without killing the fade: .nk-mbar.is-hidden gets visibility:hidden and .nk-mbar's transition list gains `visibility .22s` (visibility animates as a discrete step at transition end, so the slide-out still plays); same for .nk-lg-totop — base state visibility:hidden + `visibility .22s` in its transition, .is-on restores visibility:visible. No JS changes needed; alternatively toggle the inert attribute alongside the class if other focusables are ever added inside the bar.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/globals.css:1169`, `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:892-907`, `app/components/legal/legal.css:187-193`, `app/components/legal/LegalChrome.tsx:134-141`

**F-165 · MEDIUM** — Mislabeled controls (legal drawer close, categories clear) (/teisine/naudojimo-taisykles)
- **What:** Two icon buttons reuse the wrong dictionary strings as their accessible names: (1) the legal TOC drawer's X close button has aria-label={contents} — it announces 'Turinys/Contents', identical to the dialog title beside it, instead of 'Close' (LegalChrome.tsx:117); (2) the categories search clear-× uses label={dict.bridge.close} ('Uždaryti/Close') where the feed's identical control correctly uses t.clear ('Išvalyti/Clear') (CategoriesScreen.tsx:52 vs FeedScreen.tsx:322).
- **Why it matters:** A close button named after the panel's content is confusing to SR users ('Contents, button' twice in a row), and inconsistent naming for the same clear affordance across pages breaks predictability (WCAG 3.2.4).
- **Fix:** Wire the existing-but-orphaned key: add a closeContents prop to LegalChrome, pass t.closeContents from DocumentScreen (alongside contents at DocumentScreen.tsx:98), and use it as the aria-label at LegalChrome.tsx:117 — no new dictionary entries needed since lt/en/types already carry it. In CategoriesScreen.tsx:52 change label={dict.bridge.close} to label={dict.feed.clear} to match the feed's identical clear-× control (WCAG 3.2.4 consistent identification).
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/legal/LegalChrome.tsx:117`, `app/lib/i18n/types.ts:35`, `app/components/legal/DocumentScreen.tsx:96-98`, `app/components/CategoriesScreen.tsx:52`

**F-166 · MEDIUM** — Breadcrumb home crumb (all breadcrumbed pages) (/en/skelbimai)
- **What:** Breadcrumb hardcodes the home crumb as href:"/" (ui.tsx:291) while every other crumb is locale-prefixed by callers. On any /en page (feed, categories, listing detail, legal docs) the 'Home' breadcrumb navigates to the Lithuanian home instead of /en — a silent language switch, most disorienting for screen-reader users navigating by the labeled breadcrumb nav.
- **Why it matters:** Cross-cutting i18n/navigation defect surfaced by the breadcrumb landmark: EN users following 'Home' land on a page in the wrong language with no warning.
- **Fix:** In Breadcrumb (ui.tsx:290-291): const { locale } = useI18nOptional(); then build the home crumb as { label: homeLabel, href: localeHome(locale) } — mirroring the Logo component eight lines above in the same file. Also change the fallback in the map (href ?? "/") to href ?? localeHome(locale) for consistency. No prop-signature change needed, so all callers (FeedScreen.tsx:305, CategoriesScreen.tsx:40, ListingScreen.tsx:120) stay untouched.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/ui.tsx:291`, `app/components/ui.tsx:6-7`, `app/components/ui.tsx:20-22`

**F-167 · MEDIUM** — Sub-44px touch targets (mobile chips, lightbox controls) (/skelbimai)
- **What:** Three touch controls fall under the house --nk-tap:44px standard on coarse-pointer surfaces: (1) .nk-fchip active-filter remove chips — padding 9px + 15px/1.2 text ≈ 36-38px tall, and this chip row is MOBILE-ONLY (.nk-fchips hidden ≥561px), so it exists exclusively where touch accuracy matters; (2) .nk-lightbox__nav shrinks to 42×42 at ≤560 (globals.css:1154); (3) .nk-lightbox__thumb is 46px→40px tall at ≤560 with only 8px gaps between adjacent targets.
- **Why it matters:** Everything else in the kit deliberately hits 44px (--nk-tap, WCAG 2.5.8 comment at globals.css:144); these three mobile-first controls are the stragglers, and mis-taps on the chip's × clear a filter the user meant to keep.
- **Fix:** (1) .nk-fchip: add min-height:var(--nk-tap) (padding already centers content via inline-flex align-items:center) — 8px taller chips also read better next to the 44px filter bar controls. (2) Remove the ≤560 shrink of .nk-lightbox__nav (keep 44×44; 48px only above 560 if desired). (3) Keep thumbs visually 40px but extend the hit area: padding:4px with background-clip:content-box on .nk-lightbox__thumb (the .nk-dot--btn trick), which also absorbs the 8px gap into tappable space.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/globals.css:1026-1032`, `app/globals.css:1153-1154`, `app/globals.css:1598-1599`, `app/globals.css:144`

**F-047 · POLISH** — Categories page — "Vaikams" tile (http://localhost:3000/kategorijos)
- **What:** The "Vaikams" tile's white icon sits on a pale yellow-olive disk over a light gradient — visibly lower icon contrast than every sibling tile, which all use saturated mid-tone disks.

Severity stays polish: the glyph is label-accompanied (tile title carries meaning), so it is a consistency/identity nit rather than a hard a11y failure.

**F-127 · POLISH** — App-redirect modal (all variants) (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** The modal offers no explicit textual decline path — dismissal is only the icon ×, scrim click, or Escape. Every variant stacks three install affordances (QR, smart-link button, two badges) with no 'Toliau naršyti svetainėje' / 'Not now' escape hatch.
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb's and Booking.com's app interstitials pair the install CTA with an explicit low-emphasis text dismiss; it reduces the 'trapped' feeling for users who deliberately chose the web, which matters for a bridge site whose browsing is intentionally web-first. An icon-only × is functional but colder than the 2026 norm for interruption surfaces.
- **Fix:** Add a low-emphasis text dismiss under the badge row: a new Dict key bridge.keepBrowsing in app/lib/i18n/types.ts plus both dictionaries (lt: 'Toliau naršyti svetainėje', en: 'Keep browsing the site'), rendered in AppRedirect.tsx after .nk-redirect-stores as a ghost button (existing nk-btn nk-btn--ghost tokens, centered, fontSize ~15) whose onClick just calls close(). It stays inside the focus trap automatically; optionally trackEvent('Bridge Dismissed', {placement:'text_button'}) for funnel data.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/redirect-navdefault-1440.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-redirect-0390.png`; code: `app/components/AppRedirect.tsx:94-131`

**F-168 · POLISH** — aria-label on generic elements (offer-card rating, footer social group) (/skelbimai)
- **What:** OfferCard exposes the pluralized review phrase via aria-label on a plain <span> (cards.tsx:74) while aria-hiding the visible '(52)' count — but aria-label is prohibited on role=generic (ARIA 1.2) and ignored by several AT/browser pairs, so those users hear only '4,8' with the count silenced by the aria-hidden. Similarly the footer social wrapper puts aria-label={t.socialLabel} on a bare <div> (sections-home.tsx:174) where it is ignored.
- **Why it matters:** The carefully-authored dict.common.reviewCount pluralization never reaches many screen readers; the group label likewise does nothing without a role.
- **Fix:** Rating: give the wrapping span role="img" with the existing aria-label (the APG-sanctioned pattern for composite rating glyphs — keeps dict.common.reviewCount's pluralization), leaving the inner nodes aria-hidden; or drop aria-label/aria-hidden and add an nk-sr-only span carrying the full phrase. Footer social: change the <div className="nk-footer__social"> to <nav aria-label={t.socialLabel}> (it is a set of navigation links, matching the adjacent nk-footer__col <nav>s) or add role="group" if nav feels heavy.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/cards.tsx:74-79`, `app/components/sections-home.tsx:174`

**F-169 · POLISH** — Heading hierarchy (feed grid, footer columns) (/skelbimai)
- **What:** On the feed the outline jumps h1 → h3: OfferCard titles (cards.tsx:68) and the InterruptionBanner title (cards.tsx:148) are h3s that appear before the page's first h2 (the SEO block at FeedScreen.tsx:443). CategoriesScreen fixed this exact skip with an sr-only h2 (CategoriesScreen.tsx:61-63) but FeedScreen has no equivalent. Footer columns are hardcoded <h4> (sections-home.tsx:185,190), producing h1→h4 jumps on pages with no h2/h3 (StatusScreen 404/error, /invite).
- **Why it matters:** Heading-level skips degrade rotor/outline navigation; the codebase demonstrably cares (the categories fix + its comment) so the feed is an inconsistency.
- **Fix:** Mirror the CategoriesScreen fix: add <h2 className="nk-sr-only">{t.titleAll}</h2> immediately above the results region in FeedScreen (reuses existing dict copy, no new key). Demote the InterruptionBanner title from h3 to a <p> with the same inline styles — it is a CTA banner, not a document section. In Footer, change the two column <h4>s to <h2>s and keep the current visual size via the existing .nk-footer__col heading selector in globals.css (update the selector from h4 to h2), which also fixes the h1→h4 jump on StatusScreen and /invite.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:310`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:443`, `app/components/cards.tsx:68`, `app/components/cards.tsx:148`

**F-170 · POLISH** — Loading live regions mounted with content (/skelbimai)
- **What:** The skeleton wrappers use role="status" aria-live="polite" on elements that MOUNT already containing the sr-only 'loading' text (FeedScreen.tsx:397, ListingScreen.tsx:61, CategoriesScreen.tsx:65) and unmount entirely when data lands. Live regions must exist before their content changes to announce reliably, so most SR/browser pairs announce neither the loading start nor the completion. Notably the always-mounted count region (FeedScreen.tsx:343, CategoriesScreen.tsx:56 — with an explicit comment about this exact rule) does it correctly.
- **Why it matters:** Blind users get no feedback that results are loading or have arrived except the (correct) count region on filter changes; initial page loads announce nothing.
- **Fix:** Per screen, keep one persistent sr-only <span role="status"> mounted for the life of the screen (like the categories count region) whose text toggles between "" / dict.common.loading / the loaded result-count string, and drop role/aria-live from the transient skeleton wrappers (keep the wrappers purely visual). Uses existing dict.common.loading + existing count strings — no new dictionary keys.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:396-399`, `app/components/ListingScreen.tsx:61-63`, `app/components/CategoriesScreen.tsx:64-67`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:343`

**F-171 · POLISH** — Filter trigger accessible names lose their label (/skelbimai)
- **What:** When a FilterSelect has a value, the trigger's visible text — and therefore its accessible name — is replaced by the bare value (ui.tsx:411: `{active && selected ? selected.label : label}`), with no aria-label preserving the control's purpose: a SR user tabbing the filter bar hears 'Vilnius, collapsed' with no indication it's the City filter. The HeroCityPicker has the same issue on desktop where its .nk-search__label micro-label is display:none (globals.css:794), naming the trigger just 'Visa Lietuva'.
- **Why it matters:** WCAG 4.1.2 name quality: controls should expose role+purpose, not just current value; Airbnb-class filter pills announce 'Filter, City: Vilnius'.
- **Fix:** On the FilterSelect trigger button (ui.tsx:404) add aria-label={active && selected ? `${label}: ${selected.label}` : label} so SRs hear "Miestas: Vilnius, collapsed" while the visible pill keeps showing just the value. On the HeroCityPicker trigger add aria-label={`${dict.search.labelWhere}: ${value || dict.cityPicker.all}`}. Both reuse existing dictionary strings.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/ui.tsx:404-413`, `app/components/ui.tsx:411`, `app/components/HeroSearch.tsx:71-93`, `app/globals.css:792-794`

**F-172 · POLISH** — Hand-rolled glyph SVGs lack aria-hidden (/)
- **What:** The inline glyph branch of Icon (Play, Apple, Facebook, Instagram, Linkedin — visual.tsx:93-109) emits raw <svg> without aria-hidden="true"/focusable="false", unlike the Lucide branch (lucide-react 1.21 auto-adds aria-hidden when no a11y prop) and the legal Icon set (legal Icon.tsx:33 sets it). Inside the footer social links the unnamed SVGs can be announced as 'image' or 'group' noise by some SR/browser combos alongside the link's aria-label.
- **Why it matters:** Inconsistent with the other two icon systems in the same repo; trivially closes a SR-noise gap on the store/social brand marks.
- **Fix:** Add aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" to both glyph <svg> returns in app/components/visual.tsx (the def.f filled branch and the def.s stroked branch), matching the Lucide branch's effective output and the legal icon set.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/visual.tsx:93-109`, `node_modules/lucide-react/dist/esm/Icon.mjs:36`, `app/components/legal/Icon.tsx:33`

**F-173 · POLISH** — Lightbox thumbnail focus ring clipped (/skelbimai/{id})
- **What:** The thumbnail strip .nk-lightbox__thumbs is an overflow-x:auto container with only 2px padding (globals.css:1147); the global focus outline renders 3px offset + 2px width outside each thumb button, so the ring's top/bottom edges are clipped by the scroll container — keyboard focus on thumbs shows at best a partial hairline.
- **Why it matters:** Thumbnails are the only per-photo navigation for keyboard users inside the lightbox; a mostly-clipped ring is easy to lose against the near-black backdrop.
- **Fix:** Bump .nk-lightbox__thumbs padding from 2px to 6px (covers the 3px offset + 2px ring + 1px slack) so the ring renders fully inside the scroll container; alternatively add .nk-lightbox__thumb:focus-visible{outline-offset:-2px} for an inset ring that can never clip. Keep --nk-purple-hover as the ring color.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/globals.css:1147`, `app/globals.css:1149-1152`, `app/globals.css:484-485`

**R2-007 · POLISH** — Listings feed — results grid semantics (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The results grid is plain nested <div>s (head/tail .nk-grid-feed wrappers around per-card divs, FeedScreen.tsx:411/413), so screen readers get no list context — no 'list, 3 items' announcement and no per-item position — for the page's primary content.
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb and Booking.com expose result grids as lists (role=list/listitem or ul/li) so assistive-tech users can gauge result count and skip between items; here the truthful '3 pasiūlymai' count exists visually but the grid itself is structurally anonymous. Distinct from F-169 (heading levels) and F-170 (live-region mounting).
- **Fix:** Add role="list" to the two results .nk-grid-feed wrappers (head at :411, tail at :413) and role="listitem" to the per-card wrapper div (:270); leave the skeleton grids (already aria-hidden) without list semantics. Note the banner split yields two lists (8 + N-8) — acceptable; screen readers announce each. Keep existing grid styling (roles don't affect CSS).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-fp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:410-419`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:268-276`

**R2-031 · POLISH** — App-redirect modal — desktop handoff options (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id] (reserve variant))
- **What:** The desktop modal's only phone-handoff mechanism is the QR code (plus store links that open on the desktop itself): there is no 'send the link to my phone' alternative — no SMS, no email-me-the-link. AppRedirect.tsx (133 lines) contains no such affordance.
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb, Uber and DoorDash desktop install prompts pair the QR with a 'Text me a link' input because a meaningful share of desktop users can't or won't scan (no camera to hand, QR-unfamiliar, phone elsewhere) — QR-only handoff loses that segment at the single most decisive moment of this site's funnel (reserve intent).
- **Fix:** Scope in two steps, and integrate with the F-130 hierarchy cleanup rather than stacking a fifth parallel action: (1) zero-dependency stopgap — under the QR caption add a muted 'Nusiųsti nuorodą sau el. paštu' / 'Email yourself the link' text link (mailto with the absolute /go URL prefilled in body, subject localized), styled --nk-text-muted so it reads as a fallback, with a trackEvent('Send Link Email Click', {placement:'bridge_modal'}) alongside the existing analytics; strings in the Dict contract + both dictionaries. (2) A real 'Text me the app' SMS input needs a messaging provider — new infra that violates the no-new-dependencies default, so file it as a discuss-first follow-up, not part of this fix.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/redirect-reserve-1440.png`; code: `app/components/AppRedirect.tsx:113-129 (QR + /go button + store badges — full action set, no handoff alternative)`, `app/components/AppRedirect.tsx:122-123 (trackEvent pattern to mirror)`

**R3-006 · POLISH** — How-it-works — step buttons vs hidden aria-live preview (≤1280) (http://localhost:3000/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** Every step button declares `aria-controls="htw-preview"` and the code comment relies on the `aria-live="polite"` preview region to announce step changes ("2 / 4 · Reserve"), but at ≤1280 `.htw-right{display:none}` removes that region from the accessibility tree while the replacement inline device is `aria-hidden`. So on phones and tablets the buttons reference a non-rendered element and selecting a step announces nothing — the documented audible payoff exists only >1280.
- **Why it matters:** WAI-ARIA: aria-controls should reference perceivable content, and a live region that is display:none never fires announcements. Screen-reader users on mobile (the majority context for this site) get no feedback that the phone preview changed. New — F-157/158/159/163 cover other a11y defects on this page but not this one.
- **Fix:** Move the announced payoff into an always-mounted live region: render a .nk-sr-only span (utility already exists, globals.css:503) with id="htw-preview" aria-live="polite" containing the `${active+1} / ${steps.length} · ${current.title}` string at all widths, and drop the id/aria-live from .htw-right (its visible copy of the counter stays purely visual). aria-controls then always references a rendered element and announcements work ≤1280 too.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-how-owner-s4-0768.png`; code: `app/components/HowItWorksScreen.tsx:70-84`, `app/components/HowItWorksScreen.tsx:215`, `app/components/HowItWorksScreen.tsx:237`, `app/globals.css:1512-1515`


### Legal pages (15)

**F-084 · HIGH** — legal-terms (EN) (http://localhost:3000/en/naudojimosi-salygos)
- **What:** The Terms incorporate ~8 sub-policy documents by reference — 'Prohibited and Restricted Items Rules', 'Payments, Fees, and Stripe Rules', 'Cancellation, Refund, and Right of Withdrawal Rules', 'Deposit, Damage, Loss, and Dispute Rules', 'Reservation, Handover, and Completion Process Rules', 'Trust, Checks, and Safeguards Standard', 'Reviews, Search, and Ranking Rules', and a 'Rules Center' — and the 'Where to find the most important information' table explicitly tells users to 'Read the … Rules'. None of these documents are published on the site: the legal manifest contains only terms-of-use, privacy-policy and account-deletion, and no reference is hyperlinked (visible in the table at all captured widths: 1440 y≈5800–8800, 768 y≈6500–8000, 390 y≈15500–17500, 320).
- **Why it matters:** A user told to read rules that govern their money (deposits, cancellations, fees) has no way to reach them on the web — a dead end on the platform's own legal center. Airbnb and Turo publish every policy their terms incorporate by reference and hyperlink them inline; here the references quietly point at app-only documents, which erodes trust in exactly the sections (payments, deposits, disputes) where trust matters most.
- **Fix:** Two-stage fix. (1) Content task (legal team): publish the incorporated sub-documents — the loader/manifest architecture already supports N docs (add JSON pairs + manifest entries + CANONICAL_PATHS routes), and Inline.tsx already resolves [label](doc:slug) markup, so once published only link markup in the four terms/privacy JSONs is needed. (2) Until then, code-fixable now: soften the wayfinding-table copy and body references in both locales' JSON so 'Read the X Rules' is not a dead instruction (e.g. 'described in the X Rules, available in the Naudokis app'), stating explicitly where the documents live. Note the scope is wider than the finder claimed: the Privacy Policy has the identical pattern — section 22 lists 5+ 'appendices' that 'form part of this Policy' whose content is published nowhere.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/legal-audit/terms-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/legal-audit/privacy-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/legal-audit/terms-en-1440.png`; code: `app/lib/legal/data/manifest.json`, `app/lib/legal/data/terms-of-use.en.json:290-313`, `app/lib/legal/data/terms-of-use.lt.json:276`, `app/lib/legal/data/privacy-policy.en.json:128-131`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-085 · MEDIUM** — legal-terms + legal-privacy (EN) (http://localhost:3000/en/naudojimosi-taisykles)
- **What:** No in-document cross-reference is hyperlinked: the 'Where to find the most important information' table's 'Read' column ('Section 3', 'Sections 4 and 6', 'Section 24'…) is plain text even though every section has an anchor id the TOC already scrolls to; same for body references like 'the Identity Verification and Fraud Prevention Appendix'. Emails and external URLs elsewhere ARE styled as purple links, so the absence of link styling here is conclusive. Visible at 1440 (terms y≈5800–8800), 768, 390.
- **Why it matters:** The table exists to route readers, but every destination requires manual scrolling through a ~35k-CSS-px document. 2026 legal-center benchmarks (Stripe SSA, Airbnb Terms) hyperlink every section and policy cross-reference.
- **Fix:** Author section cross-references as anchor links in the doc JSONs (all four terms/privacy LT+EN files): e.g. '[Section 3](#3-what-naudokis-is)' in the wayfinding table's Read column and in body text — Blocks.tsx already stamps every h2 with its toc id and Inline.tsx already renders [label](#anchor) as a link, so zero renderer changes are needed. Scope note: only SECTION references can be linked today; the 'Rules'/'Appendix' references cannot until those docs are published (F-084) — Inline deliberately renders unresolvable doc: refs as plain text. Correction: the terms page URL is /en/naudojimosi-salygos (the finder's /en/naudojimosi-taisykles returns 404).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/legal-audit/terms-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/legal-audit/terms-lt-0768.png`, `screenshots/legal-audit/terms-en-1440.png`; code: `app/components/legal/Blocks.tsx:49-55`, `app/components/legal/Inline.tsx:46-47`, `app/lib/legal/data/terms-of-use.en.json`, `app/lib/legal/data/terms-of-use.lt.json`; seen independently by 3 reviewers

**F-086 · MEDIUM** — Legal docs — all three (LT) (http://localhost:3000/naudojimosi-salygos)
- **What:** All three docs carry the yellow eyebrow 'TEISINĖS INFORMACIJOS CENTRAS' and the terms wayfinding table promises 'Visų teisinių dokumentų žemėlapį → Taisyklių centrą', but the policy-center hub was retired (no /teisine or equivalent route exists — verified 404; app/lib/legal/types.ts comments 'the hub was retired'). The copy advertises a destination the site no longer has, and there is no page listing all legal documents (footer links only 3).

Cheaper interim: rewrite those two JSON rows/sentences in both locales to name the three published documents instead of a non-existent 'Rules Center'. Note corrected code refs — the finder's lt.ts:358-364 / DocumentScreen.tsx:54-58 were the wrong lines.

**F-089 · MEDIUM** — legal-terms + legal-privacy (EN, desktop) (http://localhost:3000/en/naudojimosi-salygos)
- **What:** The sticky sidebar TOC visually ends at numbered item 16 on both Terms (24 sections) and Privacy (23 sections) with no scroll affordance — no fade mask, no visible scrollbar, the left rule just stops (terms-en-1440 y≈2350–2950; privacy-en-1440 same band). Sections 17–24 (Moderation/DSA, complaints, liability, GDPR rights, Contacts) appear not to exist. Code shows the list is overflow-y:auto inside max-height:calc(100vh - 110px), so items are reachable by an invisible internal scroll.
- **Why it matters:** On page load a reader wanting to jump straight to 'Contacts' or GDPR-rights — the most-sought parts of legal docs — sees a TOC that silently cuts off; macOS overlay scrollbars give no cue until the user happens to scroll inside the box. Best-in-class legal centers (Stripe, Airbnb) either show the full TOC or give an explicit overflow cue.
- **Fix:** In legal.css give .nk-lg-toc a persistent thin scrollbar (`scrollbar-width:thin; scrollbar-color:var(--nk-border) transparent;`) and add a sticky bottom fade inside the scroller: `.nk-lg-toc::after{content:"";position:sticky;bottom:0;display:block;height:36px;margin-top:-36px;background:linear-gradient(to top,var(--nk-bg),transparent);pointer-events:none;}` — both use existing --nk-* tokens; apply the same treatment to .nk-lg-drawer__panel for parity.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/legal-audit/terms-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/legal-audit/terms-en-1440.png`, `screenshots/legal-audit/privacy-en-1440.png`; code: `app/components/legal/legal.css:73`, `app/components/legal/legal.css:74`, `app/components/legal/LegalChrome.tsx:37`; seen independently by 3 reviewers

**F-091 · MEDIUM** — legal-privacy (EN) (http://localhost:3000/en/privatumo-politika)
- **What:** Critical contact blocks render as run-on inline key-value text instead of structured lists. §23 Contacts: 'Privacy requests: info@naudokis.lt Support: info@naudokis.lt Operator: MB Naudokis, legal entity code…' flows as one wrapped paragraph — two identical purple links sit adjacent with only a bold label between them. §21 supervisory authority block does the same: 'SDPI website: https://vdai.lrv.lt/ Address: L. Sapiegos g. 17… Email: ada@ada.lt (…) E-delivery box: 188607912…'. The Terms page formats the identical Contacts content as a clean bulleted list (§24), so the two docs are inconsistent. Visible at 1440 (y≈49500–51300) and 390 (y≈90200–93500).
- **Why it matters:** Regulator and controller contact details are exactly what a stressed user scans for; run-on pairs are hard to parse and look unfinished next to the Terms' tidy list. GDPR-mature products (e.g. Booking.com privacy hub) present these as labeled rows.
- **Fix:** In privacy-policy.en.json and .lt.json convert the §21 SDPI block and §23 Contacts block (and the LT §1 controller run-on) from single `p` blocks to `ul` blocks with `**Label:** value` items, mirroring terms-of-use §24 exactly. Data-only change — the existing ul renderer already handles it; no components, no new copy invented (same facts, restructured).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/legal-audit/privacy-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/legal-audit/terms-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/legal-audit/delete-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/lib/legal/data/privacy-policy.en.json:1133`, `app/lib/legal/data/privacy-policy.en.json:1162`, `app/lib/legal/data/privacy-policy.lt.json:1102`, `app/lib/legal/data/privacy-policy.lt.json:1131`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-062 · POLISH** — Listing detail — rental terms (Nuomos sąlygos) section (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/{id} (Dodge RAM 2016))
- **What:** Four full-width single-fact cards (50 €/para, 500 € užstatas, 1–60 dienų, Griežta atšaukimo politika) stack to ~640px of vertical space at 390px, and the first two facts duplicate values already shown in the booking card directly above.

**F-090 · POLISH** — Account deletion — page title (LT) (http://localhost:3000/paskyros-trynimas)
- **What:** The H1 'Paskyros ir duomenų trynimas' renders as two balanced lines ('Paskyros ir / duomenų trynimas') at every width including 1440/768 where one line would comfortably fit — .nk-lg-title caps at max-width:18ch and the 28-char LT title exceeds it, so text-wrap:balance splits it with a short orphan-ish first line and a large empty area to the right.

**F-096 · POLISH** — footer (seen on legal pages, EN) (http://localhost:3000/en/naudojimosi-salygos)

**F-098 · POLISH** — Terms — numbered section headings (http://localhost:3000/naudojimo-taisykles)
- **What:** Two-line numbered legal H2s break with a single-word widow — "12 Atšaukimai, grąžinimai ir teisė atsisakyti / sutarties" leaves "sutarties" alone on line 2.
- **Why it matters:** The site balances its marketing display headings; the legal H2s (the strongest typographic element of the doc system) should get the same treatment so multi-line headings read as set type.

The h2 is display:flex, so balance must go on the text span (a blockified flex item), not the h2 itself. Consistent with .nk-lg-title and the balanced marketing headings; no markup or copy changes.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-algirdasjasaitis-naudokis-web/9fb9966e-78df-4d65-8b0d-80b115027573/scratchpad/terms-mid.png`, `screenshots/legal-audit/terms-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/components/legal/legal.css:88`, `app/components/legal/legal.css:103`, `app/components/legal/legal.css:50`, `app/globals.css:1311`

**F-120 · POLISH** — Legal TOC drawer (http://localhost:3000/teisine/naudojimo-taisykles)
- **What:** The TOC list is cut dead at the drawer's bottom edge (item 11 half-visible, later items hidden) with no bottom fade or scroll affordance, unlike the filter sheet which fades content under its footer.
- **Why it matters:** For a 15+ item document TOC, a hard clip gives no signal that more sections exist below; the sheet's fade treatment already establishes the site's convention for scrollable overlay content.
- **Fix:** Give .nk-lg-drawer__panel an end-of-scroll affordance consistent with the site's overlay language: simplest is a sticky, pointer-events:none sentinel pinned to the panel bottom (e.g. a ::after or last-child div with `position:sticky;bottom:0;height:28px;margin-top:-28px;background:linear-gradient(to bottom, transparent, var(--lg-elevated))`), which signals more content mid-scroll and dissolves into the existing 24px end padding at scroll end. Alternative: adopt the filter sheet's anchored-footer pattern (opaque bar + border-top var(--nk-border-soft)) and relocate the drawer's back-to-top action into it.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `e2e/__screens__/state-legaldrawer-390.png`; code: `app/components/legal/legal.css:206-209`, `app/globals.css:925-926`

**F-140 · POLISH** — listing-detail (rental terms) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id] (Dodge RAM 2016))
- **What:** Insurance coverage ('Įskaičiuotas draudimas: Taip') exists only as one row in the middle of the 20-row spec table; it is not surfaced in the booking card or the 'Nuomos sąlygos' trust tiles where price, deposit, duration and cancellation live.
- **Why it matters:** Included insurance is a top-3 trust signal for renting a vehicle; Turo/Getaround surface protection level right next to the price. Burying real, already-on-the-wire data in a spec table wastes it.
- **Fix:** Derive a real boolean in the detail view-model mapping (app/lib/listings.ts, near the attributes mapping at :528) from the attributes_display entry with id 'insurance_included' (verified on the wire: value_label_lt 'Taip', display_order 45 of 18 rows). When true, append a fifth FactCard to TermsSection (ListingDetail.tsx:640-650) — icon 'Shield' or 'BadgeCheck' (ShieldCheck is already used by the deposit tile), title = new dict keys detail.termInsuranceIncluded / termInsuranceSub in both lt.ts and en.ts mirroring the backend attribute wording ('Įskaičiuotas draudimas' / 'Insurance included') — no claims beyond the field. Keep the spec-table row (it is generic backend data); the tile is additive emphasis. Verify the 2-col tile grid handles an odd fifth item gracefully.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-fp-lt-1440.png`, `/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-algirdasjasaitis-naudokis-web/9fb9966e-78df-4d65-8b0d-80b115027573/scratchpad/crop-terms.png`; code: `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:640-650`, `app/lib/listings.ts:528-530`, `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:547`

**F-152 · POLISH** — Terms of Use (mobile, EN) (http://localhost:3000/en/naudojimo-taisykles)
- **What:** EN legal text uses straight ASCII quotes throughout — ("Terms"), ("Naudokis", "we", "us", "our") — while LT correctly uses typographic Lithuanian quotes („Sąlygos“, „Naudokis“).
- **Why it matters:** Straight quotes in a formal legal document read as unfinished next to the properly typeset LT version; Stripe/Airbnb legal pages use curly quotes. EN typography should match LT care level.
- **Fix:** In app/lib/legal/data/terms-of-use.en.json and privacy-policy.en.json, replace each paired escaped straight quote (\" ... \") with English typographic quotes “ ” (matching account-deletion.en.json's existing convention), taking care to keep the JSON valid (curly quotes need no escaping). Edit the JSON directly — it is the source of truth; do NOT run the stale md→JSON converter (yarn legal:json) per the legal-pages memory. While in there, spot-check for straight apostrophes in the same files for the same treatment.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/legal-audit/terms-en-0390.png`, `/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-algirdasjasaitis-naudokis-web/9fb9966e-78df-4d65-8b0d-80b115027573/scratchpad/crops/d5-terms-en-head.png`, `/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-algirdasjasaitis-naudokis-web/9fb9966e-78df-4d65-8b0d-80b115027573/scratchpad/crops/d5-terms-lt-head.png`; code: `app/lib/legal/data/terms-of-use.en.json`, `app/lib/legal/data/privacy-policy.en.json`, `app/lib/legal/data/account-deletion.en.json`


### How-it-works (17)

**F-075 · HIGH** — how-it-works — steps journey layout (http://localhost:3000/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** At exactly 1280px the page serves the single-column phone-style layout: the active step becomes a full-container (~1216px) card holding one sentence of copy top-left and a small 230px inline phone centered in a ~950px-tall mostly-empty panel; collapsed steps 3/4 are lone title rows floating in full width. The proper two-column layout (steps left, synced device right) only engages at 1281px+, as seen at 1440.
- **Why it matters:** 1280 is one of the most common laptop CSS widths; a design-literate user gets a blown-up mobile composition with ~60% dead space on a core educational/conversion surface. Airbnb's and Turo's how-it-works pages hold a split text+device composition at all desktop widths. The CSS comment shows the single-column fallback was a deliberate mitigation for 1024–1280, but the observed result at 1280 is still far below marketplace-class — the container comfortably fits the 1.05fr/.95fr grid there.
- **Fix:** Lower the collapse breakpoint at globals.css:1512 from max-width:1280px to ~1120px so 1121-1280 gets the two-column .htw-grid (the 340px .htw-phone plus the step list fit comfortably in ~536px columns; spot-check the toggle row and step copy at 1121-1200). For the remaining single-column range, stop the active card stretching empty: constrain the step composition (e.g. .htw-step{max-width:720px} centered, or place the inline .htw-phone--inline beside the step text in a compact row) so the panel height is driven by content, not the phone floating in a full-width void.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/hiw-renter-s2-1280.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-how-owner-s4-1280.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/how-fp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/globals.css:1512-1519`, `app/globals.css:1385`, `app/globals.css:304`, `app/globals.css:1516-1519`; seen independently by 4 reviewers

**F-076 · MEDIUM** — how-it-works — step phone mockups (http://localhost:3000/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** The step device mockups read as unloaded/skeleton UI rather than product UI: step 1 shows four gray tiles with camera icons (reads as failed image loads), step 2 shows one camera tile + a gray bar with ~40% of the screen empty between the "Rezervuota" chip and the "Rezervuoti" button, renter step 4 has stars + two gray bars at top and a button at bottom with a large void between, and the owner payout screen is a single small card + chip in a mostly empty phone.

Turo/Getaround/Fat Llama how-it-works mockups show believable, dense mini-app screens (item cards with imagery, prices, dates) that make the product feel real.
- **Fix:** Two moves, no fabricated data: (1) replace Ph()'s Camera tiles with illustrative category-glyph tiles reusing icons already in the ICONS registry (Wrench, Car, Laptop, Dumbbell) on --nk-ps-card backgrounds, optionally with abstract htw-ps-pill price pills — distinct from the live site's missing-photo placeholder language; (2) densify each mini-screen so content fills the 340/700 frame: add a second content row (e.g. a htw-ps-req row on reserve/review, a second amount/history row on payout) or reduce the inline/synced phone's aspect ratio for sparse screens. Keep bars abstract; do not add fake ratings, counts, or named listings.

**F-078 · MEDIUM** — how-it-works — trust strip (http://localhost:3000/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** The "Mokėjimai per Stripe" (payments) trust card uses a Snowflake icon — semantically unrelated to payments — while the other two cards use well-matched icons (Users for profiles/reviews, ShieldCheck for deposits/help). Both dictionaries hardcode icon: "Snowflake".
