**F-079 · MEDIUM** — how-it-works — hero (http://localhost:3000/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** The hero contains no action of any kind — no CTA button, no store badges, no scroll cue to the role toggle. At 390 the entire first viewport is text (eyebrow + 4-line headline + 6-line lede) and the app-download CTA is hidden behind the hamburger; at 1440 the tall hero band ends with the lede and dead pattern space before the toggle section starts.
- **Why it matters:** Every 2026 benchmark (Airbnb, Turo, Getaround how-it-works pages) pairs the hero statement with at least one action. On a bridge site whose sole KPI is app installs, the first screen offering nothing clickable is a measurable conversion leak, worst on mobile where the nav CTA is also collapsed.
- **Fix:** Add a compact action row under the lede inside .nk-hero-band__inner: simplest is the existing <AppBadges/> component (ui.tsx) which needs no new copy; alternatively (or additionally on mobile) an nk-btn anchor that scrolls to the role-toggle section (give .htw-steps or the toggle an id and use scrollIntoView or a hash link), with new Dict keys in types.ts + both dictionaries (LT 'Pasirinkite vaidmenį', EN 'Choose your role'). **R2-001 · MEDIUM** — How-It-Works — bottom CTA banner (.htw-cta) (http://localhost:3000/kaip-tai-veikia)

Keep text-wrap:balance. Re-verify both locales at 1280/1440/1536.

**F-082 · POLISH** — how-it-works — step chips (http://localhost:3000/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** The dot-chip accent colors across the eight steps carry no consistent meaning: renter Greita=yellow, Apsaugota=green, Netoliese=yellow, Užbaigta=purple; owner Lengva=purple, Patvirtinta=green, Perduota=green, Išmokėta=purple. **R3-007 · POLISH** — How-it-works — owner step 4 payout mock vs step copy (http://localhost:3000/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** The owner journey's mocks price the item at "50 € / d." (step 1 list screen) and the step-4 payout screen shows "+ 50 €" / "Išmoka pervesta" — a payout equal to the full gross daily price — while the step-4 body text directly above it says platform fees apply and are shown upfront ("Taikomi Platformos mokesčiai parodomi iš anksto"). The illustration contradicts the fee disclosure in the same card.
- **Why it matters:** Owner-conversion pages at Turo/Airbnb are careful that example earnings read as net or are clearly framed, because gross-as-payout is the classic bait new hosts complain about. Showing fee-free payout right under a sentence promising transparent fees mildly undercuts the trust message on the supply-side pitch.

**R3-008 · POLISH** — How-it-works — hero H1 line breaking (LT, phone widths) (http://localhost:3000/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** At 390 the LT hero H1 wraps as "Nuomokitės / tai, ko reikia. / Uždirbkite iš / to, ką turite." — the preposition "iš" is stranded at the end of line 3, split from its object "to". `text-wrap:balance` is already applied but cannot know LT prepositions. (Distinct from F-018, which is the HOME hero H1 rag.)
- **Why it matters:** Lithuanian typographic convention keeps short prepositions with the following word; a line ending on "iš" reads as a typesetting error in the page's largest type. Best-in-class LT marketing sites bind these pairs with non-breaking spaces.
- **Fix:** Dictionary-only: in lt.ts:131 bind the preposition to its object with a non-breaking space — "…Uždirbkite iš to, ką turite." — so balance reflows to 'Uždirbkite / iš to, ką turite.' at narrow widths. Recheck 320/360/390 after the change (balance will redistribute all four lines).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/how-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/how-fp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:131`, `app/globals.css:1358-1359`

**R3-009 · POLISH** — How-it-works — bottom CTA banner (.htw-cta) desktop layout (http://localhost:3000/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** At >1280 the HIW CTA banner absolutely pins the Google Play / App Store badges to the TOP-left corner while the headline "Pasiruošę rezervuoti? Tęskite programėlėje" sits at the bottom — the install actions come before the value proposition in reading order. This is the same badges-above-headline pattern flagged as F-003, but on a different component (`.htw-cta`, not the home `CtaBanner`), so F-003's fix will not touch it. The ≤1280 stacked order (copy → badges → QR) is already correct.
- **Why it matters:** Conversion banners at Airbnb/Booking lead with the claim and end with the action; action-first reading order weakens the banner and is now inconsistent with this page's own mobile order once one of the two components gets fixed.
- **Fix:** Mirror F-003's resolution on this component: in HowItWorksScreen.tsx move the <div className="htw-cta__badges"><AppBadges height={50}/></div> to be the last child inside .htw-cta__copy (after the <p>), and change .htw-cta__badges to position:static in the >1280 layout (delete the absolute top-left rule at globals.css:1502). The copy block is already a bottom-anchored flex column with gap:18px, so desktop then reads headline → body → badges; the ≤1280 stacked order (copy → badges → QR) becomes automatic and the order:1/order:2 overrides at 1525-1526 can be dropped. No new tokens or strings.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/how-fp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/globals.css:1502`, `app/globals.css:1503`, `app/globals.css:1522-1527`, `app/components/HowItWorksScreen.tsx:119-124`

**R3-010 · POLISH** — How-it-works — CTA banner QR card (no scan caption) (http://localhost:3000/kaip-tai-veikia)
- **What:** The white QR card in the HIW CTA banner (shown at >768) carries no caption — nothing says "scan with your phone to get the app", while the sibling surfaces already solved this: the invite page renders `qrHint` ("Nuskenuokite QR kodą telefonu…") under its QR and the app-redirect modal has its own "Nuskenuokite telefonu". Same class as F-023 (home hero QR) but a different, unflagged surface that F-023's fix won't cover.
- **Why it matters:** An unlabeled QR floating in a gradient banner relies on the user inferring its purpose; every 2026 install-funnel benchmark (Turo, Revolut-style fintech banners) captions the code. The site is already inconsistent with itself — two of its four QR placements have hints, two don't.
- **Fix:** Make .htw-cta__qr a flex column (QR + caption span) and add a short muted caption under the card. Add a dedicated key howItWorks.ctaQrHint to the Dict contract (types.ts) and both dictionaries, reusing the established short copy 'Nuskenuokite telefonu' / 'Scan with your phone' (same as bridge.qrHint) so no new copy needs sign-off. Style per the invite hint pattern (.invite-qr__hint, globals.css:1565): var(--nk-font-display) 600 14px var(--nk-text-muted), centered under the card. Because the caption lives inside .htw-cta__qr it is automatically hidden ≤768 with the QR (globals.css:1537). Apply the same treatment when F-023's home-hero fix lands so all captioned QRs share one pattern.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/how-fp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-how-owner-s4-1280.png`; code: `app/components/HowItWorksScreen.tsx:124`, `app/globals.css:1506`, `app/globals.css:1537`, `app/components/InviteScreen.tsx:90`


### Overlays (nav, modal, sheet, pickers) (19)

**F-110 · HIGH** — Locale switcher inside mobile nav drawer (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** Opening the language listbox inside the mobile drawer renders a floating panel that is clipped flush against the left viewport edge (the selected "Lietuvių" pill's left rounding and flag are cut at x=0) and it overlays the primary "Atsisiųsti programėlę" CTA, visually truncating it to "…sisiųsti programėlę".
- **Why it matters:** The panel is anchored `right:0` to the trigger with `minWidth:160` (sections.tsx:444-448); the trigger sits ~26px from the left edge inside the drawer, so the panel extends past the screen edge. A dropdown clipping off-screen and occluding the install CTA — the site's #1 conversion action — reads as broken; Airbnb/Booking mobile menus expand language selection in-flow or in a properly clamped layer.
- **Fix:** Give the locale listbox an alignment escape hatch like FilterSelect's existing `[align]: 0` pattern: add an align ('left'|'right') prop to LocalePicker's panel (sections.tsx:446), keep right:0 for the desktop nav and pass left-aligned from the drawer so the panel opens rightward into available space, clamped by the existing maxWidth calc(100vw - 2*var(--nk-gutter)). Better still for the drawer: render the options as an in-flow expansion beneath the Kalba row (accordion inside the drawer) so the layer can never clip at x=0 nor occlude the 'Atsisiųsti programėlę' CTA — the site's primary conversion action.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/locale-open-drawer-0390.png`; code: `app/components/sections.tsx:437-458`

**F-074 · MEDIUM** — Gallery lightbox (desktop, loading state) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])
- **What:** Opening the lightbox shows a huge empty gray panel with only a faint 30px spinner (rendered at 28% opacity via .nk-imgph .nk-imgicon) — still empty 700ms after open in the capture. The full-res photo is fetched from scratch because LB_SIZES requests a 1024/2048px rendition with a different optimizer URL than the already-visible gallery images, and there is no low-res layer underneath the spinner.
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb/Getaround lightboxes feel instant because they paint the already-cached grid rendition immediately and swap in the hi-res image when ready. Here the user taps a photo they can already see and gets a blank void — a step backwards from what was on screen, and the near-invisible spinner (28% opacity in a ~1600px panel) gives almost no feedback that anything is happening.
- **Fix:** In LightboxImage, render an underlay <Image> of the same src using the byte-identical sizes string the big bento tile used ('(max-width: 980px) 100vw, 60vw') so the browser reuses the already-cached grid rendition (objectFit:contain, aria-hidden, faded out once the hi-res photo flips data-loaded); keep the hi-res LB_SIZES image on top and the existing error fallback. Additionally raise spinner visibility with a dedicated override, e.g. .nk-lightbox__ph .nk-imgicon{opacity:.6} in globals.css, using the existing --nk-ps-icon token.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/lightbox-open-1440.png`; code: `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:368`, `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:375-407`, `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:67`, `app/globals.css:378`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-111 · MEDIUM** — Desktop feed filter popovers (category, city) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The category and city popovers have no max-height or internal scroll: at 1440×900 both panels run past the viewport bottom, with the last visible option clipped mid-row (category list cut at "Renginiai…", city list cut at "Palanga") and further options entirely out of view.
- **Why it matters:** FilterSelect's panel (ui.tsx:415) sets `position:absolute` with no maxHeight/overflow. Options past the fold (Kita; Palanga and any later cities) are invisible when the popover opens, and reaching them requires scrolling the page under an open popover — Booking.com and Airbnb clamp long dropdowns to the viewport with internal scrolling.
- **Fix:** On the FilterSelect panel style (ui.tsx:415) add `maxHeight: "min(60vh, 480px)", overflowY: "auto", overscrollBehavior: "contain"` so long option lists (11 categories, 10+ cities) scroll inside the layer instead of running past the viewport bottom; applies to both the down and `direction="up"` variants. Options remain keyboard-reachable today (focus scrolls the page), so this is a UX clamp, not a functional unblock — no dynamic anchor-bottom math needed.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/popover-filter1-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/popover-filter2-1440.png`; code: `app/components/ui.tsx:399-429`, `app/components/ui.tsx:415`

**F-112 · MEDIUM** — Feed filter bottom sheet — apply CTA (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The sheet's apply button says only "Rodyti rezultatus" / "Show results" with no result count, even though the desktop feed already computes and displays a truthful count ("3 pasiūlymai" visible in popover-filter1 shot). This holds in default, EN, and active-filter states.
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb's and Booking's filter sheets preview the outcome ("Show 128 places") so users know whether their filter combination is worth applying — critical here where inventory is tiny and a filter can easily yield 0 results; applying blind then seeing an empty feed wastes the tap.
- **Fix:** Change Dict feed.filtersApply from string to a function key (types.ts:349), e.g. filtersApply(n) with proper Lithuanian pluralization ('Rodyti 1 pasiūlymą' / '… 3 pasiūlymus' / '… 10 pasiūlymų'; EN 'Show 3 results'), following the existing resultCount/reviewCount function-key pattern. In FeedScreen, pass the already-computed truthful count into FilterSheet's applyLabel (the sheet's chips apply instantly, so the parent's list.length/totalCount is live while the sheet is open); reuse the resultCountAtLeast '+' variant when more pages exist, and fall back to the countless label while isLoading so the button never shows a stale number.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-en-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-active-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:643-648`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:156-160`, `app/lib/i18n/types.ts:349`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:606`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-113 · MEDIUM** — All overlays — close buttons (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** Three different close-button treatments across the site's overlays: the mobile nav drawer uses a filled dark rounded-square X, the legal TOC drawer a bordered dark rounded-square X, and the filter sheet a thin white outlined circle X.
- **Why it matters:** Overlay chrome is a system-level component; 2026 marketplace products (Airbnb's sheet/modal system) use one dismiss affordance everywhere so muscle memory transfers. Three styles on three overlays reads as three different authors.
- **Fix:** Add one shared close-button primitive to ui.tsx (e.g. CloseButton: 44px = var(--nk-tap), border-radius matching the nav aesthetic (14px or var(--nk-r-icon)), background var(--nk-surface), border 1px solid var(--nk-border), hover var(--nk-surface-2), Icon name="X") styled once in globals.css, and use it in all four overlays: the filter sheet (FeedScreen.tsx:633, replacing nk-round--outline whose 1px var(--nk-text) white ring is the outlier), the legal drawer (LegalChrome.tsx:117, replacing nk-lg-iconbtn), the app-redirect modal (AppRedirect.tsx:104, replacing nk-redirect-close), and restyle .nk-nav-burger (globals.css:522) to the same geometry so its toggled X state matches. Keep each overlay's existing localized aria-label.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `e2e/__screens__/state-navdrawer-390.png`, `e2e/__screens__/state-legaldrawer-390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/sections.tsx:199-213`, `app/globals.css:522-525`, `app/components/legal/LegalChrome.tsx:117`, `app/components/legal/legal.css:38-41`

**F-114 · MEDIUM** — Feed filter bottom sheet — city section discoverability (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The city filter sits below the sheet's fold at 390px. In both LT shots there is zero visual hint it exists — the only scroll cue is the last category chip row clipped mid-glyph ("Sveikata ir medicininė įranga" cut through the letterforms) under the sticky footer fade. Only the EN shot happens to reveal the "CHOOSE A CITY" label because EN chip copy is shorter.
- **Why it matters:** Location is a primary filter for a P2P rental marketplace (Turo and Hygglo put location first, not last); a filter users cannot see effectively does not exist for most mobile sessions, and the mid-glyph text clipping itself looks unpolished.
- **Fix:** Reorder the FeedFilterSheet groups (FeedScreen.tsx:637-642) so location is above the fold: city → category → delivery → sort (or minimally city above category) — a pure JSX reorder, all labels already in both dictionaries. Note the mid-glyph slicing under the opaque sticky .nk-filtersheet__foot is inherent to any scroll position and cannot be padded away mid-scroll; adding a small padding-bottom to the last group only fixes the fully-scrolled resting state. The ordering change is the substantive fix — with 4 sort chips + 13 category chips the last group will always start below the fold at 390x844, so put the primary marketplace filter (city) first.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-active-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-en-0390.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:637-642`, `app/globals.css:910-911`, `app/globals.css:925-926`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-125 · MEDIUM** — App-redirect bottom sheet (mobile) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])
- **What:** The mobile sheet renders a grabber pill (state-redirect-0390.png, centered above the logo) whose own CSS comment says it 'signals the sheet is dismissible (2026 mobile-sheet convention)' — but AppRedirect.tsx has zero touch/pointer/drag handling. Swiping the handle down does nothing; the sheet only closes via the ×, scrim tap, or Escape.
- **Why it matters:** A grab handle is a strong learned affordance on iOS/Android; every 2026-grade sheet (Airbnb filters, Google Maps, App Store product sheets) that shows one supports drag-to-dismiss. A handle that ignores the gesture reads as broken to mobile-native users — the exact audience this app-install sheet targets.
- **Fix:** Add a minimal pointer-drag dismiss to the sheet: onPointerDown on the panel's grabber zone (≤560px only, gate via matchMedia('(max-width:560px)')), track dY>0 and apply transform:translateY(dY) to .nk-redirect-panel, on pointerup close() past a ~120px threshold (close() already plays the nk-sheet-out exit) else snap back; skip the drag transform entirely under prefersReducedMotion() (already imported in AppRedirect.tsx). If that is judged too much code for the bridge modal, remove the .nk-redirect-grabber span (AppRedirect.tsx:103) and its CSS (globals.css:1608-1614) instead — the sheet already dismisses via scrim tap, × and Escape, so the pill is the only false promise.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-redirect-0390.png`; code: `app/components/AppRedirect.tsx:103`, `app/globals.css:1608-1614`

**F-130 · MEDIUM** — App-redirect modal — action hierarchy (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id] (Dodge RAM 2016))
- **What:** The modal presents up to four parallel install actions. Desktop (1440): QR tile, filled purple 'Atsisiųsti programalę' button, and two store badges — the strongest visual weight (filled button) is on the least appropriate desktop action, while the QR (the actual desktop path) is styled as secondary content. Mobile (390): the /go button plus both store badges are three near-identical download choices.
- **Why it matters:** Fintech-grade interstitials commit to one primary per context: desktop = 'scan to continue' with the QR as hero, mobile = one smart store button. Splitting emphasis measurably dilutes conversion at the funnel's last step.
- **Fix:** Branch hierarchy on the existing ≤560 sheet breakpoint. Desktop (>560): promote the QR to hero — larger QR (e.g. 128–144), a display-font heading via a new Dict key (bridge.qrTitle, LT ≈ 'Nuskenuokite ir tęskite telefone' / EN equivalent), keep the store badges as a quiet secondary row, and demote or drop the /go button (restyle nk-btn--ghost/outline at most), since /go on desktop only round-trips to the home page. Mobile (≤560): keep the single filled /go CTA and collapse the badge pair into a muted text row ('Taip pat: Google Play · App Store' via Dict) or remove it — /go already resolves the correct store from the UA. All new copy through types.ts + both dictionaries; reuse --nk-* tokens and existing nk-redirect-* classes.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/redirect-reserve-1440.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-redirect-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/redirect-navdefault-1440.png`; code: `app/components/AppRedirect.tsx:113-129`, `app/globals.css:952-964`, `app/go/route.ts:11-21`; seen independently by 3 reviewers

**F-141 · MEDIUM** — App-redirect modal (nav default) (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** The role-neutral nav "Atsisiųsti programėlę" button always opens the modal with renter-only body copy: "Programėlėje pasirinksite datas, matysite galutinę kainą ir užstatą, susirašysite, mokėsite per Stripe ir valdysite rezervaciją." (choose dates, see final price/deposit, chat, pay, manage the reservation). An owner-framed variant exists in the dictionary (bridge.listTitle/listBody) but is only used by the hero owner link — an owner who just read the HIW owner tab and clicks the nav install button is sold the renting flow.

(equivalent EN). Keep the specialized variants (reserveBody, listBody) for contextual triggers. Keep lt.ts/en.ts Prettier-conformant.

**F-063 · POLISH** — Gallery lightbox (bottom bar) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])
- **What:** The photo counter reads '1 / 1' when the listing has a single photo — visible at both 1440 and 390. Nav arrows and thumbnails are correctly suppressed for single-image galleries (the `many` flag), but the counter is not, so the bar leads with information that has no function.
- **Why it matters:** Best-in-class galleries (Airbnb, Booking) hide the position indicator for single-photo sets; '1 / 1' reads as leftover chrome and subtly advertises how thin the photo set is without helping the user.

**F-115 · POLISH** — Filter labels — sheet sections and desktop popovers (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** Label voice is inconsistent within the same control set: sheet sections read SORT and CATEGORY (nouns) but CHOOSE A CITY (imperative sentence); on desktop, the sort and category popovers have no internal header while the city popover alone carries a "PASIRINKITE MIESTĄ" heading.
- **Why it matters:** One taxonomy, three label conventions — a design-literate user reads this as the city control having been bolted on later. Best-in-class filter systems (Airbnb) keep every section label in the same grammatical form and every popover with identical anatomy.
- **Fix:** Drop the heading override at both feed call sites: remove heading={cityHeading} from the sheet group (FeedScreen.tsx:639) so it falls back to cityLabel (MIESTAS / CITY, already in both dictionaries at feed.cityLabel), and remove heading={dict.cityPicker.heading} from the desktop FilterSelect (FeedScreen.tsx:338) so all three popovers share identical headerless anatomy. dict.cityPicker.heading stays for the hero city picker. For full LT noun harmony, optionally add a feed sort-section noun (e.g. 'Rūšiavimas'/'Sort by') to types.ts + both dictionaries for the sheet label, since feed.sortLabel ('Rūšiuoti', a verb) doubles as the desktop trigger label.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-en-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/popover-filter0-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/popover-filter2-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:554`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:639`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:338`, `app/components/ui.tsx:416`

**F-116 · POLISH** — Desktop filter popovers — anchor alignment (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** Adjacent popovers anchor to opposite edges of their triggers: the category panel is left-aligned to the Kategorija chip, while the city panel is right-aligned to the Miestas chip and extends leftwards back underneath the Kategorija chip.
- **Why it matters:** With no viewport constraint forcing it (there is ample room to the right at 1440), the flip looks arbitrary; consistent left-edge anchoring for left-cluster filters is the expected pattern and keeps each panel visually tied to its trigger.

One-word diff — ui.tsx already supports it.

**F-117 · POLISH** — Feed filter bottom sheet — chip selection reflow (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** Selecting a category chip appends the check icon, widening the chip and re-wrapping the entire chip cloud: in the default shot the rows are [Visos kategorijos] / [Įrankiai ir statyba, Namai ir sodas] / [Transportas, Fotografija ir video]…, in the active shot they reshuffle to [Visos kategorijos, Įrankiai ir statyba] / [Namai ir sodas, Transportas] / [Fotografija ir video✓]….
- **Why it matters:** Every tap makes all chips jump to new positions mid-interaction, so the chip the user just read is no longer where it was — Airbnb's filter chips keep constant width on selection (state shown by fill/stroke only) precisely to avoid this.
- **Fix:** Make chip width state-invariant in FilterSheetGroup (FeedScreen.tsx:559-564): render the BadgeCheck slot unconditionally with opacity: sel ? 1 : 0 (fixed 18px slot, aria-hidden) so selection never changes a chip's width — preserves the non-color state cue alongside the .is-selected accent fill. Alternative (Airbnb pattern, saves ~26px per chip): drop the icon entirely and let the accent fill/border carry state — role=radio aria-checked already conveys it programmatically — but prefer the fixed slot for the redundant visual cue.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-active-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:559-564`, `app/globals.css:917-920`

**F-118 · POLISH** — Feed filter bottom sheet — footer buttons (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** In the active-filter state the footer pairs a noticeably shorter "Išvalyti" ghost pill (~50px) next to the taller "Rodyti rezultatus" CTA (~64px); the two pills sit center-aligned with mismatched heights and radii scale.
- **Why it matters:** A mixed-height button pair in a sticky footer reads unfinished; Airbnb's sheet footer resolves this with a text-style "Clear all" link against a solid button, or two equal-height buttons.
- **Fix:** Equalize the pair with a footer-scoped rule in globals.css: `.nk-filtersheet__foot .nk-btn--ghost{padding-block:16px;border-radius:var(--nk-r-pill)}` so Išvalyti matches the CTA's 52px height and pill radius without touching other ghost-button uses (e.g. the feed's load-more). Alternative per Airbnb's sheet footer: restyle Išvalyti as a plain text control (reuse the .nk-clear pattern from FeedScreen.tsx:345) vertically centered against the CTA — but the equal-height pill is the smaller diff and matches the site's pill language.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-active-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:643-648`, `app/globals.css:335-336`, `app/globals.css:321-323`

**F-126 · POLISH** — App-redirect bottom sheet (mobile) — store badge row (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])
- **What:** In the mobile sheet, the global ≤560px override (.nk-appbadges{width:100%} + .nk-badgebtn{flex:1 1 0} + img{object-position:left}, written for the hero) also hits the modal's badge row: it defeats .nk-redirect-stores' intended centering, stretches each badge button to half-width with the graphic left-fitted, and produces an uneven rhythm — ~36px of visual gap between the two badge graphics (vs the 10px flex gap) plus ~22px of trailing dead space after the App Store badge. The badge graphics are also capped at 40px tall there (max-height:40px), just under the --nk-tap 44px token, though the stretched hit area compensates in width.
- **Why it matters:** The store badges are the legally-recognizable install affordance; a lopsided, unevenly-gapped badge row in the site's key conversion sheet reads as unfinished next to the otherwise crisp left-aligned stack. App-install sheets on Booking/Airbnb keep badge pairs optically even.
- **Fix:** Don't rescope the global hero rule (footer, CTA banner, invite and HIW badge rows also render ≤560px and may rely on it); instead add a counter-override for the sheet inside the existing @media(max-width:560px) redirect block (globals.css:957-965): .nk-redirect-stores .nk-appbadges{width:auto;gap:12px!important} .nk-redirect-stores .nk-badgebtn{flex:0 1 auto;min-width:0} .nk-redirect-stores .nk-badgebtn img{width:auto!important;max-width:100%;max-height:44px;object-position:center}. That restores the intended centered, evenly-gapped intrinsic-width pair at 44px (matching --nk-tap and the AppBadges height={44} prop), and the min-width:0 + object-fit:contain path still shrinks gracefully at 320px.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-redirect-0390.png`; code: `app/globals.css:1298`, `app/globals.css:1316-1318`, `app/globals.css:956`, `app/components/AppRedirect.tsx:127`

**F-128 · POLISH** — Gallery lightbox (mobile, full-screen overlay) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])
- **What:** The lightbox overlay (position:fixed inset:0) uses uniform padding clamp(12px,3vw,40px) — only 12px at 390 — with env(safe-area-inset-bottom) applied to the bottom bar but no safe-area-inset-top, so the 44px close button sits 12px from the physical top edge. Fine in the Pixel-7 capture, but in iOS standalone/PWA display (the site ships a manifest) the button would collide with the status-bar/Dynamic-Island zone.
- **Why it matters:** Full-screen media viewers at the 2026 bar (Airbnb, Photos-style viewers) pad interactive chrome by the top safe-area inset so the close control is always tappable on notched devices.
- **Fix:** In .nk-lightbox (globals.css:1118-1119) keep the uniform padding but add padding-top:max(clamp(12px,3vw,40px),env(safe-area-inset-top)) — and for landscape-notch completeness padding-left/right:max(clamp(12px,3vw,40px),env(safe-area-inset-left/right)). The bottom bar already handles env(safe-area-inset-bottom) (1133). No token or markup changes needed; the site already opts into insets via viewportFit:'cover'.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/lightbox-open-0390.png`; code: `app/globals.css:1118-1122`, `app/globals.css:1132-1133`, `app/[lang]/layout.tsx:83-90`, `app/manifest.ts:14`

**R2-002 · POLISH** — Footer bottom bar — payment marks row (all pages, both locales) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The June-26 baseline footer paired the four payment marks (Visa / Apple Pay / G Pay / Mastercard) with a green shield-icon caption "Saugūs atsiskaitymai"; the current footer bottom bar renders only the copyright line plus the four bare logos. The caption is gone from the JSX (bottom bar renders only t.copyright + FOOTER_PAY images) and the footer.secure key — briefly renamed to "Apsaugoti mokėjimai" in commit 61c0342 — has since been deleted from the Dict contract entirely, which reads as an unintended drop rather than a decision.
- **Why it matters:** Unlabeled card logos in the footer of a site that takes no web payments read as decorative clutter rather than a trust signal; Booking.com and Airbnb always frame payment branding with a caption ("Secure payments", partner framing). The baseline framing tied the marks to the platform's escrow story; losing it weakens the only payment-trust cue in the persistent chrome.
- **Fix:** Get an explicit owner decision. Option A (recommended): reinstate the caption — restore the footer.secure Dict key with the last-shipped real values ('Mokėjimai per Stripe' / 'Payments by Stripe' — no fabrication; Stripe is already named on the home/HIW trust cards), the nk-footer__secure span in Footer, and the two removed .nk-footer__secure CSS rules verbatim from git. Option B: remove the four payment marks as well so the footer doesn't ship unexplained card logos. If the removal was deliberate, record it in do-not-reflag so it isn't re-flagged.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/desktop/lt-skelbimai.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-fp-lt-1440.png`, `/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-algirdasjasaitis-naudokis-web/9fb9966e-78df-4d65-8b0d-80b115027573/scratchpad/crops/tb-bot.png`; code: `app/components/sections-home.tsx:156-158`, `app/components/sections-home.tsx:195-203`, `app/lib/i18n/types.ts (footer.secure removed in working diff)`, `app/globals.css (.nk-footer__secure rules removed in working diff)`

**R3-011 · POLISH** — Mobile bottom sheets — feed filter sheet vs app-redirect sheet (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The two mobile bottom sheets disagree on the grabber convention: the app-redirect sheet renders a centered grabber pill above its content (state-redirect-0390.png, y~938), while the feed filter sheet — the site's other, more heavily used bottom sheet — has none (sheet-filters-lt-0390.png / sheet-filters-en-0390.png / sheet-filters-active-lt-0390.png all open straight into the 'Filtrai' title row). Code confirms: `.nk-redirect-grabber` (globals.css:1608-1614) exists only in the redirect panel; the filter sheet's `.nk-sheet` (globals.css:904) has no grabber element.
- **Why it matters:** The CSS comment itself calls the grabber a '2026 mobile-sheet convention'; applying it to one sheet but not the other makes the overlay system read as assembled from two kits. Airbnb and Booking.com apply one sheet anatomy (grabber, header, footer) uniformly, so users learn the dismiss affordance once. This also compounds the already-flagged close-button inconsistency (F-113) and grabber-semantics issue (F-125).
- **Fix:** Unify sheet anatomy: promote .nk-redirect-grabber to a generic .nk-sheet-grabber (same tokens: 36×4px, var(--nk-border-strong), display:block ≤560 only), reference it from both AppRedirect.tsx:103 and as the first child of .nk-filtersheet in FeedFilterSheet (aria-hidden="true"). Resolve jointly with F-125: if grabbers stay, implement swipe-to-dismiss on both sheets in one shared handler; if F-125 resolves by removing the affordance, remove it from the redirect sheet instead — either way both sheets must match.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-redirect-0390.png`; code: `app/components/AppRedirect.tsx:103`, `app/globals.css:1608-1614`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:630-636`, `app/globals.css:904`

**R3-012 · POLISH** — Feed filter bottom sheet — section order vs desktop toolbar (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The mobile filter sheet leads with the SORT section (RŪŠIUOTI first, then KATEGORIJA, then city, then the delivery toggle — FeedScreen.tsx:637-641), while the desktop surface presents Category → City → Delivery as the filter row and keeps sort as a separate control on the search row. In the sheet, the 4 sort chips plus 12 category chips consume the entire first screen at 390px (sheet-filters-lt-0390.png), which is what pushes the city section and delivery toggle below the fold in the first place.
- **Why it matters:** Sort is a results-presentation control, not a filter, and it is the least decision-critical dimension for a 3-listing inventory; Airbnb's and Booking.com's mobile filter sheets either exclude sort or place it last, leading with the highest-intent dimensions (category/location). The order mismatch also breaks the mental model users form on desktop. Reordering (category → city → delivery → sort) would surface part of the city section at the fold, directly easing the known F-114 discoverability problem.
- **Fix:** Reorder the FeedFilterSheet children (FeedScreen.tsx:637-641) to category → city → delivery → sort, i.e. move the sort FilterSheetGroup below the delivery Toggle so the sheet mirrors the desktop filter-row order and sort sits last as a presentation control. Pure JSX move — no new strings, tokens, or props; combined with F-114's scroll-cue fix this surfaces the city section at or near the 390px fold.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/sheet-filters-en-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/popover-filter0-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:637-641`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:325`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:337-339`


### Footer & chrome (10)

**F-015 · MEDIUM** — Sitewide sticky header (scrolled state) (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** The condensed scrolled nav uses a 40%-alpha translucent background, so the hero's white search pill and purple 'Ieškoti' button stay clearly readable through the header band mid-scroll: the placeholder 'Ką norite išsinuomoti?' is legible through the chrome, and the nav labels 'Kategorijos' / 'Nuomojami daiktai' sit directly over the washed-white bleed-through, visibly reducing their contrast and making the band look noisy.
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb, Booking.com and Turo all solidify the header to near-opaque on scroll precisely so page content can never wash out the primary navigation; a chrome band that content shines through reads as unfinished on the most-trafficked path (home scroll).
- **Fix:** Tokenize and raise the scrolled veil: add --nk-nav-veil:rgba(20,22,23,.22) and --nk-nav-veil-scrolled:rgba(20,22,23,.74) to :root, use them in .nk-nav-bar (app/globals.css:507) and .nk-nav-bar.nk-scrolled (app/globals.css:512). At ~.74 alpha the existing blur(34px) saturate(160%) brightness(.82) keeps the glass identity while the hero's white search pill can no longer wash out the nav labels mid-scroll; keep the at-rest .22 'melted' state unchanged.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/faq-open-1280.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/nav-scrolled-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/feed-backtotop-0390.png`; code: `app/globals.css:506-514`; seen independently by 5 reviewers

**F-029 · MEDIUM** — Listings feed — breadcrumb (small phones) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai?q=zzznonexistent)
- **What:** At 320px the breadcrumb wraps into three stacked rows ("Pagrindinis ›" / "Nuomojami daiktai ›" / current-page chip), each chevron orphaned at line end, consuming roughly 250px of vertical space before the H1; at 390px the search-results breadcrumb also wraps with a dangling "›" at the right edge.
- **Why it matters:** Three loosely-spaced breadcrumb rows on a small phone spend ~30% of the first viewport on wayfinding chrome. Booking.com and Airbnb collapse mobile breadcrumbs to a single back-link or ellipsis-truncate middle crumbs; orphaned trailing separators are a classic unfinished-responsive tell.
- **Fix:** In Breadcrumb (app/components/ui.tsx), wrap each non-last crumb and its trailing chevron in a single `<span style={{display:"inline-flex", alignItems:"center", gap:4, whiteSpace:"nowrap"}}>` so a crumb never separates from its '›' on wrap; keep the nav's flexWrap but set `row-gap: var(--nk-gap-2xs)` (or the closest existing --nk-gap-* token) via .nk-crumbs in globals.css to tighten stacked rows. Combined with hiding the current-page chip ≤680px (F-031), the 320px trail collapses to one row ('Pagrindinis › Nuomojami daiktai').
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-empty-vp-lt-0320.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-0320.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-search-vp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/ui.tsx:302-309`, `app/globals.css:975-979`, `app/components/ui.tsx:293`; seen independently by 7 reviewers

**F-101 · MEDIUM** — Root 404 (unlocalized not-found) (http://localhost:3000/<unmatched-root-url>)
- **What:** The root-level 404 renders visibly off-brand chrome: headline and body are system-ui (SF Pro in the capture), not Archivo/Sora; the header drops the language picker and the 'Atsisiųsti programėlę' CTA button and right-aligns the nav links instead of centering them; there is no footer. The localized 404 (StatusScreen) keeps full Nav+Footer chrome, so the two 404 variants look like different products.
- **Why it matters:** Error pages are part of the brand surface — Airbnb's 404 keeps full chrome and brand typography. The comment in app/not-found.tsx explains the standalone constraint (outside app/[lang]), but the font break and missing install CTA/locale switcher are all visible and fixable without the locale layout.
- **Fix:** In app/not-found.tsx: (1) load Archivo + Sora via next/font/google at module scope and apply them (display font on h1/nav/buttons, body font on paragraphs) instead of system-ui at line 80; (2) mirror the standard header — centered nav links plus the pill install CTA linking to /go (reuse the existing bilingual 'Atsisiųsti programėlę / Get the app' label); (3) add a slim static footer bar (logo + © + contact link). Keep the standalone-page constraint and the inlined --nk-* mirror values (documented at :5) in sync; the LT-primary + EN-secondary copy stays.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/root-404-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/root-404-1440.png`, `e2e/__screens__/notfound-0390.png`; code: `app/not-found.tsx:80`, `app/not-found.tsx:83`, `app/not-found.tsx:101`, `app/not-found.tsx:218`; seen independently by 6 reviewers

**F-145 · MEDIUM** — Listing detail vs feed/landing breadcrumbs (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/<id>)
- **What:** On the listing detail the header highlights 'Nuomojami daiktai' as the active section while the breadcrumb routes through a different parent ('Pagrindinis > Kategorijos > Transportas > Dodge RAM 2016'); the city landing breadcrumbs instead route through 'Nuomojami daiktai' ('Pagrindinis > Nuomojami daiktai > Kaunas'). The same inventory thus has two competing canonical trails, and active-nav and breadcrumb disagree on the listing page.
- **Why it matters:** One coherent product should present a single mental model of where a listing lives; Turo's detail breadcrumb and nav state always agree. The mismatch is subtle but exactly the kind of seam a chrome audit should catch.
- **Fix:** Standardize the listing detail's visible trail on the feed parent to match nav active state, the landing pages and the page's own JSON-LD: in detailCrumbs (app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:912-920) replace the 'Kategorijos' root crumb with the feed crumb ({ label: dict.feed.titleAll, href: localePath(locale, '/skelbimai') }), keeping the category crumb's existing search href as the middle level. Optionally add that same category level to the JSON-LD in app/[lang]/skelbimai/[id]/page.tsx:106-110 — but only as a /skelbimai search/landing path; note the detail wire's category_names carry no category id (listings.ts:8,79), so the canonical /nuoma landing path can't be linked until the backend exposes the id. No layout or dictionary changes needed (feed.titleAll exists in both locales).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-vp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-city-kaunas-1440.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:912-920`, `app/components/sections.tsx:59-63`, `app/[lang]/skelbimai/[id]/page.tsx:106-110`, `app/lib/breadcrumbs.ts:11-37`

**F-045 · POLISH** — Footer (all pages) (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** The footer 'Kategorijos' column lists 10 category landing links with no 'Visos kategorijos' link to the /kategorijos hub, even though the dictionary key footer.allCategories ('Visos kategorijos') exists and is unused; the categories page itself reports 12 categories, so two are unreachable from the footer, and the help column likewise has no link to the browse feed (/skelbimai).

**F-133 · POLISH** — Footer (all desktop surfaces) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The two-column "Kategorijos" link grid row-pairs items, so two-line labels (Elektronika ir technologijos, Garsas, muzika ir renginių technika) stretch their row and leave irregular vertical gaps in the sibling column — gap deltas alternate ~52px vs ~85px raw down the left column.

**F-136 · POLISH** — Footer at mobile (all pages) (http://localhost:3000/naudojimo-taisykles)

**F-150 · POLISH** — Feed — mobile pre-results chrome (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** At 390px the 'Filtrai' pill sits alone on its own row under the full-width search field with ~60% dead space to its right, and the stack of breadcrumb + H1 + 2-line subhead + search + filter row + count pushes the first listing photo to ~500px CSS.

- **Fix:** At the phone breakpoint, move the 'Filtrai' trigger onto the count row: render the .nk-filters-mobilebtn inside .nk-filter-meta's row (count left, button right), mirroring the count/'Išvalyti' pattern already at FeedScreen.tsx:343-349, via a ≤680 media rule in globals.css (hide it in the search row, show it in the meta row) or a conditional layout.
