**R2-005 · POLISH** — Listings feed — sticky filter bar while scrolled (mobile) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The sticky .nk-filterbar pins not just the search field + Filtrai pill but also the result-count meta row ('3 pasiūlymai' / clear link) and its divider, so mid-scroll the pinned chrome stack is nav (68px) + bar (~112px) ≈ 180px of a 390×844 viewport — visible pinned at scroll 2200 in feed-backtotop-0390.png where the count row and divider are still stuck under the nav long after the grid has scrolled past.
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb collapses its pinned search into a compact pill on scroll and does not pin the result count; the count is context, not a control, and pinning it costs ~40px of card visibility on every phone scroll. The house CSS comment itself frames the sheet collapse as 'reclaims ~200px', so pinned-height economy is an explicit design goal this row works against.
- **Fix:** Move the .nk-filter-meta row (count + clear) out of .nk-filterbar in the JSX so it scrolls away with the page — Airbnb-style: pin only search + Filtrai. Preserve the aria-live='polite' count announcement by keeping the span mounted in the same position relative to the results (relates to F-170's mount-with-content note). Alternative if desktop must keep the count in the bar: add an is-stuck class via an IntersectionObserver sentinel (filterBarRef already exists) and collapse .nk-filter-meta ≤560 only while stuck.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/feed-backtotop-0390.png`; code: `app/globals.css:1004-1006`, `app/globals.css:1015-1023`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:315`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:342-349`

**R3-001 · POLISH** — Footer (all pages) — category column heading (http://localhost:3000/ vs http://localhost:3000/en)
- **What:** The footer's category-links column is headed "Kategorijos" in LT but "Browse" in EN (footer.browseHeading). The two locales name the same column by different concepts — LT describes the content (Categories), EN describes an action (Browse). On /en, "Browse" additionally does double duty: it is already the home categories-section eyebrow ("BROWSE / Popular rental categories"), so the same word labels two different navigation tiers, while LT keeps them distinct ("NARŠYKITE" eyebrow vs "Kategorijos" footer heading).
- **Why it matters:** The brief requires EN to be an equivalent-quality parallel of canonical LT, not a loose paraphrase. Airbnb/Turo footers use content-descriptive column heads ("Support", "Hosting", "Categories") consistently across locales; a locale-dependent heading concept reads as unreviewed translation drift, and reusing one word for two nav tiers weakens scannability on /en.
- **Fix:** Change en.ts:313 footer.browseHeading from "Browse" to "Categories" — matches the canonical LT concept (content-descriptive column head), matches the column's actual content, and stays distinct from the 'Browse' section eyebrows at en.ts:41/460. One-line dictionary change; the Dict contract and layout are untouched, and the footer nav's aria-label improves for free.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-en-0390.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-en-1440.png`; code: `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:313`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:341`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:41`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:460`


### Invite / 404 / states (6)

**F-099 · HIGH** — Listings feed — offline state (/skelbimai?q=sony (offline))
- **What:** When the connection drops after a browse, the feed keeps rendering the previously cached, unfiltered results under the NEW query's heading with no offline indication anywhere: the shot shows "Rezultatai pagal „sony“" and "3 pasiūlymai" over a Dodge RAM, a MacBook and a Toyota Prius — none of which match "sony". Live prod API check confirms q=sony returns 0 items, so the page is asserting three matches that don't exist, with no banner, toast or dimming to signal offline/stale data.
- **Why it matters:** Stripe/Airbnb-grade products never silently assert wrong results: Airbnb greys the grid and shows a connectivity toast; Google apps pin a persistent "You're offline" strip. Mislabeled result counts are a direct trust failure on the core browse surface. The code has all the pieces (dict.offline copy, offline illustration, useReloadOnReconnect) but the offline branch at FeedScreen.tsx:401 only fires when `isError || loaded.length === 0`, so cached/keepPreviousData results render as a normal, fully-trustworthy-looking feed.
- **Fix:** Two-part fix in FeedScreen.tsx, all copy already in both dictionaries: (1) when !online && list.length > 0, render a persistent slim offline strip above the grid (role="status", dict.offline.title, styled with existing tokens — e.g. color-mix(--nk-yellow 8%) background + --nk-hairline border, --nk-font-display 15px); (2) read isPlaceholderData (and fetchStatus) from useListingsInfinite and, while placeholder pages back a changed queryKey, replace countLabel with an em-dash and dim the grid (opacity ~.55) so the previous total is never asserted under the new query heading. No fabricated data, aria-live already present on the count.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/feed-offline-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/feed-offline-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:401`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:137`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:155`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:343`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-100 · MEDIUM** — Listings feed — error state (/skelbimai?q=canon (API error))
- **What:** While the feed request has failed and the retry card is displayed, the results toolbar still asserts "0 pasiūlymų" (plus an "Išvalyti" clear action). The page simultaneously claims a known-zero result count and "we couldn't load results".
- **Why it matters:** A count is a factual claim; during an error the count is unknown. Stripe's error-state guidance (and Booking.com's failed-search behavior) is to withhold metrics you can't verify — "0 offers" next to "couldn't load, check your connection" is contradictory and can convince a user the marketplace is empty. Code-confirmed: countLabel at FeedScreen.tsx:156-160 renders unconditionally at line 343 regardless of isError.
- **Fix:** Gate the count in FeedScreen.tsx:343: render the span only when !isError && !isLoading (or show an em-dash otherwise) — e.g. {!isError && !isLoading && <span aria-live="polite" ...>{countLabel}</span>}. One-line conditional, no new dictionary keys; keep the Išvalyti button (clearing the query is a valid recovery action during an error).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/feed-error-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/feed-error-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:156`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:343`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:404`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-054 · POLISH** — Category landing intro vs empty state (/nuoma/foto-video)
- **What:** The intro promises concrete browsable inventory — "Skelbimuose matysite konkrečias parinktis: fotoaparatus, objektyvus, dronus ir apšvietimą; palyginkite kainą, būklę, nuotraukas…" (EN: "Browse real options such as cameras, lenses, drones…") — rendered directly above a "Šioje kategorijoje dar nėra nuomos pasiūlymų" empty state in the same viewport at 1440.
- **Why it matters:** Promise/reality contradiction on one screen undermines the otherwise honest empty state; trust-first marketplaces (and this site's own no-fabrication rule) avoid copy that asserts inventory the page visibly lacks.
- **Fix:** Make the landing subtitle state-aware in FeedScreen: once the listings query has resolved with totalCount === 0 on a category landing, swap the authored seoBody for a capability-framed Dict string (new `feed.subtitleEmptyCategory`, or reuse subtitleAll) and restore the authored copy when totalCount > 0 — the count is already in the hydrated cache so no extra fetch or flash. Longer-term content task: author seo_description_* as capability framing ('palyginkite kainą, būklę…') rather than inventory assertions ('Skelbimuose matysite…').
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/land-cat-foto-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-cat-foto-en-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-cat-sveikata-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:199`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:311`, `app/lib/categories.ts:72`

**F-102 · POLISH** — Root 404 page — EN parity (/<unmatched-url> (reached from /en))
- **What:** On the bilingual root 404, English gets only one smaller, lower-contrast body sentence ("The address may be wrong…") — no EN title, and both action buttons ("Į pradžią", "Naršyti nuomą") are LT-only. Only the tertiary link is bilingual ("Atsisiųsti programėlę / Get the app").
- **Why it matters:** An EN visitor hitting a bad URL can read why they're here but cannot read what the two buttons do. The brief's rule is EN must be equivalent quality, not an afterthought; Booking.com localizes error CTAs fully. The current design translates the diagnosis but not the recovery.
- **Fix:** Make the two CTAs bilingual in the same primary/secondary pattern the tertiary link already uses (app/not-found.tsx:203-208): 'Į pradžią / Home' and 'Naršyti nuomą / Browse rentals'. No locale inference needed — /en URLs already get the localized StatusScreen 404 (verified), and this standalone page sits outside I18nProvider so inline bilingual strings match its existing convention (cf. the bilingual metadata title at :10).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/root-404-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/root-404-1440.png`; code: `app/not-found.tsx:203`, `app/not-found.tsx:206`, `app/not-found.tsx:213`, `app/not-found.tsx:192`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-106 · POLISH** — Invite referral page — desktop layout (http://localhost:3000/invite)
- **What:** At 1440 the hero is a narrow centered column floating in a very wide pattern band, and five install affordances stack in one viewport: nav CTA button, hero button, two store badges, and the QR — all triggering the same action.
- **Why it matters:** Desktop referral pages at benchmark products use the width (copy left, device/QR right) instead of a mobile column blown up; the redundant CTA pile dilutes the primary action's weight.
- **Fix:** At ≥1120px split .invite-hero .nk-hero-band__inner into two columns (CSS grid in globals.css, reusing --nk-gap-* tokens and the home hero's intro/media split pattern): left = eyebrow/h1/lead + primary button with badges; right = QR card with its hint and the future reward/code slot. This both uses the width and de-stacks the redundant install affordances (nav CTA + hero button + 2 badges + QR all in the first viewport at 1440, confirmed in the shot).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/invite-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/invite-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/InviteScreen.tsx:80-91`, `app/globals.css:1557-1568`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-148 · POLISH** — 404 (localized) + feed empty state (/<unmatched-path> and /skelbimai?q=…)
- **What:** The localized 404 reuses the exact same magnifier illustration (with a refresh-arrows glyph inside the lens) as the feed's no-search-results state, even though the illustration registry has five distinct states (search/listings/filter/error/offline).
- **Why it matters:** Distinct states deserve distinct visual anchors — a "searching" magnifier on a page-not-found slightly misframes the situation (nothing was searched), and the refresh glyph inside the lens hints at "retry", which isn't the 404 recovery model. Minor, but the registry already supports differentiation.
- **Fix:** Extend IllusName with a dedicated "notFound" entry in NK_ILLUS (app/components/ui.tsx:137-156) drawn in the same 200x200 duotone language (#6665E0 backdrop, #F9F367 outline, floating dots/sparkles — e.g. a map-pin-off or compass motif; colors stay literal hex per the existing SVG-presentation-attribute constraint) and use it in app/[lang]/not-found.tsx:15. Consider also switching ListingScreen.tsx:74's gone-listing state off "search" (it's a 'gone', not a search miss). No dictionary changes needed.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `e2e/__screens__/notfound-0390.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-empty-vp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/ui.tsx:137-156`, `app/[lang]/not-found.tsx:15`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:283`, `app/components/ListingScreen.tsx:74`


### SEO landings (/nuoma, /miestai) (7)

**F-025 · HIGH** — Category SEO landing (/nuoma/[category]) (/nuoma/foto-video (also /en/nuoma/foto-video, /nuoma/sveikata-medicinine-iranga))
- **What:** The visible on-page H1 renders the meta-title-style brand suffix: "Foto ir video technikos nuoma | Naudokis", "Medicininės įrangos nuoma | Naudokis", EN "Photo & Video Gear Rental | Naudokis". At every width the line wraps so a dangling "|" pipe hangs at the end of line 1. City and category+city landings render clean H1s ("Foto ir video technikos nuoma Vilniuje", "Nuomojami daiktai Kaune"), making the category pages inconsistent with their siblings.
- **Why it matters:** These are Google entry pages — a "| Brand" pipe inside an H1 is a classic machine-generated-content tell that no 2026 marketplace (Airbnb category hubs, Turo city pages) exhibits; it damages first-impression trust exactly where SEO traffic lands. A prior audit fixed the H1 brand-suffix leak on the layout metaTitle; this is a distinct surface — FeedScreen renders the backend-authored `seoTitle` (seo_title_lt/en, which is authored WITH the suffix per the code comment in listing-landing-page.tsx:72-74) directly as the H1.
- **Fix:** Sanitize at the data layer so every consumer is covered: in toCategory (app/lib/categories.ts:71) map seoTitle through a brand-suffix strip, e.g. `const stripBrand = (s?: string) => s?.replace(/\s*\|\s*Naudokis(\.lt)?\s*$/i, "").trim(); seoTitle: stripBrand(en ? c.seo_title_en : c.seo_title_lt) || title`. This fixes both the visible H1 (FeedScreen.tsx:196) and the CollectionPage JSON-LD name (listing-landing-page.tsx:129) in one place while leaving metaTitle untouched for <head>. Optionally ask the backend team to de-suffix seo_title_* content, but keep the frontend safeguard regardless. No dictionary change needed.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-cat-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-cat-vp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-filtered-vp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:196`, `app/lib/categories.ts:71`, `app/lib/listing-landing-page.tsx:128-130`; seen independently by 4 reviewers

**F-028 · MEDIUM** — Category landing intro block, mobile (/nuoma/foto-video (also /nuoma/sveikata-medicinine-iranga))
- **What:** At 390 the authored category intro runs ~13 lines of body text between the H1 and the search box, pushing search, filters and the results area (the page's actual product) far below the first screen. The page then repeats a second authored SEO paragraph below the grid ("Foto ir video technikos nuoma Lietuvoje" block), so long-form copy exists twice on one page.
- **Why it matters:** 2026 marketplace SEO landers (Airbnb category hubs, Getaround city pages) clamp the intro to 2–3 lines above the fold — the long-form copy belongs below the inventory, which this page already provides. On a phone, a wall of text before any interactive element depresses engagement from the exact traffic these pages are built to convert.
- **Fix:** Give the subtitle <p> at FeedScreen.tsx:311 a class (e.g. nk-feed-intro) and add to globals.css: at ≤560px, `display:-webkit-box; -webkit-line-clamp:3; -webkit-box-orient:vertical; overflow:hidden` applied only when the landing intro is long (e.g. modifier class set when `isLanding && subtitle.length > 200`), plus a dictionary-labelled toggle button (Dict: feed.introMore/introLess — LT 'Rodyti daugiau'/'Rodyti mažiau', EN 'Show more'/'Show less') with aria-expanded that removes the clamp. Full text stays SSR'd in the DOM for crawlers; desktop unchanged.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-cat-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-filtered-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-cat-vp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:199`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:309-312`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:441-444`, `app/lib/categories.ts:72`; seen independently by 3 reviewers

**F-049 · MEDIUM** — City SEO landing (Kaunas) — related-links chips (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai?city=Kaunas)
- **What:** The internal-linking chip row under 'Daiktų nuoma Kaune' truncates labels mid-word with an ellipsis: 'Garsas, muzika ir renginių tec…' and 'Elektronika ir technologijos · …' — the second one cuts exactly after the '·' separator, leaving a dangling '· …' that reads broken. Sibling chips show the full '· Kaunas' suffix, so the row is internally inconsistent.
- **Why it matters:** These chips are crawlable internal links and the page's main navigation payload; Fat Llama/Hygglo category-city link blocks wrap to full labels. A chip ending in '· …' looks like a rendering bug to any design-literate user.
- **Fix:** Scope the ellipsis cap to removable filter chips only. Keep `.nk-fchip span{max-width:220px}` for dismissible chips (it guards long free-text “q” chips at 390), and add `.nk-fchip--link span{max-width:none;white-space:normal}` in globals.css so the crawlable related-landing labels always render whole — the row already flex-wraps (FeedScreen.tsx:524), and at 390 a long label wraps inside the pill instead of truncating. No new tokens needed.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/land-catcity-foto-vilnius-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-catcity-foto-vilnius-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-city-kaunas-0390.png`; code: `app/globals.css:1032`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:508`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:524-533`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-051 · MEDIUM** — Empty-state copy on city landings (/miestai/kaunas (also /nuoma/foto-video/vilnius))
- **What:** The empty title frames an SEO landing as a filtered search: "Pagal šiuos filtrus mieste „Kaunas“ nuomos pasiūlymų neradome" — but a visitor arriving from Google set no filters. The subtitle advises "…arba išjunkite pristatymą" (turn off delivery) while the delivery toggle is visibly OFF in the same screenshot. And "mieste „Kaunas“" (nominative-in-quotes) is mechanical Lithuanian — the H1 two sections above declines correctly ("Nuomojami daiktai Kaune"), so the page mixes natural and robotic grammar for the same city.
- **Why it matters:** LT is the canonical locale and this is launch-critical copy on the most common landing state (empty city). Best-in-class empty states (Airbnb "No exact matches", Turo) describe the actual situation and only suggest actions that apply; advising users to disable a filter that is already off reads as broken logic.
- **Fix:** Make the empty copy reason-aware in the Dict: (1) for the landing state (no user-set filters) use a new city title built with the existing cityLocativeLt helper — lt 'Kaune kol kas nuomos pasiūlymų nėra' / en 'No listings in Kaunas yet' — and switch filterTitleCity itself to the locative ('…pasiūlymų Kaune neradome'), dropping the mechanical „Kaunas“ quotes; (2) change filterBody to a function of the active filters (e.g. `filterBody(delivery: boolean)`) and only append 'arba išjunkite pristatymą' when params.delivery is true. Update types.ts and both dictionaries; pairs naturally with the F-050 branch.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/land-city-kaunas-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-city-kaunas-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-catcity-foto-vilnius-1440.png`; code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:617-620`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:295-297`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:546`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:547-549`

**F-053 · POLISH** — Health category landing naming (/nuoma/sveikata-medicinine-iranga)
- **What:** Three different names for the same category on one page: H1 "Medicininės įrangos nuoma" (drops the "sveikata" half), lower SEO heading "Sveikatos ir medicininės įrangos nuoma Lietuvoje", breadcrumb/filter chip "Sveikata ir medicininė įranga".
- **Why it matters:** Keyword-variant authoring is fine for meta tags, but three visible on-page variants read as sloppy taxonomy; benchmark category hubs keep one display name and vary only the meta title.
- **Fix:** Backend content task: align seo_title_lt/en for health_medical to the visible taxonomy name — e.g. 'Sveikatos ir medicininės įrangos nuoma' — so H1, SEO heading and chip agree, and remove the '| Naudokis' suffix from all seo_title_* values (they render in the on-page H1 via FeedScreen.tsx:196; branding belongs only in meta_title_*). As a cheap frontend guard, strip a trailing '| Naudokis…' segment from seoTitle in toCategory() before it reaches the H1 — a safe transform, no fabricated copy.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/land-cat-sveikata-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-cat-sveikata-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:196`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:204`, `app/lib/categories.ts:71`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:19`

**F-056 · POLISH** — Category empty-state illustration (/nuoma/foto-video (also /nuoma/sveikata-medicinine-iranga))
- **What:** The empty-category illustration is the same generic listing-card glyph on every category — Photo & Video and Health & Medical show pixel-identical icons — even though each category has its own icon used elsewhere (tiles, placeholders).
- **Why it matters:** A category-specific glyph (camera for foto, cross/heart for sveikata) would make the ~10 programmatic empty pages feel authored rather than templated; the site already maintains a category-icon mapping (categoryIconFor), so the asset exists.
- **Fix:** Add an optional icon override to the illustration path: give Illustration (ui.tsx) an `icon?: IconName` prop that swaps the card glyph inside the 'listings' disk for the supplied lucide icon (rendered via the existing Icon wrapper so currentColor/token colors flow), thread it through EmptyState, and in FeedScreen's empty-category branch pass `categoryIconFor(cats, params.cat)` — camera for photo_video, the health glyph for health_medical — falling back to the generic card glyph when unresolved. Reuses the existing icon registry; no new assets or tokens.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/land-cat-foto-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-cat-sveikata-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:20`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:289`, `app/components/ui.tsx:137-139`, `app/components/cards.tsx:299-305`

**F-057 · POLISH** — Landing header zone, desktop (/nuoma/foto-video (all landings))
- **What:** At 1440 the H1 + intro occupy only the left ~55% of the content width with the entire right half empty; combined with the centered empty-state card below, the page reads as sparse dark space with no visual anchor on desktop.
- **Why it matters:** Turo/Getaround city landers use the header's right zone for a supporting visual, stat strip or app-CTA card, which matters more here because the empty-supply state removes all imagery from the page.
- **Fix:** On landing routes only (the isCat/isCity landing variants in FeedScreen), at >=1120px wrap the heading block (FeedScreen.tsx:309-312) in a two-column flex and add a compact right-aligned app-bridge card reusing the existing AppBadges + QR primitives from ui.tsx (real store links/QR only — no invented stats), copy added to the Dict in both lt.ts and en.ts. Keep the 65ch measure on the intro. This also softens the zero-supply state without touching the (good) empty-state card.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/land-cat-foto-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-cat-sveikata-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-city-kaunas-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:306-312`


### Categories (6)

**F-040 · MEDIUM** — Categories page — end of page (http://localhost:3000/kategorijos)
- **What:** The page ends with a plain SEO paragraph ("Daiktų nuoma pagal kategorijas") and then the footer — there is no install CTA or next-step module after the grid, at any width.
- **Why it matters:** This is a bridge site whose only KPI is app installs, yet the categories hub — a core discovery surface — peters out into SEO copy. The homepage ends with a CtaBanner; Airbnb/Turo category hubs always close with a conversion module. A user who scrolls the full grid without picking a tile gets no offer at the exit point.
- **Fix:** Render the existing <CtaBanner locale={locale} /> (sections-home.tsx:107 — shared, directive-free, takes locale, resolves its own dictionary copy) between the SEO section and <Footer /> in CategoriesScreen (after CategoriesScreen.tsx:92). No new copy, tokens, or components needed; both locales get it automatically. Keep the SEO paragraph above the banner so the page still ends on a conversion module like the homepage does.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/cats-fp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/cats-fp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/CategoriesScreen.tsx:87`, `app/components/CategoriesScreen.tsx:94`, `app/components/sections-home.tsx:107`, `app/[lang]/page.tsx:47`

**R2-013 · MEDIUM** — Categories page — live search filter (http://localhost:3000/kategorijos)
- **What:** The category filter matches with a raw `c.title.toLowerCase().includes(term)` — no diacritic folding and title-only matching. Typing "irankiai" (no į), "sventes" (no š/ė) or "iranga" returns the 'Kategorijų nerasta' empty state even though 'Įrankiai ir statyba', 'Renginiai ir šventės' and 'Sveikata ir medicininė įranga' are visibly on the page; synonyms that the authored intros use (e.g. 'dronus', 'fotoaparatus') also never match because only the title string is searched.
- **Why it matters:** Lithuanian users very commonly type without diacritics (EN keyboard layouts, fast mobile typing). Airbnb, Booking.com and Vinted search are accent-insensitive as table stakes; a zero-result state on a 12-item list the user can literally see below the input reads as broken and needlessly diverts them into the cross-feed search escape hatch.
- **Fix:** In CategoriesScreen.tsx add a fold helper and apply it to both sides of the comparison: const fold = (s: string) => s.toLowerCase().normalize("NFD").replace(/\p{Diacritic}/gu, ""); then const term = fold(q.trim()); const list = all.filter((c) => fold(c.title).includes(term)). Optionally also match fold(c.seoBody) so authored intro synonyms ('dronus', 'fotoaparatus') hit — but the diacritic fold on titles is the essential fix. No dictionary or backend changes needed; verified working against live category data.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/cats-vp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/cats-vp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/CategoriesScreen.tsx:29-31`

**R2-016 · MEDIUM** — Categories page — zero-data edge state (http://localhost:3000/kategorijos)
- **What:** If the backend legitimately returns an empty category list (online, no error), the code falls into the search-empty branch with the untyped query interpolated: LT subtitle renders 'Pagal „“ kategorijų neradome. Pabandykite platesnę paiešką.' with empty quotes, the primary CTA label renders with empty quotes too, and its handler (`searchItems`) is guarded by `if (q.trim())` so the primary button is a visible no-op.
- **Why it matters:** Empty-string interpolation plus a dead primary CTA is the kind of edge-state sloppiness 2026 products guard against — the state misdiagnoses a data/availability problem as a failed user search the user never performed (same framing flaw class as round-1 F-051, but a distinct, unreported code path on a different surface).
- **Fix:** Two-part fix. (1) In CategoriesScreen.tsx branch on the query before the search-empty state: if all.length === 0 && !q.trim(), render a data-availability EmptyState with a Retry action wired to refetch() — reuse the existing dict.categories.errorTitle/errorSubtitle/errorAction trio, or add a dedicated categoriesPage.unavailable* key to the Dict contract (types.ts) and both lt.ts/en.ts. (2) Stop masking server failures: in app/[lang]/kategorijos/page.tsx catch to null instead of [] and only setQueryData when the fetch succeeded, so a failed ISR-time fetch leaves the cache empty and the client query fetches fresh (skeleton → data or the real error state) rather than hydrating a fake-successful empty list.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/CategoriesScreen.tsx:28`, `app/components/CategoriesScreen.tsx:69-84`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:513-516`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:528`

**F-044 · POLISH** — Categories result count (desktop) (http://localhost:3000/kategorijos vs /en/kategorijos)
- **What:** The result count line differs in construction across locales: LT 'Rasta 12 kategorijų' (verb-led, reads as a search result) vs EN '12 categories' (bare count).
- **Why it matters:** Minor asymmetry in voice between locales on the same element; parity of tone is part of making EN feel first-class rather than independently authored.
- **Fix:** Align the construction in both dictionaries' categoriesPage.foundCount. Prefer the bare count in both (LT: `${n} ${word}` dropping 'Rasta', keeping the existing LT pluralization branches) since the line renders on initial page load, where a verb-led 'found' reads as a search result before any query; alternatively make EN verb-led ('Found N categories') if the search-result voice is preferred. One-line change per dictionary, no type change.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/cats-vp-en-0390.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/cats-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/cats-vp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:517-527`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:470`, `app/components/CategoriesScreen.tsx:57`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**R2-015 · POLISH** — Categories page — loading skeleton (http://localhost:3000/kategorijos)
- **What:** The loading state renders exactly 8 `CategoryCardSkeleton`s but the live backend always returns 12 categories, so on load the grid grows by a full row (2 rows → 3 at 4-up desktop; 4 rows → 6 in the 2-up mobile grid), pushing the SEO section and footer down after data arrives.
- **Why it matters:** Skeletons exist to reserve layout; a systematically wrong count guarantees a layout shift on every cold load. Marketplace-class skeletons (Airbnb, Booking) match the expected result geometry — here the count is stable and known, so the mismatch is a free fix.
- **Fix:** Change the skeleton count from 8 to 12 at CategoriesScreen.tsx:67, hoisting a CATEGORY_SKELETON_COUNT = 12 constant (ideally exported next to the data layer in app/lib/categories.ts with a comment tying it to the 4/3/2/2 grid note in globals.css) so the skeleton grid reserves the same row count as the real data at every breakpoint.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/CategoriesScreen.tsx:67`, `app/globals.css:992-994`, `app/[lang]/kategorijos/page.tsx:33-35`

**R2-017 · POLISH** — Categories page — tile imagery (http://localhost:3000/kategorijos)
- **What:** All 12 tiles are flat token-gradient panels with a single Lucide line glyph in a disk — the `.nk-cat__img` layer exists but only paints a gradient; there is no photographic or illustrative representation of any category's actual inventory anywhere on the hub.
- **Why it matters:** 2026 rental hubs (Fat Llama/Hygglo category cards, Airbnb's category system, Turo's browse tiles) use product photography or rich illustration to make categories feel stocked and desirable; an all-glyph grid reads clean but abstract, and does nothing to counter the pre-launch 'is anything actually here?' doubt that the missing counts (known F-041) already create. Distinct from F-041 (counts) — this is about the imagery itself.
- **Fix:** Content/asset-dependency, pair with the tracked real-photography work (known-open): when per-category brand photography or commissioned illustration exists, render it inside the existing .nk-cat__img layer (e.g. a next/image fill child under the gradient, with the current --cat-accent gradient retained as overlay/fallback so the per-category accent identity and the no-asset fallback both survive). Do not source or fabricate imagery of inventory that doesn't exist; until assets land, the glyph system stays.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/cats-fp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/cats-vp-en-1440.png`; code: `app/globals.css:718-722`, `app/components/cards.tsx:122`


### Listing detail (21)

**F-058 · BLOCKING** — Listing detail — mobile gallery + inline booking facts (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id] (Dodge RAM 2016))
- **What:** At 390px the single-photo gallery paints over the top of the inline booking-facts card: the card's price header row (50 € / para) is completely hidden behind the photo and the ascenders of 'Pasirinkti datas' are clipped by the photo's bottom edge. Root cause: at ≤560px `.nk-bento` uses `grid-auto-rows:116px` while `.nk-bento > :first-child` is forced to `height:230px` — the grid container's layout height is 116px, so the oversized hero tile (position:relative, paints above the later in-flow card) overflows ~114px onto `.nk-booking-inline` (margin-top:24px is swallowed). The same row/tile height mismatch exists in the ≤980 block (rows clamp(150px,22vw,190px) vs tile clamp(260px,34vw,320px)), so 561–980px single-photo (and count=0 placeholder) listings are likely affected too.
- **Why it matters:** This is the mobile renter's first pricing touchpoint after the photo — the price row is invisible and the first interactive row is visibly cut. It reads as a broken page at the exact moment Turo/Airbnb show a crisp photo→price→facts sequence; a layout that eats its own price line destroys trust on the core conversion path.
- **Fix:** In the <=980 media block change .nk-bento's grid-template-rows:none to grid-template-rows:auto (globals.css:1183) so row 1 sizes to the hero tile's explicit height; keep grid-auto-rows for the thumbnail rows and keep the height on > :first-child. The <=560 block inherits the auto template row, so no data-count-specific rules are needed. This fixes both the count<=1 booking-card overlap AND the count>=2 hidden hero bottom. Verify at 390 and 768 with the Dodge (count=1) and Macbook (count=5) listings; no token changes.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-vp-lt-0320.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-vp-lt-0430.png`; code: `app/globals.css:1183-1184`, `app/globals.css:1195-1196`, `app/components/ListingScreen.tsx:124-132`; seen independently by 4 reviewers

**F-059 · BLOCKING** — Listing detail — booking facts total row (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id] (Dodge RAM 2016))
- **What:** The 'Galutinė suma' row's value 'Apskaičiuojama programėlėje' overflows the booking card horizontally at 390px and is clipped at the right viewport edge — it renders as 'Apskaičiuojama programėl' with no ellipsis, running past the card's right padding to x=390. Cause: both label and value spans are `whiteSpace:"nowrap"` (ListingDetail.tsx:801); the bold 17px LT strings ('Galutinė suma' + 'Apskaičiuojama programėlėje') exceed the ~310px inner card width, and a nowrap flex row cannot shrink.
- **Why it matters:** The total-price line — the single most trust-sensitive row in any marketplace price breakdown — is unreadable/truncated on the most common phone width. Airbnb/Turo price breakdowns never clip; a cut-off 'final total…' invites the exact suspicion the transparent-fees design was built to prevent.
- **Fix:** At ListingDetail.tsx:801 remove whiteSpace:'nowrap' from the value span and give it textAlign:'right' plus minWidth:0 (keep nowrap on the 'Galutinė suma' label) so the value wraps to two lines at narrow widths. No dictionary change strictly needed; optionally also shorten the LT value (e.g. 'Skaičiuojama programėlėje') via the Dict in both locales if a single line is preferred at 390.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-vp-lt-0320.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-vp-lt-0430.png`; code: `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:800-802`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:448-449`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:409-410`; seen independently by 5 reviewers

**F-065 · HIGH** — listing-detail (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])
- **What:** In the booking card at 1440 the fee label 'Platformos mokesčiai' wraps onto two lines while its value 'Rodoma programėlėje' top-aligns with the first line; the deposit row below is single-line, producing ragged row rhythm in the fee block (verified in full-res crop).
- **Why it matters:** Price-breakdown rows on Airbnb/Booking keep one line per fact; a wrapping label with a floating value makes the most scanned block of the page look cramped.
- **Fix:** Upgraded from polish: this is not just ragged rhythm — the total row genuinely overflows the card border at 1440. In BookingPanel (app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:793-802): (1) drop whiteSpace:nowrap from the long i18n value spans and give them textAlign:'right' + minWidth:0 so they wrap instead of bleeding; (2) set alignItems:'baseline' (or 'flex-start') on the fee/total rows so a wrapped label no longer stretch-aligns its value; (3) shorten the LT values in app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:447-448 (serviceFeeFree/inAppValue → e.g. 'Programėlėje', keeping the shared serviceFeeHint footnote as the explainer) and mirror in en.ts:408-409 — which also fits the F-072 consolidation.

**F-068 · HIGH** — listing-detail (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])
- **What:** At 1280 and 1440 the single-photo hero renders full container width at a tall aspect and consumes essentially the entire first viewport: the booking card's '50 €' price is cut in half exactly at the fold (~888px of a 900px viewport) and the date CTA / Rezervuoti button are fully below it. At 1024 the price is barely visible bottom-right but the whole booking flow is still below the image. Same on EN (vp-en-1440: '€50' clipped at the bottom edge).
- **Why it matters:** Price and primary CTA above the fold is table-stakes for 2026 marketplaces — Airbnb caps its photo mosaic to roughly half the viewport height and Turo keeps the sticky price card visible immediately; here a renter must scroll past one giant photo before seeing any price or action, which taxes both conversion and price-trust.
- **Fix:** Make the gallery height viewport-aware so the booking price row clears a 900px fold at ≥1280: change .nk-bento height (globals.css:1067) to clamp(380px, min(46vw, calc(100dvh - 470px)), 512px) (yielding ~430px at a 900px-tall window, unchanged on tall screens), and/or tighten the pre-gallery block (H1 clamp max 50px→~44px, .nk-detail-grid margin-top 40→28 via an --nk-gap token). Re-measure priceTop < 860 at 1280/1440 after the change; keep the ≤980px mobile mosaic untouched.

**R2-022 · HIGH** — Listing detail — similar-items rail (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id] (Dodge RAM 2016))
- **What:** The 'Panašūs daiktai' cross-sell rail exists in code but never renders with live data: the page ends Atsiliepimai → footer at 1440 and 390 even though a same-category sibling (Toyota Prius Plus 2017, Transportas) is live. Root cause API-verified: SimilarRail queries useListings(locale, { q: category }) where category = listing.tags[0] — the localized display name sent as free-text q. Live check: GET /listings?q=Transportas returns 0 items on both dev and prod, while GET /listings?category_id=transportas returns the 2 Transportas vehicles on dev. The rail's own <2-siblings hide rule then suppresses it permanently, so the detail page is a dead end at every inventory size unless a title happens to contain the category word.
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb ('Similar listings'), Turo ('Similar vehicles'), Fat Llama ('More like this') and Booking.com all treat the detail page as their highest-leverage re-engagement surface — a user who bounces off one item is recirculated, not dropped to the footer. This site built exactly that module and it silently never fires, so the benchmark feature is invisible in production. The code comment even calls it 'the detail page's highest-leverage re-engagement surface'.
- **Fix:** Query by id, not display name: add the top-level category id (wire category_path[0], e.g. 'transport') to the ListingDetail view model in app/lib/listings.ts, and change SimilarRail to useListings(locale, { category: categoryId }) — listings.ts:295 already translates that to category_id. Then relax the items.length<2 gate for launch inventory: note that even fixed, today's dev data yields exactly 1 sibling (Toyota) for the Dodge page, so allow a single sibling under a broader honest heading (new Dict keys, e.g. LT 'Daugiau daiktų nuomai' / EN 'More items to rent', both dictionaries) rather than rendering nothing. Keep the no-category guard and the currentId exclusion.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-fp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-fp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/ListingScreen.tsx:88`, `app/components/ListingScreen.tsx:162`, `app/components/ListingScreen.tsx:165`, `app/lib/listings.ts:295`

**F-061 · MEDIUM** — Listing detail — description section (mobile) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/{id} (Dodge RAM 2016))
- **What:** The owner's description renders as one unclamped ~25-line block at 390px (roughly two full screens of text) with no "Show more" expander, pushing Specifications, handover, terms, reviews and the host card far down the page.

Render the toggle only when the text actually overflows (compare scrollHeight vs clientHeight) so short descriptions get no dead control; expand in place.

**F-066 · MEDIUM** — listing-detail (cancellation policy) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id] (Dodge RAM 2016))
- **What:** The cancellation policy tier 'Griežta' appears twice (rental-terms tile 'Griežta / Atšaukimo politika' and inside the green callout as 'Griežtos atšaukimo sąlygos') but is never defined — no refund percentages, deadlines, tooltip or link. Additionally, the strict-cancellation line sits INSIDE the green 'Apsaugoti mokėjimai' reassurance callout with a friendly refresh icon, styling a restrictive term as if it were a protection benefit.

**F-069 · MEDIUM** — listing-detail (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])
- **What:** The 'Daikto perdavimas' subtitle always reads 'Atsiimkite nemokamai arba susitarkite dėl pristatymo …' (pick up for free or arrange delivery), but this listing is delivery-only: the code hides the free-pickup row (showPickup=false, ListingDetail.tsx:610) and the screenshot shows only the 'Pristatymas / Iki 40 km' row — no pickup row, no 'Nemokamai' pill. **F-108 · MEDIUM** — Listing detail — invalid-ID / gone state (mobile) (/skelbimai/<nonexistent-id>)
- **What:** The captured 404-listing page shows ONLY skeleton, top to bottom: ~9,500px of placeholder blocks (breadcrumb, title, chips, gallery, 2×2 thumbs, booking card, spec rows, owner card, further cards, map grid) and the resolved gone/404 content never appears in the capture. The skeleton stack also promises sections that frequently never materialize with real data (map without an API key, reviews at zero-review inventory).
- **Why it matters:** Part of this may be capture timing (code at ListingScreen.tsx:67-76 does have a goneTitle/goneBody soft-404 and server deletions hard-404), but the visible experience stands on its own: a user opening a dead deep link scrolls through multiple viewports of fake content before any truth arrives, and an over-long skeleton inflates perceived wait. Airbnb's skeletons cover roughly one viewport and resolve into content or an error promptly.
- **Fix:** Re-scoped after live verification. The genuine defect: the backend answers 400 'Invalid UUID format' (not 404) for malformed listing IDs, so fetchListingDetailRaw (listings.ts:414-421) throws a generic Error — the server page treats it as transient and streams the client shell (HTTP 200), the client burns 2 retries (~3-6s of the full-page skeleton the screenshots caught) and then lands on a permanently-failing 'try again' error whose body blames the user's connection. Fix: in fetchListingDetailRaw also map res.status === 400 (invalid-ID-format on this GET) to ListingNotFoundError, so the server path calls notFound() and the client path shows the goneTitle/goneBody browse-others state with zero retries — same handling a well-formed nonexistent UUID already gets (that case correctly resolves to the 404 StatusScreen in <1s, so the finding's 'gone content never appears' claim was a capture-timing artifact of the retry window). Optional secondary polish: shorten ListingSkeleton on mobile (~9,500px of placeholder anatomy at 390px) to roughly one viewport plus continuation, and drop skeleton rows for conditional sections (map, reviews).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-404-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-404-lt-1280.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/state-404-en-0390.png`; code: `app/lib/listings.ts:414-421`, `app/lib/listings.ts:542-551`, `app/components/ListingScreen.tsx:59-86`, `app/[lang]/skelbimai/[id]/page.tsx:86-100`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**R2-026 · MEDIUM** — Listing detail — owner card stats (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id] (Dodge RAM 2016))
- **What:** The owner card advertises '3 Daiktai' (and '0 Atsiliepimai') as plain static text — the stats are not links and there is no owner-profile page or owner-filtered feed view anywhere on the site, so a renter who trusts this owner cannot see their other two items.

Filter by owner_id, not owner name (names are not unique). Heading strings into the Dict contract + both dictionaries; reuse OfferCard + nk tokens. Keep the zero-review stats honest and unlinked until a real owner page exists — do not fake a link target.

**R2-032 · MEDIUM** — Listing detail — specifications table (EN) (http://localhost:3000/en/skelbimai/987468db-ced6-4092-924f-d64bce7ab69d)
- **What:** The EN spec table renders a Lithuanian value in the middle of English rows: "Driver age requirement — 25 metai" (metai = years). Verified on the live dev API the site captures against: the backend sends value_label_en: "25 metai" with unit: "metai" — it composes the raw LT unit into the ENGLISH value label. "300 km" and "1700 l" only pass because those units are language-neutral. The client maps value_label_en verbatim and never reads the wire `unit` field, so it has no guard against un-localized unit-composed values.
- **Why it matters:** A mixed-language spec row on the core conversion surface makes /en read as an unfinished translation. Turo/Getaround vehicle spec sheets are fully localized per locale; a renter checking eligibility (driver age) hits the one row that matters in a language they may not read.
- **Fix:** Primary fix is backend (cross-team): localize the unit when composing value_label_en ('25 years') or ship unit_en/unit_lt — file it alongside the existing listing_count request. Site-side stopgap in fetchListing's attribute mapping (listings.ts:528-535): for locale 'en', when a.unit is set and value_label_en ends with the raw unit token, strip it and re-append a localized unit from a small map for the known LT unit vocabulary (metai→years; extend as units appear), leaving language-neutral units (km, l, kg, m) and unmapped units untouched — never fabricate a value, only re-render the unit word. Keep the map in the data layer per conventions (formatting lives in lib, not components).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-fp-en-0390.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-fp-en-1440.png`; code: `app/lib/listings.ts:528-535 (attribute mapping — value_label_en rendered verbatim)`, `app/lib/listings.ts:32 (ApiAttributeDisplay.unit modelled but never read)`, `wire: GET /listings/987468db-ced6-4092-924f-d64bce7ab69d → driver_age_minimum {unit:'metai', value_label_en:'25 metai'} (reproduced on api-dev)`

**R2-033 · MEDIUM** — Listing detail — Description section (EN) (http://localhost:3000/en/skelbimai/987468db-ced6-4092-924f-d64bce7ab69d)
- **What:** On /en the main Description block is an entire ~15-line Lithuanian paragraph ("Dodge RAM 2016 – stiprus ir patikimas pikapas…") rendered inside otherwise-English chrome, with no label, no "original language" disclosure, and no translation affordance. **F-064 · POLISH** — Listing detail — fixed mobile reserve bar (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/{id} (Dodge RAM 2016))
- **What:** At 320px the bar's disclosure line ellipsizes mid-word: "Datos ir kaina progra…" — the key "prices are set in the app" qualifier is cut.
- **Why it matters:** The disclosure exists to keep the €50/para price honest (dates/fees finalized in-app); truncating it at the narrowest common width weakens that disclosure exactly where space-constrained users see it. Graceful (ellipsis, not clip), but a shorter string would fit.
- **Fix:** Prefer copy over layout: since values-can-be-functions is already supported, keep one Dict key but shorten LT to fit (e.g. 'Kaina — programėlėje' / EN 'Price — in the app') OR allow the subtext two lines at <=360px by scoping a `white-space:normal;-webkit-line-clamp:2` override for .nk-mbar > span span in the existing <=560 mbar block. Either way update both lt.ts and en.ts via the Dict; verify at 320 with the 50 € price and the widest LT price strings.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-vp-lt-0320.png`; code: `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:897-900`, `app/globals.css:1172`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:479`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:442`

**F-067 · POLISH** — listing-detail (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])
- **What:** The owner card shows name, verified chip, items/rating/reviews stats and a contact button, but no tenure or responsiveness signal (member-since date, response time/rate) — the zero-review pre-launch state leaves '3 Daiktai' as the only differentiating fact.

Render response time only when avg_response_time_hours is non-null; omit the line entirely when the field is absent.

**F-073 · POLISH** — listing-detail (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id])

**R2-021 · POLISH** — Listing detail — booking card fee vs deposit row label tones (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/987468db-ced6-4092-924f-d64bce7ab69d)
- **What:** The two adjacent rows of the same price breakdown use different label tones: the 'Platformos mokesčiai' row is set wholesale in --nk-text-2 (85% white, ListingDetail.tsx:793) while the sibling 'Užstatas (grąžinamas)' row's label is --nk-text-muted (70% white, ListingDetail.tsx:796, with only its value promoted to 100%). Result: the fee LABEL is brighter than the deposit LABEL, and the fee VALUE ('Rodoma programėlėje', 85%) is brighter than the deposit label too — the emphasis pattern flips between rows for no semantic reason.
- **Why it matters:** Fintech-grade cost breakdowns (Stripe Checkout, Airbnb's price detail) keep one tone for all row labels and reserve brightness shifts for values only; mixed label tones make the breakdown look unsystematic on close read.
- **Fix:** Unify label tone: set the fee row container (ListingDetail.tsx:793) to color var(--nk-text-muted) like the deposit row, and keep the value span explicitly var(--nk-text-2) ('Rodoma programėlėje'). Result: both labels muted; brightness lives only on values (100% white for the real 500 €, --nk-text-2 for the deferred fee) — preserving the existing 'never reads as waived' intent.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-algirdasjasaitis-naudokis-web/9fb9966e-78df-4d65-8b0d-80b115027573/scratchpad/verify-crops/r3-listing-sidebar-1440.png`; code: `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:793-798`

**R2-029 · POLISH** — Listing detail — safety/reporting affordance (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai/[id] (Dodge RAM 2016))
- **What:** The listing page has no 'report this listing' affordance at any width — trust elements present are the verified-profile chip, escrow note and deposit line, but a visitor who spots a scam, miscategorized or prohibited item has no path to flag it (the footer's generic email is the closest recourse).
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb puts a low-key flag icon + 'Report this listing' link on every detail page and Turo ships 'Report listing' in the listing menu — in 2026 a visible abuse-report path is table-stakes marketplace safety UX, and the site's own legal center defines Prohibited and Restricted Items Rules that a reporting link would operationalize.
- **Fix:** Add a quiet report affordance at the end of the description or rental-terms section in ListingDetail.tsx: a muted text link with a Flag icon (add lucide Flag to the ICONS registry in visual.tsx) — 'Pranešti apie skelbimą' / 'Report this listing' — opening a mailto to CONTACT_EMAIL from contact.ts with a prefilled subject including the listing id and title (encodeURIComponent; e.g. 'Pranešimas apie skelbimą: {title} ({id})'). Style with --nk-text-muted at ~13-14px Sora so it never competes with the reserve CTA. Link + subject-template strings into the Dict contract and both dictionaries. Mailto is the honest zero-infra path; an in-app report form would need backend support (note as possible cross-team follow-up).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-fp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-fp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx (no Flag/report affordance — grep clean)`, `app/lib/contact.ts:4 (CONTACT_EMAIL for the mailto)`, `app/components/visual.tsx (ICONS registry — add lucide Flag)`


### Listings feed (24)

**F-016 · MEDIUM** — Listings feed — header/nav (/skelbimai)
- **What:** Primary nav and the "Atsisiųsti programėlę" install CTA collapse into a hamburger at ≤1120px, so at 1024 (iPad landscape / small laptop) the header shows only logo + burger despite abundant horizontal space; at 1280 the full nav with the purple install button appears.
- **Why it matters:** The install CTA is this bridge site's single conversion goal, and it is hidden behind a menu on an entire device class. Airbnb, Turo and Booking keep full header nav and the primary CTA visible at 1024; a burger-only header at that width reads as mobile leftovers.
- **Fix:** The install CTA (sections.tsx:180-197) currently lives INSIDE <nav className="nk-nav-links">, so it dies with the links at the ≤1120px collapse (globals.css:532-534). Move it out to a sibling slot before the burger and keep it visible in the 700-1120px band (hide below ~700px, where the drawer CTA at sections.tsx:261-277 and hero badges cover conversion). Secondarily, test lowering the links-collapse breakpoint toward ~980px — the gap already clamps to 18px (globals.css:521) but must be verified against the longer EN labels before shipping.

**F-027 · MEDIUM** — Feed — search results active-filter chip (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai?q=Sony)
- **What:** The active search chip renders English curly quotes — “Sony” — while every other LT string on the same screen uses correct Lithuanian quotes: subhead 'Rezultatai pagal „Sony“…' and empty-state 'Pagal „Sony“ nuomos pasiūlymų neradome'. The quote characters are hardcoded in the component (FeedScreen.tsx:244: `label: \`“${params.q}”\``), bypassing the dictionary and locale.
- **Why it matters:** LT is the canonical locale; mixed quotation conventions in one viewport is the kind of typographic slip a design-literate Lithuanian user notices immediately, and it breaks the project's own no-hardcoded-copy rule.
- **Fix:** Add a quote-formatting function to the Dict feed section (app/lib/i18n/types.ts): `chipQuery: (q: string) => string`, with LT `(q) => `„${q}“`` and EN `(q) => `“${q}”``, then use it at FeedScreen.tsx:244: `activeChips.push({ key: "q", label: t.chipQuery(params.q) })`. Compile-time Dict contract forces both locales; keeps the no-hardcoded-copy rule intact. Note the chip row is mobile-only (.nk-fchips hidden ≥561), which bounds the blast radius but the canonical-locale typography slip is real.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-search-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-empty-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-empty-vp-lt-0320.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:244`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:577`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:612`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:517`; seen independently by 3 reviewers

**F-034 · MEDIUM** — Listings feed — browse grid (/skelbimai)
- **What:** On common 900px-tall desktop viewports (1280/1440) the card price bar ("50 € / para") falls entirely below the fold: breadcrumb + 64px H1 + subhead + search bar + filter row consume ~660px before the grid, and the fold cuts cards at the title/badge line. In the full-page shot the price row sits ~940px down. At 768 the same header block pushes even further.
- **Why it matters:** Price is the primary scan signal on a rental feed; Airbnb and Booking compress the results-page header so the first row of cards with prices is visible on the first screen. Here a visitor must scroll before seeing any price, on the site's core browse surface.
- **Fix:** Tighten the feed header stack so the first price row clears a 900px-tall viewport: (1) drop the H1 block's marginBottom 32 (FeedScreen.tsx:309) to var(--nk-gap-lg); (2) reduce the filterbar's internal column gap 16 (FeedScreen.tsx:316) to var(--nk-gap-sm); (3) render the feed H1 at the .nk-h-section scale (clamp(30px,3.4vw,40px)) instead of .nk-h-page's 52px — the feed is a utility surface, not a marketing page; (4) shipping the F-035 LT badge fix reclaims a further ~33px of card height on the canonical locale. Together this moves the LT price bar (~900px) above an ~820px effective fold. Use existing --nk-gap-* rhythm tokens, no new px values.

**F-109 · MEDIUM** — Listings feed — error copy (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai?q=canon)
- **What:** The error body "Nuomos pasiūlymų šiuo metu nepavyko parodyti. Patikrinkite ryšį ir bandykite dar kartą." attributes every failure to the user's connection, including server-side 5xx errors (this capture is a forced API error, not a network loss — and a separate dedicated offline state already exists).
- **Why it matters:** Telling a user on perfectly good wifi to "check your connection" erodes credibility; 2026 patterns (Stripe, Airbnb) use neutral phrasing ("Something went wrong on our side — try again") when the failure isn't client-attributable, especially since this app distinguishes offline vs error states in code.
- **Fix:** Soften the three error-state bodies in both dictionaries to neutral, non-attributing copy (e.g. LT 'Šiuo metu nepavyko įkelti. Bandykite dar kartą.' / EN 'We couldn't load this right now — please try again.'): categories.errorBody (lt.ts:77/en.ts:49), offers.errorBody (lt.ts:95/en.ts:67) and detail.loadErrorBody (lt.ts:424/en.ts:385). Keep connection wording exclusively in dict.offline.* — the site already detects offline separately (useOnlineStatus in FeedScreen/CategoriesScreen), so the current copy is internally inconsistent: by the time this state shows, retries have failed while the browser reports online, i.e. usually a server-side failure. Upgraded polish→medium: factually-misattributing copy on three surfaces × two locales, and it also fronts the F-108 dead-end state.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/feed-error-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/feed-error-0390.png`; code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:77`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:95`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:424`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:49`

**F-144 · MEDIUM** — Sitewide desktop header (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** The desktop header has no search affordance at any scroll position — once the hero search bar scrolls under the nav (visible in the scrolled capture), the chrome offers only section links, the locale picker and the install CTA; a search entry point exists only in the mobile drawer (sections.tsx:221).
- **Why it matters:** Persistent chrome-level search is table stakes for 2026 marketplaces: Airbnb collapses its search into the sticky header on scroll, Booking.com keeps the search box pinned. On this site a home visitor who scrolls past the hero must scroll all the way back up (or know to open /skelbimai) to search live inventory.

Showing it always is simpler and harmless; at minimum show it in the .nk-scrolled state. Hide it ≤1120px where the drawer already provides search.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/nav-scrolled-1440.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-vp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/components/sections.tsx:154-198`, `app/components/sections.tsx:221-224`, `app/components/sections.tsx:127-141`

**R2-003 · MEDIUM** — Listings feed — header state logic (mobile + all widths) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai?q=Sony&city=Vilnius)
- **What:** When a search query is combined with a city or category filter (reachable via the normal UI: pick a city/category in the Filters sheet, then type a query), the header copy drops the query entirely. In FeedScreen.tsx:194-199 the city branch wins unconditionally: with q=Sony&city=Vilnius the H1 becomes 'Nuomojami daiktai Vilniuje' and the subtitle becomes landingDescription's 'Naršykite daiktų nuomos pasiūlymus Vilniuje: įrankius, transportą…' — while the grid is actually filtered by 'Sony'. Meanwhile isSearch (line 193, `!!params.q && !isCat`) is still true, so the breadcrumb leaf claims 'Paieškos rezultatai' — a breadcrumb/H1 contradiction on one screen. With q+category, the H1 becomes the category seoTitle and the only trace of the active query is the small removable chip.
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb and Booking.com always restate the active query in the results header ('Vilnius · "Sony"'); a header that describes a different result set than the one shown misleads users about why they see 0/N results and makes the honest 'Rezultatai pagal „X“' framing (which exists for the plain-search state) silently disappear. The subtitle even promises browsing 'įrankius, transportą, foto techniką…' over a query-filtered grid.
- **Fix:** In FeedScreen's heading/subtitle selection let an active q take precedence: when params.q is set, use t.titleSearch + t.subtitleSearch(params.q) regardless of city/cat (optionally add city-scoped search variants like subtitleSearchCity(q, city) to the Dict in both locales for 'Rezultatai pagal „X“ Vilniuje'). Drive the breadcrumb leaf and the H1 from the same predicate so they can never contradict. Also gate the landing SEO block (isLanding at :203-205) off when params.q is active so authored landing copy doesn't render under a query-filtered grid.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:193-199`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:209-222`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:131-132`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:545-559`

**R2-004 · MEDIUM** — Listings feed — mobile filter entry (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** On phones (≤560px) every filter dimension — category, city, delivery, sort — is hidden behind a single generic 'Filtrai' pill; nothing on the feed surface shows that categories exist or which ones have inventory. The visible pre-results chrome is only the search field and the lone pill (feed-vp-lt-0320/0390/0430).
- **Why it matters:** 2026 marketplace feeds surface category discovery directly: Airbnb's horizontally scrollable category rail, Fat Llama/Hygglo's category chips above results, Turo's vehicle-type row. Burying categories two taps deep (open sheet → scan chip cloud) suppresses browse behavior on the primary discovery surface — especially costly pre-launch when search of a 3-item inventory usually returns nothing and category browsing is the more forgiving path. Adjacent to (but distinct from) F-150's dead-space note and F-114's in-sheet city discoverability: this is about zero on-page visibility of the category dimension itself.
- **Fix:** Add a horizontally scrollable category chip rail under the search row, shown only ≤560px (where .nk-filters-desktop is hidden): reuse the already-fetched cats array (backend titles — no new Dict copy; lead with the existing t.allCategories chip), style with existing nk-pillctl/nk-fchip tokens + an overflow-x:auto no-scrollbar wrapper, chips call setParams({cat}) and reflect the active category. Keep the Filtrai sheet for sort/city/delivery; the badge count already communicates active sheet filters.

**R2-008 · MEDIUM** — Listings feed — filter bar + offer cards (delivery concept) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The same 'delivery' concept uses two different icons on the same screen: the card media badge 'Pristatymas'/'Delivery' uses the Lucide Truck icon (cards.tsx:59), while the filter toggle 'Pristatymas galimas'/'Delivery available' directly above the grid uses the Car icon (FeedScreen.tsx:339 and the mobile sheet at :641). ListingDetail also uses Car for its delivery rows (ListingDetail.tsx:582, 632). Both icons are simultaneously visible on every feed view at every width.
- **Why it matters:** Icon-to-concept mapping should be 1:1 — Airbnb/Turo-class products bind one glyph per concept so users can scan-match the filter to the badge it controls. Here the control that filters by delivery and the badge that indicates delivery don't visually match; worse, on a marketplace whose top listings are literally cars, a Car icon on the filter reads as 'vehicle category' rather than 'delivery'.
- **Fix:** Standardize on Truck (the conventional delivery glyph, already on the badge) for every delivery affordance: change icon="Car" → "Truck" at FeedScreen.tsx:339 and :641, and name="Car"/icon="Car" → "Truck" at ListingDetail.tsx:582 and :632. Keep Car in the ICONS registry — it remains in use as the transport category glyph via category-style.ts.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-0768.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-en-1440.png`; code: `app/components/cards.tsx:59`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:339`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:641`, `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:582`

**R2-024 · MEDIUM** — Search inputs — hero and feed (http://localhost:3000/ and /skelbimai)
- **What:** Both search entry points ('Ką norite išsinuomoti?' hero field, 'Ko norite išsinuomoti?' feed field) are bare text inputs: focusing or typing produces no suggestions of any kind — no category shortcuts, no popular/example queries, no recent searches. Code check confirms no datalist/autocomplete/suggestion logic in HeroSearch.tsx, sections.tsx or FeedScreen.tsx.
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb's destination field and Booking.com's search box open a suggestion panel on focus (recent searches, popular destinations/categories) — in 2026 an unassisted marketplace search field reads a generation behind, and on a 3-listing pre-launch inventory a blind free-text search usually returns nothing, teaching visitors the marketplace is empty. Suggestion chips built from the real categories API keep every guided path to a non-empty result.
- **Fix:** Add a focus-opened suggestion panel to both search inputs, populated ONLY from real wire data already on the client: the 12 backend categories (useCategories) as tappable rows routing to /skelbimai?category=<id>, optionally followed by the 6 picker cities → /skelbimai?city=<name>. Reuse the existing popover/listbox machinery (nk-citypick panel styling, focusListboxSelection/listboxKeyNav helpers, FilterSelect option skin) and --nk-* tokens; add panel heading strings to the Dict contract and both lt.ts/en.ts. No fabricated 'popular searches' or recent-search persistence claims — categories and cities are real data. Keep the panel dismissible (Escape/outside click) and restore trigger focus on close (avoid re-introducing the F-159 pattern).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-fp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/components/HeroSearch.tsx`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:127`, `app/components/sections.tsx`

**R2-025 · MEDIUM** — Listings feed — filter row (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The filter set is Kategorija, Miestas, Pristatymas galimas toggle, plus Rūšiuoti — there is no price filter (range or min/max) at any width. Price exists only as a sort key (FeedScreen.tsx:231-232 price_asc/price_desc).
- **Why it matters:** Fat Llama, Hygglo, Airbnb and Booking.com all put a price-range control in the first filter rank — price is the primary constraint renters filter by, and its absence is the most conspicuous gap a design-literate user will spot in this filter bar. Cheap to honor client-side since every card already carries a real daily price.
- **Fix:** Add a 'Kaina' filter applied client-side over the fetched offers' priceCents (already on the wire): desktop = a FilterSelect-style chip opening a popover with 3-4 honest bands (e.g. iki 10 €, 10-30 €, 30-60 €, 60+ € už parą) or a min/max pair; mobile = a new FilterSheetGroup section in the existing Filtrai bottom sheet. Keep the truthful result count and active-filter chips in sync (extend activeChips/activeFilterCount in FeedScreen.tsx:227/243), keep it out of the URL or add a ?price= param consistent with the existing setParams model, and add label strings to the Dict contract + both lt.ts/en.ts. This also makes the existing 'Browse by category, city or price' copy (lt.ts:571/610, en.ts:511/540) truthful — today the copy promises a filter the UI doesn't have. If the backend later grows a price param, swap the client-side filter for it.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-fp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:229-236 (price only as sort options; cat/city/delivery are the only filters)`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:224-227 (anyActive/activeFilterCount to extend)`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:571,610 + app/lib/i18n/en.ts:511,540 (copy already promises price filtering)`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:146,557 (HIW step 1 + category-landing meta promise price filtering)`

**F-008 · POLISH** — Home — hero search (320px) (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** At 320px the search input placeholder truncates mid-word with an ellipsis: 'Ka norite issinuomo...' — the question is cut before its verb completes; at 360px+ it fits.
- **Why it matters:** A truncated prompt in the primary conversion control looks unfinished at the smallest common width; Booking.com/Airbnb keep mobile placeholders short enough to never clip.
- **Fix:** Shorten the single placeholder in both dictionaries so it never clips at the 320px floor — LT 'Ko ieškote?' / EN 'What do you need?' — keeping search.inputLabel as the full accessible name. This is simpler and more robust than a width-conditional second Dict key (placeholders can't be swapped by media query without JS or duplicate inputs); verify the shortened strings at 320 with recrop before closing.

**F-031 · POLISH** — Listings feed — header area (mobile) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The current-page breadcrumb chip repeats the H1 verbatim directly above it: chip "Nuomojami daiktai" over H1 "Nuomojami daiktai" (default feed), chip "Paieškos rezultatai" over H1 "Paieškos rezultatai" (search).
- **Why it matters:** Saying the page name twice within ~80px is dead weight on a phone where vertical space is the scarcest resource; Airbnb's mobile breadcrumbs omit the current page for exactly this reason.
- **Fix:** CSS-only in globals.css: `@media (max-width: 680px){ .nk-crumbs [aria-current="page"]{display:none} .nk-crumbs svg:has(+ [aria-current="page"]){display:none} }` — the :has() rule removes the now-dangling chevron that precedes the chip (chevron is the chip's immediate previous sibling per ui.tsx:307). Desktop trail and BreadcrumbList JSON-LD stay intact. If the F-029 pair-wrapping refactor lands first, target the wrapper span instead of the bare svg.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-search-vp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/components/ui.tsx:297-300`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:209-222`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:310`

**F-032 · POLISH** — Listings feed — empty search (mobile) (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai?q=zzznonexistent)
- **What:** The failed query is echoed four times in one screen: page subtitle ("Rezultatai pagal „zzznonexistent“…"), the search input value, the removable chip, and the empty-state heading ("Pagal „zzznonexistent“ nuomos pasiūlymų neradome").
- **Why it matters:** Best-in-class empty results (Airbnb, Booking.com) state the query once and spend the rest of the space on recovery paths; four echoes of a long query make the screen feel like a template dump, especially at 320px where each echo wraps.
- **Fix:** Since copy can't change per-width in JS without hydration mismatch, render the search subtitle as two spans inside the existing <p>: one with t.subtitleSearch(q) shown ≥561px, one with a new generic Dict key feed.subtitleSearchGeneric (LT 'Paieškos rezultatai visoje Lietuvoje.', EN 'Search results across Lithuania.') shown ≤560px — the same breakpoint where the .nk-fchips chip row (which already echoes the query) appears. Add the key to types.ts + both dictionaries. Mobile then carries two canonical echoes (input + empty-state heading) as claimed best practice.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-empty-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-empty-vp-lt-0320.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:199`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:244`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:283`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:577`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-039 · POLISH** — Listings feed — below-grid SEO block (/skelbimai)
- **What:** The internal-link chips under "Daiktų nuoma Lietuvoje" ("Visos kategorijos", "Vilnius", "Kaunas", …) use the identical outlined-pill styling as the functional filter chips at the top of the page, and mix one category link into a row of city links with no grouping or label.
- **Why it matters:** Same-styled pills doing different jobs (filter control vs navigation link) on one page blurs the component language; best-in-class feeds visually distinguish footer/SEO links from live filter chips.

The --link modifier hook already exists (globals.css:1037), so the CSS divergence is one rule.

**F-132 · POLISH** — Home hero — search field label (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** The hero search field stacks a question label with a question placeholder: uppercase 'KĄ?' directly above 'Ką norite išsinuomoti?' — the same interrogative twice in a row (lt.ts:55 `labelWhat: "Ką?"` + the placeholder).
- **Why it matters:** Booking.com/Airbnb use a noun-style label ('What', 'Where') with the question living in the placeholder only; 'KĄ?' with a question mark rendered in uppercase reads abrupt in LT and duplicates the placeholder's job.
- **Fix:** Same change as F-131(1): switch labelWhat to a noun ('Daiktas' / 'Item') in both dictionaries so the question lives only in the placeholder. If the team prefers keeping the interrogative style, drop the question mark ('Ką' / 'What') — but the noun form is the stronger fix and makes the pair parallel with labelWhere.

**F-146 · POLISH** — Feed page header vs sibling surfaces (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)

Applies automatically to category/city landings since they share the header block; no CSS changes needed (.nk-eyebrow exists in globals.css:213).

**F-149 · POLISH** — Feed — search results clear affordances (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai?q=Sony)
- **What:** With a single text query active, three separate clear controls are visible at once at 390px: the × inside the search input, the removable chip '“Sony” ×', and the '× Išvalyti' link on the count row — all performing effectively the same reset.
