**R2-009 · POLISH** — Listings feed — filter toolbar geometry (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** Controls sharing the toolbar rows have three different heights: the search field is ~53px tall (padding 13px 20px, FeedScreen.tsx:318) while the 'Rūšiuoti'/'Sort' pill sitting on the same row is ~44px (FilterSelect trigger, 11px padding + --nk-tap min-height), and the Kategorija/Miestas/Pristatymas pills on the row below are ~46px. Measured at full resolution: at 1440 the field is 53css vs the sort pill 42-44css; the same ~9px mismatch shows at 768.
- **Why it matters:** 2026 marketplace toolbars (Airbnb's filter bar, Booking's search rows) keep same-row controls on a single control height so the row reads as one system; a 9px delta between the field and the pill vertically centered beside it reads as an off-the-shelf mismatch on the page's primary tool.
- **Fix:** Add a shared control-height token to :root in app/globals.css (e.g. --nk-control-h: 52px) and apply it to both same-row control families: set .nk-searchfield{min-height:var(--nk-control-h);padding-block:9px} (drop the input min-height:32px at globals.css:988, or lower it so padding+input=token) and raise the pill controls to min-height:var(--nk-control-h) in FilterSelect (ui.tsx:407) and Toggle (ui.tsx:445) — replacing their minHeight:var(--nk-tap), which the larger token still satisfies. Also remove the redundant inline padding "13px 20px" at FeedScreen.tsx:318 (it duplicates the class default). Verify the categories page search field (same .nk-searchfield) still aligns, since it has no adjacent pills.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-0768.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-en-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:318`, `app/globals.css:984-988`, `app/components/ui.tsx:407`, `app/components/ui.tsx:444-447`

**R2-010 · POLISH** — Listings feed — result count placement at tablet width (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** At 768 the LT result count '3 pasiūlymai' wraps off the filter row onto its own line and lands LEFT-aligned under the Kategorija chip, while at 1024/1280/1440 it is right-aligned on the chips row. Root cause: after the three chips (~437css) the remaining space (~97css) is a few px narrower than the LT count text, so .nk-filter-meta wraps as a whole flex line; the right-alignment comes from the .nk-filter-spacer item, which stays on line 1, so the wrapped line falls back to flex-start. The shorter EN string ('3 rentals') likely still fits, making the layout locale-dependent.
- **Why it matters:** The count is toolbar metadata; marketplace-class results toolbars keep it anchored in one position across breakpoints. Here it jumps from top-right to bottom-left between 1024 and 768 with dead space remaining to its right, reading as an accidental wrap rather than a designed stack (and it wraps for LT but not EN).
- **Fix:** Add margin-left:auto to the .nk-filter-meta flex item (a one-line rule in globals.css next to the :1023 block, or inline style marginLeft:"auto" at FeedScreen.tsx:342) so that when it wraps to its own flex line it still right-aligns instead of falling back to flex-start; the .nk-filter-spacer can then be removed or kept harmlessly. The existing ≤560px override (width:100%; justify-content:space-between) is unaffected by an auto margin.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-0768.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-1024.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:335-343`, `app/globals.css:1015-1023`

**R2-011 · POLISH** — Listings feed — below-grid SEO block reading measure (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The below-grid SEO paragraph ('Daiktų nuoma Lietuvoje' block) is capped at maxWidth:900px at 16px/26px type (FeedScreen.tsx:442-444), which yields ~105-110 characters per line at 1440 — visibly overrunning readable measure in the fullPage capture. The page's own header intro two screens up is deliberately capped at 65ch (FeedScreen.tsx:309, comment cites the .nk-prose measure), so the page applies two different reading-measure conventions to comparable body copy.
- **Why it matters:** Best-practice body measure is ~65-75ch; at 16px, 900px is roughly 110ch. Long-line SEO copy reads as filler text, and the internal inconsistency (65ch header intro vs 110ch footer block) undercuts the otherwise-tokenized rhythm system.
- **Fix:** Split the constraint inside the section at FeedScreen.tsx:442: keep the 900px wrapper for the h2 + RelatedLandingLinks chip row, but cap the body <p> itself at the same 65ch measure the header intro uses (maxWidth:"65ch" inline, or introduce a shared --nk-read token in :root and use it in both places). Apply the same paragraph cap to the twin SEO block on CategoriesScreen.tsx:90 so the convention is consistent across discovery surfaces.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-fp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:441-452`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:306-309`, `app/components/CategoriesScreen.tsx:88-90`

**R2-018 · POLISH** — Home hero search — query input vs city value typography (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** Within the single hero search pill the two value lines are set in different sizes: the query input is 16px (.nk-search__input, globals.css:795-796) while the city value inherits 18px from .nk-citypick--hero .nk-citypick__trigger (globals.css:573). At 1440 'Visi miestai' renders visibly larger than the query placeholder sitting 30px to its left; at 390 the stacked rows repeat the mismatch (measured input font-size 16px vs value 18px).

- **Fix:** One shared value-slot size inside the hero pill: change .nk-citypick--hero .nk-citypick__trigger (globals.css:573) from font-size:18px to 16px so the city value matches .nk-search__input; if the larger size is the intent, instead raise .nk-search__input to 18px. Leave the panel option size (.nk-citypick__opt 17px) as is — only the two in-pill value slots must match.

**R2-019 · POLISH** — Offer card meta row — location pin glyph treatment (http://localhost:3000/skelbimai)
- **What:** The offer card's city pin is rendered FILLED (cards.tsx:86 passes fill="var(--nk-text)" + stroke, which floods Lucide MapPin's inner dot and turns it into a solid white teardrop blob), while every neighbouring surface draws the same location glyph as a stroke outline: the listing-detail header meta (ListingDetail.tsx:281), the hero city picker (HeroSearch.tsx:79), and the feed 'Miestas' filter chip. The solid blob is clearly visible next to 'Vilnius' in both card crops.

Reserve fill for the Star rating icon, which is the only intentionally solid glyph in the meta row.

**R2-020 · POLISH** — Home hero search (stacked mobile layout) — leading icon optical alignment (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** In the ≤560px stacked search card the leading icons are flex-centered against the whole label+value column, so they sit ~7px above the value line's optical center: measured at 390 the magnifier center is y=512.4 vs input center y=519.4, and the MapPin center is y=565.9 vs 'Visi miestai' center y=572.9. Both icons read as riding high, hovering beside the gap between the 11px 'KĄ?/MIESTAS' micro-label and the value text.
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb's stacked mobile search anchors field icons to the value line, not the geometric center of a label+value block; the high-floating icon is the kind of 5–7px optical slip that separates template-grade from crafted mobile forms.
- **Fix:** Inside the existing ≤560 .nk-search media block, offset the leading icons down by half the label block (11px label + 2px margin ≈ 14px → 7px): e.g. `.nk-search > span:first-child > svg, .nk-search .nk-citypick__trigger > svg:first-child{transform:translateY(7px)}` — or restructure so the icon sits inside the value row. Optionally apply the same offset to the trailing chevron (it also rides 7px high) for a single optical baseline.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-algirdasjasaitis-naudokis-web/9fb9966e-78df-4d65-8b0d-80b115027573/scratchpad/verify-crops/r3-hero-search-0390.png`; code: `app/components/HeroSearch.tsx:161-172`, `app/globals.css:1320-1328`


### Home (22)

**F-139 · HIGH** — Home (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** The entire supply-side pitch on the homepage is one 15.5px muted text line in the hero ("Turite nenaudojamų daiktų ar nuomos verslą? Skelbti daiktą ir uždirbti →"). There is no dedicated owner/host section anywhere on the page — the section flow is hero → categories → listings → renter trust cards → use-case cards → renter-framed CTA banner ("Raskite internete. Rezervuokite programėlėje.") → FAQ. The only owner entry is a small inline text-link that opens the install modal directly, skipping the site's best owner sales asset (the How-It-Works owner tab).
- **Why it matters:** For a two-sided P2P marketplace at pre-launch, supply acquisition is at least as important as demand — the feed currently has ~3 listings. Turo ("Become a host" band + nav item), Airbnb ("Airbnb your home" card + nav), and Fat Llama/Hygglo ("Rent out your stuff" section) all give the owner journey a full homepage band and a persistent nav entry. Here an owner-intent visitor gets a low-contrast one-liner and is bounced straight to an app-install modal with zero persuasion. The inline text button is also a sub-44px coarse-pointer target on mobile.
- **Fix:** Add a compact server-rendered owner band to sections-home.tsx (dictionary copy in both lt.ts/en.ts via a new Dict section, e.g. ownerBand) wired into app/[lang]/page.tsx between UseCases and CtaBanner: headline + 2-3 benefit bullets reusing existing truthful trust themes (Stripe payouts after handover, deposits, fees shown before confirming — mirroring hiw.owner copy; NO invented earnings figures per content-integrity rule) + a real nk-btn CTA. Note: the HIW owner tab is client useState only (HowItWorksScreen.tsx:25) — add a ?role=owner searchParam (or #owner hash) initializer so the CTA can deep-link to /kaip-tai-veikia?role=owner; a secondary client-leaf button can open the existing bridge.listTitle/listBody modal. Also add an owner link to footer.help (lt.ts:358-363) and consider a nav entry; give the existing HeroOwnerCta button real padding/min-height ~44px for coarse pointers.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-vp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/components/HeroSearch.tsx:21-33`, `app/components/sections-home.tsx:44`, `app/[lang]/page.tsx:42-50`, `app/components/sections.tsx:157-198`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-002 · MEDIUM** — Home — section headers (mobile) (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** On phone widths the SectionHead 'view all' action stacks BETWEEN the eyebrow and the H2: 'NARSYKITE' -> 'Visos kategorijos ->' -> 'Populiarios nuomos kategorijos', and 'ATRINKTA JUMS' -> 'Visi daiktai ->' -> 'Populiarus daiktai nuomai netoliese' (same on EN: BROWSE -> All categories -> Popular rental categories). The secondary action interrupts the eyebrow-to-title reading order on every section that has one.
- **Why it matters:** Best-in-class marketplaces (Airbnb section rows, Booking.com carousels) always render eyebrow -> title first and put 'view all' after or beside the title; an action link floating above the H2 reads as a stray element and weakens hierarchy on the flagship page.
- **Fix:** Correction: the stack breakpoint is 560px, not 700px. CSS-only fix at ≤560px: set .nk-head__top{display:contents} so its children join .nk-head's column flex, then order them — .nk-eyebrow{order:0}, .nk-head h2{order:1}, .nk-head__top > *:not(.nk-eyebrow){order:2} — yielding eyebrow → title → action with no markup change and no effect ≥561px (where the row layout keeps the action top-right). Verify the action link keeps a ≥44px touch target after reflow.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-vp-lt-0430.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/nav-scrolled-0390.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-lt-0320.png`; code: `app/components/ui.tsx:38-47`, `app/globals.css:698-702`; seen independently by 3 reviewers

**F-003 · MEDIUM** — home (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** In the bottom CTA banner the Google Play / App Store badges are pinned above the headline ("Raskite internete. Rezervuokite programėlėje." / "Find it online. Book it in the app.") at every width, including the stacked ≤1024 layout where badges render first, then heading, then supporting copy.
- **Why it matters:** Action-before-message inverts conversion hierarchy — the user meets the ask before the reason. Airbnb/Turo app banners lead with the promise and end with the store badges; on the stacked mobile/tablet layout the inversion is most jarring.
- **Fix:** Move the .nk-cta__badges div after the .nk-cta__body div in CtaBanner (sections-home.tsx:115-116). Desktop (>1024) and 901-1024 are unaffected because both blocks are absolutely positioned there; the ≤900 static stack becomes headline → copy → badges. Then swap the static paddings in the ≤1024 block (globals.css:1265-1266): body → '48px 32px 0', badges → '24px 32px 48px'. Desktop's badges-top-left corner composition can stay — the badges are visually subordinate to the display-size headline there; the stacked inversion was the real defect.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-lt-0320.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-en-0390.png`; code: `app/components/sections-home.tsx:115-116`, `app/globals.css:1263-1266`, `app/globals.css:1280-1285`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-004 · MEDIUM** — Home — features band (http://localhost:3000/)

**R2-027 · POLISH** — Home — process explainer (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** The homepage has no numbered how-it-works strip: between the offers row and the FAQ it presents a 3-card trust band ('Daugiau informacijos prieš rezervuojant' / 'Mokėjimai per Stripe' / 'Aiškios taisyklės') and use-case cards, but the browse-online → book-in-app sequence is only ever stated as prose (hero subhead, CTA banner headline) and inside a collapsed FAQ answer.

All strings through the Dict contract + both dictionaries. Keep it link-first, not another install-CTA stack (the CTA banner below already owns install).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/[lang]/page.tsx:42-48 (section order — no steps module)`, `app/components/sections-home.tsx (target file for the presentational section)`, `app/components/HowItWorksScreen.tsx (numbered-dot step pattern to reuse)`

**R3-002 · POLISH** — Home — bottom CTA banner headline (mobile, EN) (http://localhost:3000/en)
- **What:** At 390px the EN CTA-banner headline "Find it online. Book it in the app." wraps as "Find it online. / Book it in / the app." — the second sentence breaks after the preposition "in", stranding a short widowed last line "the app." The LT equivalent stacks cleanly one word per line ("Raskite / internete. / Rezervuokite / programėlėje.") so only EN shows the ragged break.
- **Why it matters:** This is the page's closing conversion moment; a prepositional line break plus widow is the kind of display-type rag Airbnb-grade marketing pages suppress (balanced wrapping is now a one-line CSS convention). Distinct from R2-001, which is the How-It-Works banner at 1440 — this is the home banner at phone widths, EN only.
- **Fix:** Dictionary-only: in en.ts:272 bind the final phrase with non-breaking spaces — "Find it online. Book it in the app." — so the balanced 3-line wrap becomes 'Find it online. / Book it / in the app.' Do NOT add text-wrap:balance (already present at these widths, globals.css:1311). LT needs no change (stacks cleanly).
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-en-0390.png`, `/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-algirdasjasaitis-naudokis-web/9fb9966e-78df-4d65-8b0d-80b115027573/scratchpad/crops/en390-band05-y10000.png`; code: `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:272`, `app/globals.css:1311`, `app/globals.css:224-228`

**R3-003 · POLISH** — Home — bottom CTA banner QR placement (desktop) (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** In the desktop CTA banner the white QR card is positioned directly on top of the phone-mockup photo's focal element: it clips the bottom-right corner of the Naudokis app icon and cuts the "Naudokis." wordmark off mid-label. Confirmed at full resolution in the 1440 capture (both locales use the same layout). The collision looks accidental rather than composed, and this QR (like the hero one, F-023) carries no caption saying what scanning it does.
- **Why it matters:** The banner exists to hand off to the app store; letting the QR obscure the very brand mark the photo is showcasing reads as an unfinished composite — Turo/Booking app-handoff modules keep the code in reserved clear space beside the device art, never over its logo. (Only the caption half overlaps F-023, which is scoped to the hero QR; the icon/wordmark collision is unreported.)
- **Fix:** At ≥1025 nudge the QR card's inline offsets in sections-home.tsx:120 (e.g. increase right from 80 toward ~40 and/or reduce bottom) or shift the phone image's objectPosition so the card lands in the dark bezel area clear of the app icon and wordmark; apply the equivalent nudge to the 901-1024 override (globals.css:1283, currently right:40/bottom:36). Verify at 1025/1280/1440 in both locales (same asset). When F-023's hero-QR caption ships, reuse the same caption string here for consistency.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-en-1440.png`, `/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-algirdasjasaitis-naudokis-web/9fb9966e-78df-4d65-8b0d-80b115027573/scratchpad/crops/f1440-cta-qr.png`; code: `app/components/sections-home.tsx:114`, `app/components/sections-home.tsx:120`, `app/globals.css:1282-1283`


### i18n & copy (22)

**F-070 · HIGH** — i18n (detail.deliverySub)
- **What:** LT deliverySub interpolates the raw nominative city into a locative slot: `dėl pristatymo ${city + " mieste"}` produces "Atsiimkite nemokamai arba susitarkite dėl pristatymo Vilnius mieste." — "Vilnius mieste" is broken Lithuanian (needs "Vilniuje" or "Vilniaus mieste"). ListingDetail.tsx:612 passes listing.city (raw backend nominative) directly.
- **Why it matters:** A blatant case-agreement error in the canonical locale on the listing-detail handover section — a core conversion surface. Airbnb/Turo-class products never ship broken grammar in their home market; this reads machine-translated and erodes trust exactly where handover logistics are being explained.
- **Fix:** In lt.ts:462-463 replace `city + " mieste"` with `cityLocativeLt(city)` → 'dėl pristatymo Vilniuje', keeping the 'savo mieste' fallback for empty city — exactly matching the established seoTitle usage at lt.ts:373. Note cityLocativeLt falls back to the raw name for cities outside LT_CITIES; acceptable today (backend city values come from the same fixed list) but worth a comment. Best shipped together with the F-069 option-aware rewrite of the same key.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/listing-howitworks-audit/listing-fp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:462-463`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:2`, `app/lib/cities.ts:28-30`, `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:612`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-178 · HIGH** — i18n (/skelbimai/{id} meta description truncation)
- **What:** listingDescription hard-cuts the listing's own description at `clean.slice(0, 200)` — no word boundary, no ellipsis. Any owner description over 200 chars produces a meta description ending mid-word ("…puikiai tinka savaitga").
- **Why it matters:** Mid-word amputated SERP snippets look broken and depress CTR. The repo already has the correct pattern — legal/format.ts truncate() cuts on a word boundary and appends "…" — so the two SEO paths are inconsistent.
- **Fix:** In listingDescription(): first strip tags — `const clean = data.description.replace(/<[^>]*>/g, " ").replace(/\s+/g, " ").trim();` — then reuse truncate() from app/lib/legal/format.ts (word-boundary + "…") at ~160 chars instead of slice(0,200). Apply the same stripped text to the Product JSON-LD `description` in page.tsx (no-fabricated-data rule is satisfied: same real text, just de-tagged). Consider hoisting truncate() out of legal/format.ts into a shared lib since it now serves two SEO paths.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/[lang]/skelbimai/[id]/page.tsx:22-25`, `app/[lang]/skelbimai/[id]/page.tsx:113`, `app/lib/legal/format.ts:16-21`, `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:542`

**F-174 · MEDIUM** — i18n (detail.seoTitle / detail.seoDescription (LT listing <title>))
- **What:** LT listing SEO templates interpolate the raw nominative listing title where Lithuanian requires genitive/accusative: seoTitle `${title} nuoma ${locative}` yields e.g. "Elektrinis paspirtukas nuoma Vilniuje — Naudokis.lt" (correct: "Elektrinio paspirtuko nuoma"), and seoDescription `Išsinuomokite ${title}…` yields "Išsinuomokite Elektrinis paspirtukas…" (išsinuomoti takes accusative). metaFallbackTitleForId has the same `${readableId} nuoma` pattern.
- **Why it matters:** Every LT listing detail page — the site's largest indexed surface — can emit an ungrammatical <title>/description in the canonical locale. Titles that are pure brand/model strings ("Bosch GSB 13") read fine, but any common-noun title is broken in SERPs, which both looks unprofessional and hurts LT query matching.
- **Fix:** Switch the LT templates to the indeclinable quoted citation form: seoTitle → `„${title}“ nuoma${locative} — Naudokis.lt`; metaFallbackTitleForId → `„${readableId}“ nuoma — Naudokis.lt`; seoDescription → lead with the quoted title (`„${title}“${categoryText} — išsinuomokite${location} per Naudokis.lt. Peržiūrėkite paros kainą…`) so no inflection of free-text titles is ever needed. LT-only change; en.ts templates are grammatical as-is.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:369`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:372-377`, `app/[lang]/skelbimai/[id]/page.tsx:65-67`, `app/[lang]/skelbimai/[id]/page.tsx:22-25`

**F-175 · MEDIUM** — i18n (cityLocativeLt fallback (lib/cities.ts))
- **What:** LT_CITY_LOCATIVES covers only the 8 picker cities; cityLocativeLt falls back to the raw nominative for anything else. But detail.seoTitle/seoDescription and the feed landing templates pass whatever city the backend listing carries (or the raw ?city= URL param, FeedScreen.tsx:195). A listing in Utena renders "… nuoma Utena — Naudokis.lt" and /skelbimai?city=Utena renders h1 "Nuomojami daiktai Utena" — broken locative.
- **Why it matters:** The locative map silently degrades to broken grammar the moment inventory appears outside the 8 filter cities — a data-driven time bomb in the canonical locale on SEO titles and visible h1s.
- **Fix:** Two-part fix: (1) validate the client-parsed city param in FeedScreen against LT_CITIES (mirroring resolveListingLanding) so an unknown ?city= falls back to "all cities" instead of rendering raw — this closes the live h1 hole; (2) make cityLocativeLt robust for backend-supplied cities on detail SEO: add a suffix-rule locative (-as→-e, -us→-uje, -ys→-yje, -ė→-ėje, -a→-oje, -iai→-iuose) with LT_CITY_LOCATIVES as the override map, and for anything unmatched emit a construction that stays grammatical with the nominative (e.g. `mieste ${city}` / omit the city rather than break).
- **Evidence:** code: `app/lib/cities.ts:17-30`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:373`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:539-571`, `app/components/FeedScreen.tsx:53`

**F-176 · MEDIUM** — i18n (detail.reviewsInApp)
- **What:** detail.reviewsInApp is the only LT count string without 3-form pluralization: `Visi ${n} atsiliepimai programėlėje`. For n=10–20 and round tens it must be "atsiliepimų" ("Visi 10 atsiliepimai" is wrong; correct "Visi 10 atsiliepimų"), and n=21/31… needs the singular form. Every sibling (reviewCount, galleryMore, resultCount, foundCount, ownerListings) implements the 1/2-9/10-20 rules correctly.
- **Why it matters:** The pluralization bug surfaces exactly on the most-reviewed (highest-trust) listings — the CTA into the app's review modal shows broken grammar precisely when social proof is strongest.
- **Fix:** Either apply the shared 3-form logic used by siblings: `const d=n%10, dd=n%100; const word = (dd>=11&&dd<=19)||d===0 ? "atsiliepimų" : d===1 ? "atsiliepimas" : "atsiliepimai";` — noting numeral agreement with "Visi" also shifts for d===1, so the cleaner option is to sidestep agreement entirely: reviewsInApp: (n) => `Visi atsiliepimai programėlėje (${n})`. EN string needs no change.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:414`, `app/components/ListingDetail.tsx:728-732`

**F-177 · MEDIUM** — i18n (detail.seoDescription (EN))
- **What:** EN seoDescription juxtaposes title and category with a bare space — `Rent ${title} ${category.toLowerCase()} in ${city}` → "Rent DJI Mavic 3 photo & video in Vilnius on Naudokis.lt." LT wraps the category in parentheses (` (${category.toLowerCase()})`), EN dropped that treatment.
- **Why it matters:** Every EN listing meta description with a category reads as word salad in SERPs and link previews — the two locales diverged on the same template, so this is a straight port bug, not a style choice.
- **Fix:** In en.ts detail.seoDescription, mirror the LT treatment: `const categoryText = category ? ` (${category.toLowerCase()})` : "";` so it reads "Rent DJI Mavic 3 (photo & video) in Vilnius on Naudokis.lt…". One-line change in en.ts only; LT is already correct.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:349`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:376`, `app/[lang]/skelbimai/[id]/page.tsx:67`

**F-005 · POLISH** — i18n (features[1].body / faq.items[1].a — "Platformos mokesčiai")
- **What:** LT marketing copy capitalizes the legal defined term mid-sentence — "Galutinė nuomos kaina, Platformos mokesčiai ir grąžinamas užstatas…", "Taikomi Platformos mokesčiai parodomi iš anksto.", "administruoja Platformos ginčo procesą" — while EN uses lowercase "platform fees" everywhere, and LT itself is inconsistent (howItWorks.faq lt.ts:243 says lowercase "taikomi mokesčiai").
- **Why it matters:** Defined-term capitalization belongs in the Terms document; on the homepage it reads as a typo to ordinary users, and the LT↔EN + LT↔LT inconsistency shows the copy wasn't normalized. Airbnb/Turo marketing copy never carries contract-style capitals.
- **Fix:** Lowercase the contract-style capitals in LT marketing dict entries: 'platformos mokesčiai' at lt.ts:116, 211, 221, 315 and 'platformos ginčo procesą' at lt.ts:247. Leave capitals only inside the legal documents (app/lib/legal/data/ JSON is source of truth there — do not touch). No EN change needed. Keep lt.ts on Prettier-default formatting per the i18n-dicts memory note.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-lt-0320.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:116`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:211`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:221`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:243`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-022 · POLISH** — Nav language picker (desktop) (http://localhost:3000/ + /en)
- **What:** The language switcher represents languages with national flags (Lithuanian tricolor for 'Kalba', Union Jack for 'Language').
- **Why it matters:** Flags denote countries, not languages — a long-standing i18n guideline (and the site's EN audience in Lithuania is not British); 2026-class products (Airbnb, Booking.com) use a globe icon + language names in their own language.
- **Fix:** Register Globe in the ICONS registry (named-import Globe from lucide-react, add Globe: lucide(Globe) in app/components/visual.tsx per the documented pattern), then replace <Flag code={locale} /> in the trigger (sections.tsx:424) with <Icon name="Globe" size={16} stroke={2} /> and drop the Flag glyphs from the options (endonyms 'Lietuvių'/'English' already render there). Delete the now-unused Flag component. Keep dropdown mechanics and dict.nav.languageNames unchanged.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-vp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-vp-en-1440.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/focus-home-t6-1440.png`; code: `app/components/sections.tsx:287-358`, `app/components/sections.tsx:424-425`, `app/components/sections.tsx:484`, `app/components/visual.tsx`; seen independently by 3 reviewers

**F-055 · POLISH** — i18n (EN terminology: rentals/items/listings + reserve/book)
- **What:** EN mixes three nouns for the same object — "We couldn’t load rentals" (offers.errorTitle) vs "We couldn’t load this listing" (detail.loadErrorTitle); goneBody "Browse other rentals instead" vs its own CTA backToListings "Items to rent"; feed counts "N rentals" under the h1 "Items to rent" — and two verbs for the same action: cta.title "Book it in the app" / meta.description "book in the Naudokis app" vs detail.reserve "Reserve in the app" / HIW "Ready to reserve?".
- **Why it matters:** LT is disciplined ("rezervuoti" throughout); EN reads like multiple authors. Marketplace-class products (Airbnb, Turo) lock one verb for the conversion action and one noun per concept so users learn the vocabulary.
- **Fix:** en.ts-only editing pass with a three-line style-guide comment at the top of the file: 'item' = the physical thing, 'listing' = the ad/page, one count noun for results (pick 'listings' or 'rentals' and use it in resultCount/resultCountAtLeast/loadMore, offers.errorTitle/emptyTitle and feed.empty.* alike), and one conversion verb — 'reserve' (already used by detail.reserve, interruptTitle and HIW): change cta.title to 'Reserve it in the app' and meta.description 'book in the Naudokis app' → 'reserve in the Naudokis app', and align goneBody with backToListings ('Browse other listings' + 'Items to rent' CTA reads fine once nouns are consistent). No Dict shape change; LT untouched.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/gap-audit/land-cat-foto-en-0390.png`, `screenshots/gap-audit/land-cat-foto-en-1440.png`; code: `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:8`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:65`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:108`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:272`; seen independently by 2 reviewers

**F-131 · POLISH** — i18n (search.labelWhat / search.labelWhere / feed.searchPlaceholder)
- **What:** Two sibling inconsistencies in the search UI copy: (1) the paired micro-labels mix forms — labelWhat is a question ("Ką?" / "What?") while labelWhere is a noun ("Miestas" / "City"); (2) LT uses two different placeholders for the same search action — hero "Ką norite išsinuomoti?" (lt.ts:52, also howItWorks.screen) vs feed "Ko norite išsinuomoti?" (lt.ts:593). Both LT forms are individually grammatical but inconsistent; EN uses one string in both places.
- **Why it matters:** Same control, two voices — a design-literate user notices the field labels don't parallel and the site can't decide between "Ką" and "Ko".
- **Fix:** Two one-line dictionary edits, both locales: (1) make the label pair parallel nouns — labelWhat: 'Daiktas' / 'Item' alongside labelWhere: 'Miestas' / 'City' (Booking/Airbnb noun-label pattern; also resolves F-132's double-question stack); (2) unify the LT placeholder to one form across search.placeholder, feed.searchPlaceholder and howItWorks.screen.searchPlaceholder — recommend 'Ką norite išsinuomoti?' (already used in 2 of 3 slots). Both forms are grammatical, so either is fine as long as one is chosen. No markup changes needed.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/discovery-audit/feed-vp-lt-1440.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-vp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-vp-lt-1440.png`; code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:52-57`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:256`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:593`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:33-38`; seen independently by 4 reviewers

**F-179 · POLISH** — i18n (detail.galleryImageError)

**F-180 · POLISH** — i18n (<title> brand-suffix separators)
- **What:** Two brand-suffix conventions coexist: hub/feed/category titles use " | Naudokis.lt" (meta.title, metaTitleFallback, landingTitle, categoriesPage/feed/howItWorks metaTitle) while listing detail and legal pages use " — Naudokis.lt" (detail.metaFallbackTitle, seoTitle, metaFallbackTitleForId, legal page template).
- **Why it matters:** Inconsistent SERP branding across the same site; best-practice sites pick one separator so titles read as a coherent family in search results and browser tabs.
- **Fix:** Standardize on " | Naudokis.lt" (majority form): update detail.metaFallbackTitle, detail.metaFallbackTitleForId and detail.seoTitle in both lt.ts and en.ts, the three legal page.tsx templates, and the stale contract comments at types.ts:99/194 so the convention is documented once.

**F-181 · POLISH** — i18n (detail.escrowNote / detail.hostVerifiedNote trailing punctuation)
- **What:** Full-sentence trust notes lack terminal periods — escrowNote "Mokėjimus ir grąžinimus administruoja Naudokis per Stripe pagal taisykles" / "Naudokis administers payments and refunds through Stripe under the applicable terms" and hostVerifiedNote — while the sibling note in the same booking panel (appOnlyNote) ends with a period in both locales.
- **Why it matters:** Adjacent microcopy in one panel alternating between punctuated and unpunctuated sentences is a classic polish tell.
- **Fix:** Add terminal periods to escrowNote and hostVerifiedNote in both dictionaries (4 one-char edits) — matching appOnlyNote/serviceFeeHint, i.e. one rule: full-sentence panel notes are punctuated, short labels are not.

**F-182 · POLISH** — i18n (dead Dict keys (detail.owner*, dateFrom/dateTo, pricePerDayLine, contact))

**F-183 · POLISH** — i18n (types.ts stale contract comments)
- **What:** Contract comments no longer match the shipped values: types.ts:252 `serviceFeeFree: string; // "Nemokama"` but both locales now say "Rodoma programėlėje" / "Shown in the app"; types.ts:251 calls serviceFeeHint a "tooltip explaining the free service fee" (the fee is no longer claimed free); types.ts:214 documents deliveryRadius as "Pristatymas iki N km" but lt.ts:408 renders "Iki N km".
- **Why it matters:** The Dict contract is the translators' spec — stale annotations invite regressions back to the abandoned "free service fee" claim, which was an honesty fix.

Especially 251-252 — the abandoned "free service fee" claim was an honesty fix and the spec comment invites regression.

**F-184 · POLISH** — i18n (howItWorks.screen.listPrice)
- **What:** The HIW phone-mock price reads "50 € / d." while every real price surface uses "/ para" (common.perDay, detail.perDay, detail.perDayShort lt.ts:415/438/484). EN is internally consistent ("€50 / day" vs "per day").

Optionally align en.ts listPrice to the card-visible unit too, but the LT change is the one that matters — verify with the app team only if the mobile app genuinely renders "/ d.", in which case align the sitewide unit instead (one convention).

**F-185 · POLISH** — i18n (legal meta descriptions from manifest blurbs)
- **What:** Terms/Privacy meta descriptions are legal recitals with defined-term quote clutter: "These Naudokis Terms of Use (\"Terms\") govern your access to and use of the Naudokis Platform." and "…MB Naudokis (\"Naudokis\", \"we\", \"us\", \"our\") collects, uses, stores, discloses…". The account-deletion blurb shows the better pattern ("How to delete your Naudokis account…, what is deleted, and what is retained").
- **Why it matters:** SERP snippets full of parenthetical defined terms read as boilerplate and waste the ~160 chars; a user-benefit summary earns more clicks (compare how Airbnb summarises its terms pages).
- **Fix:** Author plain-language, user-benefit blurbs for terms-of-use and privacy-policy in app/lib/legal/data/manifest.json (both lt and en, <=160 chars), modeled on the account-deletion blurb pattern: what the doc covers and why it matters to the reader (e.g. EN terms: "The rules for renting and listing items on Naudokis: bookings, payments, deposits, cancellations and disputes."). Keep the recital sentences inside the documents themselves. Edit the JSON directly — it is the source of truth (the md->JSON converter is stale; do not run yarn legal:json).
- **Evidence:** code: `app/lib/legal/data/manifest.json:7`, `app/lib/legal/data/manifest.json:15`, `app/lib/legal/manifest.ts:37-44`, `app/lib/legal/types.ts:9-14`

**F-186 · POLISH** — i18n (meta.title (EN home))
- **What:** EN home title is 65 chars: "Item rental in Lithuania from people and businesses | Naudokis.lt" — over the ~60-char/580px SERP budget, so the brand suffix (and possibly "businesses") truncates. LT is 56 chars and safe.
- **Why it matters:** The brand is the part most worth keeping visible in SERPs for an unknown marketplace; every other title in the dictionaries fits the budget.
- **Fix:** Shorten meta.title in app/lib/i18n/en.ts to <=60 chars: "Item rental in Lithuania | Naudokis.lt" (39 chars) — the people-and-businesses qualifier already lives in meta.description ("from private or business owners in Lithuania") and in hero.badge, so no information is lost. Alternative if the qualifier must stay in the title: "Item rental from people and businesses | Naudokis.lt" (52 chars). LT title is fine as-is.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:6`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:25`

**F-187 · POLISH** — i18n (useCases.goToSlide)
- **What:** Carousel-dot aria-label "Rodyti ${i+1} pavyzdį" produces "Rodyti 2 pavyzdį" — a cardinal numeral with singular accusative ("show 2 example"); the intended ordinal needs "2-ą" ("Rodyti 2-ą pavyzdį") or a reordering ("Pavyzdys 2").
- **Why it matters:** Screen-reader-only, but it's the same numeral-agreement rigor the rest of the LT dictionary gets right.
- **Fix:** In app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:297 change to `goToSlide: (i) => `Rodyti ${i + 1}-ą pavyzdį`` (standard digit-ordinal abbreviation, correct for 1-ą/2-ą/3-ą), or the case-free reordering `(i) => `${i + 1} pavyzdys``. EN ("Show example 2") is already fine.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:297`, `app/components/sections.tsx:740`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:269`

**F-188 · POLISH** — i18n (LT wording nits: faq payments answer, business-owner answer, HIW meta title)
- **What:** Three LT wording rough spots: (1) "išmokoms taikomos Naudojimosi sąlygose nurodytos sąlygos" repeats sąlygos twice in five words (lt.ts:315 and 243); (2) "o vartotojams taikomos privalomos teisės" (lt.ts:331) is an awkward calque of "mandatory consumer rights apply" — natural LT would be "taikoma privaloma vartotojų teisių apsauga"; (3) howItWorks meta title "Kaip veikia daiktų nuoma ir skelbimas" (lt.ts:126) — "skelbimas" reads as "an ad" rather than "listing an item" (EN says "rental and listing"); "…nuoma ir daikto paskelbimas" would disambiguate.
- **Why it matters:** Each is understandable but below the polish level of the surrounding LT copy; FAQ answers are trust-critical reading.
- **Fix:** Three one-line LT edits, keeping the Dict contract untouched: (1) at lt.ts:243 and lt.ts:315 replace the payout clause with "išmokoms taikoma Naudojimosi sąlygose nurodyta tvarka"; (2) at lt.ts:331 replace "o vartotojams taikomos privalomos teisės" with "o vartotojams taikoma privaloma vartotojų teisių apsauga"; (3) at lt.ts:126 retitle to "Kaip veikia daiktų nuoma ir paskelbimas | Naudokis.lt" (48 chars, within SERP budget).
- **Evidence:** code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:243`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:315`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:331`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:126`

**F-189 · POLISH** — i18n (feed.landingTitle / landingHeading no-param branch)
- **What:** The final branches of the landing templates are unguarded against both params missing: LT emits a double space ("Nuomojami daiktai  | Naudokis.lt" — `Nuomojami daiktai ${locative} | …` with empty locative) and EN emits literal "undefined" ("Items to rent in undefined | Naudokis.lt" — `${city}` unchecked). Currently unreachable because every caller gates on `isLanding`/`params.city` (skelbimai/page.tsx:51, FeedScreen.tsx:194), but nothing in the dictionary enforces that.
- **Why it matters:** A future caller that passes `{}` (the type allows it — both parts are optional) ships "in undefined" to production metadata. Defensive copy functions are cheap.
- **Fix:** Make the last branch of landingTitle/landingHeading/landingDescription self-sufficient, mirroring landingSeoHeading: LT — `if (city) return \`Nuomojami daiktai ${locative} | Naudokis.lt\`; return "Nuomojami daiktai | Naudokis.lt";` (heading/description analogous, falling back to "visoje Lietuvoje" phrasing); EN — `if (city) return \`Items to rent in ${city} | Naudokis.lt\`; return "Items to rent in Lithuania | Naudokis.lt";` and an "across Lithuania" fallback in landingDescription. No caller changes needed.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:543`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:549`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:486`, `app/lib/i18n/en.ts:491`

**F-190 · POLISH** — i18n (LT "video" vs "vaizdo" terminology)
- **What:** LT mixes "vaizdo" and "video" for the same category: homepage FAQ says "foto ir vaizdo techniką" (lt.ts:319) while the SEO label is "Foto ir video technikos" (lt.ts:12) and the footer/backend label is "Fotografija ir video" (lt.ts:347, matches backend name_lt).
- **Why it matters:** Inconsistent product vocabulary in the canonical locale; VLKK also flags "video" as non-standard, so the FAQ's "vaizdo" is the careful form while the taxonomy uses the colloquial one — pick one deliberately.
- **Fix:** One-word edit for consistency now: at app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:319 change "foto ir vaizdo techniką" to "foto ir video techniką" so the FAQ matches every visible category label (footer, tiles, SEO labels, backend name_lt). Separately, raise a deliberate terminology decision with the backend team — if they rename name_lt to the VLKK-preferred "vaizdo", update lt.ts:12 and lt.ts:347 in the same pass. Do not leave the two forms mixed.
- **Evidence:** code: `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:319`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:12`, `app/lib/i18n/lt.ts:347`


### SEO & metadata (1)

**R2-023 · MEDIUM** — Sitewide <head> metadata — native app-install banners (http://localhost:3000/ (all pages))
- **What:** No apple-itunes-app meta (iOS Safari Smart App Banner) and no Open Graph appLinks metadata anywhere — grep across app/ finds zero 'itunes'/'appLinks' references, and app/[lang]/layout.tsx generateMetadata emits neither. The App Store id needed for it already exists in the repo (app/lib/contact.ts:14, id6753683957).
- **Why it matters:** Airbnb, Booking.com and Turo mobile-web all ship the OS-native install banner: on iOS Safari it renders Apple's own trusted 'GET — Open in App Store' strip above the page for free, with no custom UI. For a bridge site whose only KPI is app installs, forgoing the platform-native install surface on the highest-intent segment (mobile Safari visitors) leaves the standard conversion channel unused. This is complementary to F-007 (custom install CTA in scrolled mobile chrome) — the smart banner is the zero-code OS affordance, not site chrome.
- **Fix:** In app/[lang]/layout.tsx generateMetadata add `itunes: { appId: "6753683957" }` (exact Next 16 shape: ItunesApp = { appId, appArgument? }); extract the bare id as a constant next to APP_STORE_URL in app/lib/contact.ts so the store URL and banner id share one source. Optionally set appArgument to the page URL for app-side deep-link context. The appLinks OG field is available in the same Metadata type but is a legacy Facebook mechanism — treat it as optional, not the core fix. No copy/design changes; the banner renders only in iOS Safari and is Apple-native chrome.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-vp-lt-0390.png`; code: `app/[lang]/layout.tsx:30-56`, `app/lib/contact.ts:14`, `node_modules/next/dist/lib/metadata/types/extra-types.d.ts:41-44`


### Cross-cutting / benchmark (1)

**F-012 · POLISH** — Capture infrastructure — fullPage mobile shots (http://localhost:3000/)
- **What:** All three mobile fullPage captures are solid black below exactly y=16384 device px (Chromium max-texture-size limit): home-fp-lt-0320 loses the last ~1120 CSS px (footer Browse list bottom, Help & policies, copyright), home-fp-lt-0390 ~390 CSS px, home-fp-en-0390 only ~64 CSS px. Verified programmatically — every capture's black run starts at row 16384. NOT a product defect; the LT mobile footer bottom is effectively unaudited in this batch.
- **Why it matters:** Future audit passes will misread the black band as broken footer rendering, and anything below 16384 device px is invisible to reviewers.
- **Fix:** In the capture scripts (scripts/home-audit-shots.mjs and the other *-shots.mjs that use fullPage), when scrollHeight × deviceScaleFactor > 16384 either drop to deviceScaleFactor:1 for that page or stitch segment captures (scroll + clip) instead of fullPage; then re-shoot the LT mobile home fullPage set so the footer bottom is auditable. Also note in artifact-pitfalls that the dead band is a uniform rgb(18,18,18) fill (not pure black) starting at exactly device row 16384 — Chromium's max-texture clamp.
- **Evidence:** screenshots: `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-lt-0320.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-lt-0390.png`, `screenshots/home-audit/home-fp-en-0390.png`; code: `scripts/home-audit-shots.mjs`, `scripts/gap-audit-shots.mjs`, `scripts/discovery-audit-shots.mjs`

## Appendix — what is verifiably good (205 notes from independent reviewers)

- Locale-aware price and copy quality: LT '50 € / para' vs EN '€50 per day', fully translated categories, badges and FAQ — EN is a first-class equivalent, not an afterthought (home-fp-en-0390 slices vs home-fp-lt-0390).
- Offer cards are at the 2026 marketplace bar: delivery trust chip on the photo, honest 'Naujas skelbimas'/'New' state instead of fabricated ratings, 48x48px glass save button (code-verified .nk-fav), clear price+period row and city — consistent across all three live listings (home-fp-lt-0390, home-fp-en-0390).
- Hero search card is excellent on mobile: high-contrast white panel on the dark hero, labeled fields (KA?/MIESTAS with icons), full-width primary 'Ieskoti' button, and an owner-side entry point ('Skelbti daikta ir uzdirbti') right in the hero (home-vp-lt-0390).
- Category tiles: distinct per-category color identities with consistent icon circles in a comfortable 2-up mobile grid, no overflow at any width 320-430 (nav-scrolled-0390, home-fp-lt-0320).
- Use-case carousel dots are real 44px-target buttons (18px padding, background-clip content-box, aria-labels) despite their small 8px visual — accessible pagination done right (code-verified ui.tsx Dots + globals.css .nk-dot--btn).
- FAQ accordion: first item open by default with a clear purple open-state border, large full-row tap targets, readable answer contrast, single-open behavior working in the interaction capture (faq-open-0390).
- Hero search pill (1440): high-contrast white field with integrated city picker and a solid purple Ieškoti/Search button — clear, marketplace-grade primary control (home-vp-lt-1440.png, home-vp-en-1440.png).
- FAQ accordion open state at 1280: purple active outline, flipped chevron, generous padding and a readable answer measure — clean and unambiguous (gap-audit/faq-open-1280.png).
- Offer cards handle the zero-review launch state honestly: New badge, delivery badge, location and per-day price with no fabricated ratings (home-fp-en-1440.png, home-fp-lt-1440.png).
- Category tile grid (4x2) with per-category accent gradients, icon disks and consistent arrow affordances is distinctive and coherent at 1440 (gap-audit/nav-scrolled-1440.png, home-fp-lt-1440.png).
- EN copy quality is native-level and structurally equivalent to LT across hero, eyebrow, subhead and FAQ — not an afterthought translation (home-vp-en-1440.png, home-fp-en-1440.png).
- Owner-side conversion path is present right in the hero ('Turite nenaudojamu daiktu ar nuomos versla? Skelbti daikta ir uzdirbti →' / 'List an item and earn'), addressing both marketplace sides early (gap-audit/nav-scrolled-1440.png, home-fp-en-1440.png).
